O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	O you, three dear sons, I have completed this book which is the last of medical science entirely, and have made the end by its explanations and by its declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in vision that I complete it for you with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, that is to say "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is fortified in our region and is strange throughout all, so is its science perished and cut off, and nothing remains of it except for the small descriptions in books of the ancients that the hands have moved.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this has come the error and the vanity, and are closed the understandings and is alienated the science.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	Or it seems to me that I will vivify it together with the ordering of this treatise according to the way of exposition and declaration and of abbreviation; and I will come together the forms of the implements of cautery, and of the other instruments of the work with the adjustment of the declaration and of preparation of them, as much as it is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And for the reason of those that no good masters of hands are found in our time, the art of medicine is extended.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary that he who undertakes it mounts in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, until he knows the judgment of members, and the forms and connections and separations of veins, and has knowledge of bones and nerves and flesh and the number of veins, and the movement and of moving and resting veins, and the place of their exit.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And for this reason Hippocrates says that the name with the body is much, and with the work little; and similarly in the art of the hand.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We say to you in the introduction of this book that he who is not acquainted with the things said before, if he guards himself so that he does not fall into error and that he does not injure men; thus I have often seen more than those who engage in this science and abandon themselves to their ignorance and without experiment.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa .i. apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I see a fool who mixes  i.e., an abscess of scrofula or a woman's neck, and mixes the arteries of the neck; for that reason so much blood came out that the woman fell dead in his hands.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens .iij. jors.	And I see one other fool who treats a stone of a man with water, and the stone was large; so he took away with it a piece of the bladder, and within three days the man died.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I have already been called to treat it, and saw the disposition of the patient and the size of the stone, and well if one cut it he would die.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui prist en cure .i. duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi .i. termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And I saw another mire who took care of one duke of our land who had a broken leg, and with the fracture he had a wound; and the mire, full of ignorance, strained the fracture onto the wound as stars by strong ligature, and did not leave any room for drainage to the wound, and left it thus; and he commanded him that he should not untie it at all; and remained so that the leg was all swollen and the foot came to perdition.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to come to him, and I hastened to come to untie the leg; and when I untied it so it was in peace and he felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But every way the corruption was already confirmed in the limb, and he could not heal it; and did not cease the corruption to go through the limb as long as the limb was all lost.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And see .i. another sore that opened .i. abscess and then inflamed by the evil of its lord.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	Because a sore, when it is pure of melancholic humor, it is not fitting that one touch it with iron unless in such a place where one can entirely remove what is corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en .ij. divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And for this, dear son, it is necessary that you know the work of hands is divided into .ij. divisions: namely, work where there is peril in many dispositions; and I will show in each place of this book where there is fear and peril.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	For this reason it is necessary that you keep yourselves safe, so that the foolish people cannot speak ill of you. Take up your arms in caution and undertake your patients lightly and firmly, and use the best way so that by the grace of God you come to salvation and be praised; and leave the terrible diseases of grievous health; and remove your arms from those who make you doubt, and have faith in yourselves so that you may come from this world to the other of glory. 
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Galians says in some of his admonitions: "Do not take care of a bad illness unless you want to be called a foolish healer." 
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have devised this treatise according to three chapters. 
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapter is of fire cauteries and medicine cauteries, and the chapter is ordered from the head to the feet; and the forms of the instruments, and the workings of the cautery, and of everything that is necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter is of cutting and probing, and of cupping and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar things; and the chapter is ordered and the forms of the instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is of restoring dislocations and twists, and similar things; and it is ordered from the head to the feet, and the forms of the instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Thus as we remember from the work, it is necessary for me to say the quality of the aid and of the nuisance of each complexion.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the qualities of aid and of nuisance are the longest discourse and most subtle science and secret replies; and of this speak most of the sages, and agree with it; and I suffice myself little their words, because I fear the length.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que .ij. complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that cauterization helps universally to every complexion where it has matter, except for two complexions: namely, hot complexion without matter, and dry complexion without matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In hot and dry complexion together with matter, some advised against it and said that cauterization is great help there; and the others said the opposite: that cauterization is not good for illnesses that come from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is so hot, and should not be cured from hot disease by heat, nor by dryness; and he who says the contrary that cauterization does great help to hot and dry disease that comes in the body of men.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of man and his moisture to the complexion of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree to this word.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it never by experiment.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And every way, let no one intervene except he who has experienced it and who knows by long usage the chapter of cauteries, and the diversity of complexions of men, and their dispositions and causes of their illnesses, and the occurrences and the space of time; of other complexions we have no more fear, even in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the mirrors assembled and agreed on the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, sons, that a cautery assembled fire is of greater secrecy of cures, and of greater goodness than cautery of burning medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For the fire is simple, and does not come out except to the member that is burned, and harms no other member at all.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	The hot medicines come from member to another in separating, and bring to the member diseases of harsh healing; and by chance kills the patient The fire because of his height and for the goodness of his substance does not do this, if there is not superfluity. 
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And this I have found by experiment and through the length of service and study that I have put into the art, and it is upon the truth of things; and for this reason I excuse myself from the length of the speech, because it does not please me that I lose the secret which is deposited in fire, and the quality of the work, how it expels the diseases of the body, as the philosopher says when demonstrating; now receive it into your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they must agree on what time the cauteries should be made, and when they are ready.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that cautery is advisable at all times, because the nuisances arising are reduced by the help of cautery; and also if the cauteries are for necessary pains before and until they cannot wait for the time when greater evil comes to the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And never think, dear son, like the fools do; because the disease that is healed by cautery has no return; and they say so; but it is not as they think, because cauteries are only medicine that changes the complexion, and dries up the humors that are the cause of the pain, and is worth more than medicine for the haste of its power, and for the virtue of its work and its authority.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And a most certain thing is that the disease comes at times according to the complexion of the patient and the place of the disease and its virtue; and they are gathered together in him the superfluities by the acquisition of meats and similar things, if it is not cauteries administered where there are few superfluities and moisture, such as cauteries of iron for pain, and similar things, and such pain does not return; but this happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand for what reason cautery is called the last of medicine, and this is true; but they do not believe that cautery is worth after medicine, but their intentions are false, and it is cautery the last of medicine because when we administer ways of cures in any illness and they do not work, then we administer the cautery, and it works.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Therefore, it is clear that cautery is the last of medicine, not according to the intentions of foolish people.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that cautery of gold instrument is more effective than iron, and they said this because of the quality of gold and the high value of its substance; and they said that the tool of cautery does not cause decay, but this is not true because I have experienced it, and I have found that it is true in some people; and gold cautery is more effective than iron, as they claimed.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And however when you heat an instrument of gold, you do not know whether it is heated by the color of the gold, and it is soon cooled; and if it is heated too much; so they do at the fire; and thus there is enough impediment.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this we use our cautery of fire that we have made appeared in our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Or I have ordered this chapter of the head to the feet, for that the way may be easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	of the olivewood cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cautery is good for moisture and cold on the brain, and there are two kinds of it made because of a disease called “soda”, and because of many humors that descend from the head to the eyes, and to the ears, and for a multitude of dreams and tooth pain and throat pain, and even for all diseases that come from cold such as paralysis and soda and apoplexy and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief .iij. nuis ou .iiij., selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is that the patient be purged by a medicine that loosens and liquefies the head, three or four times, according to what the virtues and the temperament and the habit of the patient can bear; and then raise the head of the patient.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses .ij. eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then make him sit crossed between your hands, and place his hands upon your thighs; afterwards put the root of your palm upon the root of his nose between his two eyes; and where your two thumbs meet, if it bleeds a little, then cauterize with the cautery called “olivare”, because of which this is the form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os .i. sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren .i. poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse .iij. jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place it on the place marked with ink, and do in descending and restraining your hand poke and poke while turning it; then lift your hand gently, and look at the place if you see the bone i.e. small; and if you do not see it, so begin the cautery until you see the bone as I told you; after take .i. poke of silk, and put in soft cotton inside, and put on the place, and leave it for .iij. days; after put a compress moistened in butter; and leave on it until the scalding is gone; after cure the wound with the ointment which is called "tetrafarmaçon", until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And it is said by the ancients, that when the wound stays open longer, it purges more; and for this reason they help to move it.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And they say that one must let the cautery burn so that part of the bone is burned, and then reseal what is burned of the bone, and be cured.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme .i. vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And they say the other that one must leave the cautery thus longer, and to press so forcefully that one lowers the bone as wide as a ring that women put in their spindles for those that the humors come out mixed; and one must leave the wound long uncovered; after that one must cleanse and dress.
Et ces .ij. manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two ways of cauteries do not seem to me to be good at all, except in some men where there is a way of fear; and I think that I should leave them; because the bone is weakened by the continuous solutions of nature, as we testify in other members; and even when the bone of the patient is weak by nature, and the first semblance of cautery is more cured and mixed for me, and of this I use thus in assembly salvation.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	of the old pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When throughout the head comes chronic pain, and it lasts long, the patient must use herbs and pills that are called "cochie", and of purging of head and oils and plasters; and if one does to him the cautery that we have said before, and it is not worth.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take ward if the shoulder of the sick person is of strong nature, and that it be not too cold; therefore cauterize below that cautery a little which we have said above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai .i. cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est .i. leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After make cautery on each horn of the head up to the bone, as we have said before, and make one cautery where it is called "vasselz"; and there are one of them in which one puts ventouses; and align your hand so that you do not see until the bone: the sick person feels much more great pain in this cautery than in the others, and I will speak of it later; and it is necessary that the cauteries of the horns be more subtle than those with which one cauterizes the middle of the head, and this is the form:
dou cautere dou chief	of the cautery of the head
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc .ij. manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When in one part of the head comes sudden pain, and it is spread to the patient up to the eye, and the shoulder is purified by medicines calming, and one has made the other cures that I have said in the division of diseases, and all this does not profit: then I make cauteries according to .ij. manners, that is to say of medicine sharp and of fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope .i. poc as .ij. chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi .xij. houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi .ij. jors ou .iij.; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The cautery of sharp medicine is that you take a piece of alum, and remove the rind and cut it 1 pock as 2 shoulders, and then make a temple where the pain holds in such a manner that you can place the piece of alum under the skin; and when it will be placed so lie and bind it well and leave it so for 12 hours; and then untie it and treat fiercely the piece of alum, and leave the wound so for 2 days or 3; then put on cotton dipped in butter as much as possible.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the cure of ointment until it is healed; and if you see so do these of some burning medicines that I have written or dose treat burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The iron cautery is as follows in this manner. 
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cautery in this shape: 
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait .i. poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And it is called "closed" because the head is made in the shape of a clo or it has .i. inch of curvature, and in the middle a small appearance; and put it on the painful place, and hold your hand and stir the fire slightly, until half the thickness of the heart be burned; and lift your hand that the artery does not burn, which is outside, and flows abundance of blood.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par .iij. jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	After put cotton in awe of seil, and put on the place for .iij. days; then you put cotton moistened in butter, and then cure the place with ointment until it is healed; and if you want to cauterize this migraine with the cautery which is called "cultellare", at all the point, and guard yourself from covering the artery in this migraine which is not old.
de emigraine	of migraine
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you treat migraine as we have said before in the divisions of illnesses, and it does not benefit, and see that the cauteries before said of medicine and of iron do not suit it, then it is necessary that you heat the cautery which is called "cultellare" until it is white; and rule thus on the painful place a line of half a finger's length, and withdraw your hand once, and restrain that you do not cut the artery and that you do not come close to the bone; and guard yourself from the jaw that it moves when one thrusts, and that the nerve does not feel more than the movement and that spasm does not come to the patient, and guard yourself from blood loss of the artery when it will be cut, or cutting has great fear and even more so to him who does not know it, and who is not studied and experienced; and leave the work in mid-way; but I will tell you how one restrains blood when the artery is cut, and I will show you at the place where it appears in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait .ij. coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you see that this cautery does not suit the illness, and the patient is suffering, cauterize the middle of the head as we have said, and cure the wound until it is healed; and if you see, administer the cautery that we have said or chapter of the extraction of the artery, with the cautery which has .ij. points; and this cautery is better than that one and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	of the pain of the ears from cold
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When in the ear comes pain from cold, and one has opened medicines solutives and other cures that we have said in the division, and the pains do not change, then use this cautery which is called "poins," for this is its form:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les .ij. se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait .x. poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After prick all around the ear of the sick one, or around the two if the pain is in both, and you are distanced a bit above the root of the ear after that you have marked the place to be cauterized; and have ten poins around each ear; after cure the place until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	of the torture of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	Torment that must be cured by cautery are not other than those that move from phlegm, as we have said in the division of diseases; and do not make cautery to resemblances that come from dryness and sprain of nerves.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de .iij. cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des .ij. levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you cure this semblance of torment that moves from phlegm of ears and expulsions of the head and gargles, and this is not enough, then it behooves you to cauterize the patient with three cauteries: one at the root of the ear, and the other a pock of fire on the temple, and the third in the adjustment of the two lips; and put the cautery in the part that opens healthy, and make cautery on the head of the ear above a pock below the horn of the head, and another on the temple as long as a pock; and leave the cautery so long until the half of the heart is burnt; and this is the form of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And it is the semblance of the curette that we have put before, but it is a pock finer and it behooves the knife to be a pock larger; after curing its place as I have said before, until it is healthy.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai .iiij. cauteres: .ij. sus les .ij. cornes dou chief, et .i. emmi le chief, et .i. ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexy is old and you treat it as we have said, and it does not benefit, and the patient does not have a fever, then I make .iiij. cauteries: .ij. on the .ij. horns of the head, and .i. in the middle of the head, and .i. where it is called "vasselz" as we have said before, and the last cautery on the mouth of the stomach; and be cured as we have said before.
de litargie	of lethargy
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	For this illness it is fitting to give the patient large doses and pills that sharpen the brain; after which, rub the head of the patient all over, and put on the occiput the emplastery of mustard as is written in the treatise on plasters; and this is the manner of the cautery: if you make it as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai .iij. cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere .i. doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai .i. cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, .ij. autres sus les .ij. cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If it is healthy in this way, good is; and if it is not, make to it .iii. cauteries of the midst between the chief down to the neck, and have of space between each cautery .i. two of gross; and cure it like the others, and if you see it joined, and the sick one suffers, make .i. cautery in the middle; and if necessity is, .ii. others upon the .ii. horns, and cure it until it is healthy; and be the cauteries which are called «olivare», as I have said before.
de la froidor dou chief	of the cold of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et .i. derrier et .iij. sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai .iiij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	It behooves that the head be purified with herbs and those we have said before; after this, reheat the head of the sick one, then make cautery in the midst of the head and on each horn, and .i. behind and .iii. on the spine of the neck; and if you have more need, and the body is moist and the sick one suffers, and the illness is far away, make .iiij. cauteries on the spine of the back; and leave it until the most tender of the heart be burnt, and lift your hand; after this cure it until it is healthy, and be the cauteries which are called «olivare» as we have said before.
de l’epilempsie	of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	The epileptic people should not use fire cautery except for those who are phlegmatic, and it is necessary first to modify the brain with herbs and other treatments that we have said in the section when the patient is great and suffers from penre medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai .i. cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et .i. cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if it is a child who cannot suffer it, then make gargles and mastications that modify the brain often with boiled meats; after the king makes a hole in his head in the middle, and he makes 1 cautery according to what we have said before, and 1 cautery on the vessel, and on each horn; and if the patient is bad and suffering, then make cauteries as I have said to the one who has paralysis and softening of the body, on the spine of the back and neck, and let the cauteries be olive oil according to the manner that I have said.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai .i. cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is a child, make 1 subtle cautery according to this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When by the cause of melancholy are the superfluities or the moisture corrupted and phlegm thick, then you cauterize with such cauteries as we have said to him who has paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if by the cause of melancholy are the superfluities declining to melancholy, and the body of the sick is moist, then give him something to drink by which the brain may be purified, according to what is before in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai .i. torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com .i. cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After you have anointed the head of the patient; afterward make one cake of linen well done, and also one circle, so put it within the head; and the sick person should sit crossed, and be held well on all sides; afterwards present the ointment, and mix some butter of ancient goat with it; and heat it gently over a fire, so that the patient may suffer it being applied; afterwards empty the circle by within the head, and let it cool; and do this to the patient each week once with another good governance, until he be healthy.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	Or if you see someone being cauterized, doing more pricks with the whole cautery. 
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	This manner of cautery soothes the brain greatly; and then puts on cotton moistened in butter and grease of galingale.  
de l’awe des eulz	of the weeping of the eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When weeping comes first to the eyes by the signs that I have said in the division, then begin and give the patient things purifying the head, and warding off all moisture, and make him sweat or bathe more often fasting.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as .ij. eulz ensamble, ou en .i. se li dessendemens est en .i.; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	After that command him to raise his head, and make him cauterize the center of the head, and make two cauteries on the two temples if the weeping descends from the eyes both together, or one if it descends in one; and cut with all the cautery all the veins and arteries that are below the heart, and let the cautery be long according to the width of the temple; and ward off the dripping of blood, and if you see too much blood flowing out, then staunch it as much as you have.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les .ij. os derrier.	And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and in the incision the caution how you will stop it; and sometimes one does cauterization or a hatereil below the two bones behind.
dou cors des larmes	Of the course of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: .i. cautere emmi le chief, et .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples, et .ij. cauteres ou haiterel desoz les .ij. os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout .i. petit cautere.	When the tears of the eyes are old and accustomed and are on the veins, or near the arteries that are in the appearance of the head outside; and one sees that it is superfluities cold phlegmatic, then I make the cauterization that I said at the beginning of the eye downwards: one cautery in the center, two cauteries on the two temples, and two cauteries or hatereil below the two bones; and if there is need more, one cauterizes cleverly above the eyebrow to all a small cautery.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	Of the course of tears from within the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide .iij. nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai .ij. cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les .ij. sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	When you treat him according to what we have said in the division, and it does not benefit, then give the patient three cups of wine; after the king the chief, and make the cautery or olive-cautery middle; and make two cauteries of the cautery called "clavilis" on the two sores, one slightly below the cheekbones; and beware of the artery so that you do not cover it.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the cautery called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the paper of the eye is softened by illness and moisture, then the cauterization of this cautery which is called "olivare". 
de coi ci est li forme:	of this is the form: 
Et se tu vues si fai .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you see so make two cauteries on the two eyebrows as long as the eyebrows are; and do not leave the hand except until one-third of the paper is burned, according to the manner that I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	hairs that prick the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	It sometimes happens that the hairs of the eyes are converted to the padding, and prick the eye, and one makes cauteries according to two manners: that is to say of fire, or of burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they are born and are even, then place the patient on your sound; after rule over the paper of the eyes a figure that is as like the leaf of myrtle, and be its beginning beside the hairs; then put cotton moistened in egg white and musk of pearlescent above the oil, then heat the cautery of this which is the form:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi .iij. jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After cauterize upon the figure that you have signed point and point many times, that the hairs be burned at the place; and the signs of the healthiness of the work is that you see the paper retreated, and the hairs raised to the height of the eye; then raise your hand, and leave thus for three days, then put cotton moistened in butter until the burning is removed; after the cure of ointment until it be healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if after these the hairs come, and the paper is softened then begin again the cautery upon that same place, as you have done first; and if the hairs are stiff, cauterize until the paper is raised to its natural place, and be even, and do not prick the hair the eye.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en .i. oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en .i., et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse .i. poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The cauteries of burning medicine are that you command the patient to let the hairs grow long and even, then make of parchment the form of the leaf of myrtle; then take of French soap and live coals, of each one .3., and grind together well; and do it hastily, so that it does not cool, then spread on the form that you have made like the leaf of myrtle, and put under the eyes; and if the patient holds in .1. eye only, then must one work in .1., and if in both as well; and put under the eye cotton moistened in wine of egg; and let the head of the patient be in your healthy hand and place your thumb on top of the medicine, and press .1. point and the loaf every time that the patient feels the burning sensation of the medicine, for it burns as much as fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this long, then remove the medicine with your thumb.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	And when the medication has passed, lift the place of awe, and look if you see the paper lifted as if it were lifted by the constraint of fire or by incision; and if it is so, then it is well. 
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If this is not the case, put back on the medicine on the place where the medicine did not work, until your workings are even, and your eyes are set; then put on cotton soaked in butter until the burned skin is healed, after cure the place of the ointment that is called "dyaphens" and another, until it is healed. 
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if it is necessary that you guard well your work with great care that it does not fall from the medicine into the eyes.  
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And if the paper becomes soft afterwards, and the hair pricks in the eye, then begin the medicine on that place which is softened by the paper properly, as you have done before; after curing it until it is healed; and this is the form of the myrtle leaf. 
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And know that the eyes of men are diverse in size and smallness, and according to these be your constraints; and let not the right way be returned to him whose is the study of this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	Of the cure of fistula by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have said in the divisions of diseases, and your treatments do not benefit, then it is necessary that you make cauterization according to this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to put his head on your healthy side; and hold the head between your hands in such a manner that it does not move, nor lean its head; after putting moistened cotton in vinegar or in persillion juice on the eye; after heat the cautery which is like: and it is pointed to the head as like the form of a vulture's feather, altogether that it be the cautery; if you see, so it be pointed from one end to the other, and if you see, so it be like a tent; but nonetheless, this which is pointed is good for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After press the fistula when it is open, and remove the rotteness, and dry it; and if it is closed, so operate, and remove the matter from within; after put on the hot cautery form, and hold your hand to the cautery at the part under the eye, so that your hands do not make folly; and put the cautery in the fat of the eye, and corrupt.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the beginning of the cautery up to the bone, it would be well. 
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If this does not happen, repeat the cautery once more, and another if you have need for it, and leave it for three days; after which put on cotton moistened in butter, and cure with drying ointment until it is healed, and if forty days pass and it is not healed, then put on medicine corrosive aqua until the bone is uncovered; and the king according to what he would come into his chapter. 
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a way of cauterizing a fistula that none of the ancients said. 
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	Attend to a fistula, and make an incision; after putting into the opening a subtle cautery of which here is the form:  
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	and they make it to the quantity of one third of an ounce; and hold your hand on the cake firmly, and let the patient not move at all, that the melted lead does not run to his eye; and it is necessary to put on the patient's eye cotton moistened in butter or in honey: the lead will close the fistula's opening, and the healing by miraculous health.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed by the cautery that we have said, it is good. 
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If this is not so, then it is necessary to administer perfuse to the nose and bring the fistula back to the body of the nose according to how it should be in its proper place.  
des crevaices en levres	cracks in lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times there occur cracks in the lips that are called "poils," and even on the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe .i. petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you cure these cracks with what we have said in divisions, and the cure does not benefit, then  cauterize i. small surgical knife cautery according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And he places it gently in those crevices until it comes to the top; after caring for the place with cerote until it is healthy.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies .i. cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou .ij., aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess comes in the root of the throat or in the uvula, or palate, or at the roots of the teeth, after it has putrefied and rotted and is enveiled and becomes a fistula; and you cure it as we have said in divisions, and it does not benefit; therefore it behooves you to have i. cautery according to the quantity of the fistula; after the boil or perforation of the fistula, and hold your hand until the iron glows at the top of it, and the last place; and do this once or ii., after the cure of what we have said in cures, until it is healthy; and if it is cured thus, it is good; and if those are not, it behoves to discover the place and remove the rotten bone, according to what you will find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	of the movement of the teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat them with medicines and it does not work, then put the head of the sick person in your hand; after heat the cautery whose form will come here later in such a manner that you put a chain on the tooth; and put inside the cautery hot carefully, and hold so long that the sick person feels the heat coming to the root of the tooth; after raise your hand and restart the cautery according to your will; after fill the mouth of the sick person with salt water, and let it remain an hour and rinse forcefully.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in such a manner the tooth which was moving is confirmed, and the gum softened restrained, and the moisture corrupting dried.
de la dolor des dens	Of the pain of teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc .ij. manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When tooth pain comes from cold, or there is cold or wind, and the medicines do not help, then there is need for cautery in .ii. ways: cautery of butter and cautery of fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus .i. fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Cautery of butter is such that you take butter from a dish, and the end in a spoon of iron or tin; afterward take cotton and envelop it on the point of a tent, and moisten it in boiling butter, and put it on the aching tooth gently and hold until it is cooled; and thus do often as long as its virtue comes to the root of the tooth, and if you see that the cotton and wool are soaked in cold butter, and put it on the aching tooth, and put on one hot iron until the fire comes to the tip of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	The cauteries assembled fire is such that you prick a cane of iron or steel, and be thick so that the fire does not come to the mouth of the sick person; after heat the cautery, from which its shape will come afterward, and put it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery cools; do this often, for the pain will be removed that day or tomorrow.  
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it is necessary that the patient fills his mouth with good butter in the urgency of this cautery, and then the root be driven; and this is the form of the cautery: 
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And make cautery where you will, and according to what you are able; and this is the form of the caine:
des scrophules	of scrofulas
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the scrofulas are of phlegm and cold moisture, and are not obedient to digestion by medicines, then cauterize with the heated iron as is described after comes the form, and it has openings for the fumes to issue to the cautery on the other side; and put the hot cautery on the abscess once, where it is necessary, until it comes to the bottom of the abscess; and if the abscess is small put cautery according to the quantity of the abscess, and leave it so III days; and put on moist cotton in butter as long as the burn is removed; after cure the place of ointment and tents until it is healed. 
Li forme de la cainne:	The form of the chain: 
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When the moistures prevail on the channels of the throat, and even when it comes from cold complexion, then it is necessary that the patient be first emptied by resolutive medicines; after that you make cautery at the root of the throat, and keep that you do not come near to the throat, and burn only as much as a point. 
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the fire cautery to the joint of the neck at the head of the spine, and be the cautery which is called "clavicle" because we have its form before; and cure the place as we have said before until it is healthy. 
de la toust	of the pain
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et .i. autre cautere emmi le pis entre .ij. mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When all and malady of poison are from cold moisture, and the patient has no fever or dryness, and the illness is ancient, if he makes two cauteries on the forceps in their places; and one other cautery between the two breasts; and let the cauteries be which are called 'clavile' according to the form that is said before.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	And if you see, make cautery in pricking at all the cautery that is called 'points' because its form is as before in the disease of ears; and let the points be up to XXX, or wherever it reaches. 
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	After curing the place according to what is said before, and let the cautery be at III rains according to this form: 
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais .iij. a cop.	And for those are the cauteries lighter, because you make them three in one piece.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a .ij. ners douqueil ci est li forme:	After it is supported the patient on his back and on his ribs; after lift up the heart that is inside the tittle with the two fingers of your left hand; and if the joint is dislocated inside, so cauterize it which has .ij. ners  for this is the form:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble .iiij. cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a .iij. ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a .iij. ners:	and cauterize the heart until it pierces up to the ribs, and would come the figure of the cautery together four cauteries; and for this reason is made cautery with the cautery which has three ners, so that the figure of cauterization are six cauteries; and are the nerves according to the subtlety of a tent and this is the form of the cautery which has three ners:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce .i. nerf por coi il i a .viij. cauteres.	And sometimes is adjusted upon this, i.e., nerve for which there are eight cauteries.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	After place the cautery forceps ground with sail; after make rest the patient, and let not move his limbs by long time until it be well fortified.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated upwards, which rarely happens, then make a cautery on the thick part of the clavicle, or many cauteries in prickling. 
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joint is set, and the moisture is removed, and the patient is cured.  
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When in the stomach come colds and much moisture until it is altered in complexion, and are multiplied the catarrh to him, and in manners of cures accustomed and he does not profit at all, then it is necessary that the patient be treated on his back, and extend his legs and hands. 
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	Of this afterward I make III cauteries 1 under the collarbone of the hip by the quantity of one penny, to all the shoulder blade cautery, and II cauteries of fire on the two ribs until the shape of the cauteries is in III angles, and have such space between each other that they are not joined together when they will rot; and let the cauteries be so deep that they penetrate the two parts of the heart, and let the figure of the cauteries be according to this form without adjustment:  
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if you see to cauterize with a large cautery in the stomach according to this form; and he who will have fear of this cautery, cauterize by pricking and seigne on the stomach at point according to the quantity that you see of it; then cauterize the whole cautery which is called 'poins'. 
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the care of the treatment that we have had before, as long as it is healed. 
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	When to the liver comes pain from cold and moisture and great flatulence, as long as it is been taken out of its natural complexion by superfluities; and the patient is cured of those that we have said in divisions, and he does not benefit from them, it is necessary that the patient be soothed on his mattress; and sign III cauteries according to this form and this figure and this quantity on the liver, outside the hypochondria, where the ribs of man come; and there be space between each cautery the size of a finger; and let the cauteries be long in the body, and do not press your hand too much on the whole cautery; and it be burned only half of the heart, and let the patient be straight on his feet; and if he cannot, let him lie down, and extend his legs, and raise his arms; and this is the form: 
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	And if you desire it, thus cauterize these cauteries with the curette, if you are subtle and wise in the art, and take heed that you do not burn all of the heart, for you would cause the whole body to dry out; and that it does not come to boiling, because the hearts are very subtle there, and you know it well.  
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	When he has an abscess on the liver, and you want to know if it is in the flesh of the liver or in the capsule: if it is in the flesh, the patient feels pain not too strong; and if it is in the capsule, he feels piercing pain. 
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	And when this cure departs from the sights, it befits that the patient be bathed on his head; and then reign over the place where the abscess is, and then warm the cautery which is similar to the beam, for this is the form: 
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	And cauterize with the cautery as long as the hairs are burned, and come up to the shaft, so that the skin is entirely healed; after the cure according to the cure of wounds until it is healed; and it is not proper for anyone other than those who have studied medicine for a long time, and by whose hands these diseases have been cured many times, to use this cautery. 
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Therefore he can boldly operate, and altogether it seems to me better to leave it. 
dou cautere de pleuresin	of cautery of pleuresin
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize .i. cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et .ij. petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et .ij. cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et .i. cautere emmi le pis, et .i. autre sus l’estomac, et .i. entre .ij. espaules, et .ij. as .ij. costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre .ij. espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancient say that one must make on the pleuresin cauteres of roots of aristologe, and in such manner: take a root of aristologe long, the most great that thou canst find, and be dry, and as thick and as long like thy fingers; and the moisten in oil, and the press to the fire, and cauterize one cautery between the collarbone and the neck, and two little cauteres a point going down in the part which is below the beard; and two cauteres between the fifth rib and the sixth, declining behind a point; and one cautery amidst the breast, and one above the stomach, and one between the two shoulders, and two as the two ribs of the breast behind the cautery which is between the two shoulders; and press not thy hand, but do openly as if smelling.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	And they said that no one old man used cautery of fire seeming to the razor, and it is heated and put between the ribs, until it comes to this abscess; and soon goes out the pain, as we have said in the abscess of the liver.
