Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this work there is fear or the patient dies now, or a fistula comes which cannot be healed. 
de la mice	of the mouse
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent .iij. manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you cure the disease of the mice with what we have said in the divisions of cures, and it does not benefit, then there are three ways of cautery which are all good.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	Of which some manner is that thou makest III cauteries, or IIII, in lining according to the length of the mouse, according to the figure of the cautery of the liver that we have said before; and do not hasten thy hand to the whole cautery, and let the patient be laid on his back; and another manner of cautery is that thou heateth the cautery which has II nerves, as we have shown it in the dislocation of the shoulder; and raise the heart which is above the mouse, or the cuts of the patient come from the left, and let the elevation by which thou liftest the heart be according to the heart, according to the length of the body, and the cauteries be according to the width of the body. 
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	After it puts the two nerves inflamed as much as the kernels are pierced from the other side, and then pulls out the cautery, and thus there will be four. And if you see, so cauterize with all the cautery at three nerves. 
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the cure when it has gotten rot for a long time, and this is worth more than the other cures before said. 
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Cauterization is not good for dropsy, except for the manner called "asclytes".  
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	When you cure it according to the manners that we have said in divisions, and your cure does not help, then it is necessary that you make IIII cauteries around the throat, and one on the stomach, and one on the liver, and one on the mouse, and II behind the back on the spine, and one place the breast; and let the cauteries be near the edge of the heart. 
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les .ij. ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	After leave the cautery open to fight for long time putrefaction, and do not leave at all the cure of the sick after the cautery; and healing would hasten, and will be together the two intentions with the help of God.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The form of the cautery for the belly is the key that we have before shown; and that for the back is olive-shaped, according to what it is placed above.
de l’enfleure des piez	of the swelling of the feet
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	When the feet are swollen in those who are hydrophic, and are full of a bright yellow fluid, it behooves you to cauterize on the back of the foot between the little finger and the ring finger; and lift your hand with the cautery without turning.  
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not enter too deeply by force, so tightly closes outside the yellow awn, and let the cautery be according to this form: 
Aprés fai sus .ij. jambes .ij. cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	After do on .ij. legs .ij. cauteries in each leg at the point of the knife-blade; and let the cautery be long, one below the knee in front and the other outside, in the middle of the leg; and leave the cauteries open lengthwise without curing, that they may stay in place; after the cure of the other cures that we have said.
de la menoison	of the house
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai .i. grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et .iiij. cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout .i. cautere clavile subtil, et .ij. cauteres sus les hainches.	When solution of the belly comes from cold and moisture, so that the retentive and digestive virtues which is in the stomach and in the intestine are weakened, and cannot be cured by ways of cures; and you see the patient suffering well and of great virtue, then do one large cautery on the stomach according to what we have spoken of before about the cautery of the stomach, at the circulating cautery; and four cauteries around the navel small to every one cautery clavicle small, and two cauteries on the kidneys.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et .i. cautere sus chaicun yle, et .ij. petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see the moistors abundant and the patient suffering, do cautery on the groin, and one cautery on each hip, and two small cauteries on the stomach near the large, because the cure is beneficial when there is good help.
de la cure des emorroydes	Of the treatment of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	When the hemorrhoids are or at the foundation, or one or more, and they are old and are of large cold and moist humors corrupted, and are cured as we have said in divisions, and it does not benefit, if you do cauteries: III above the spine of the back, which is all outside under the almecade poc and poc in triangulating, and I cautery below the hood II should; and if you think that his stomach is cooled, and the meat does not cook, and one sees the face swell, then to the face one does I great cautery on the stomach, as it has been said before, and the other on the liver, and the other on the mice at all the cauteries clavile; and leave the cautery open long. 
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the cure the place until it is healed. 
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the flesh which is named “thelul”
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou .ij., et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you cut the “thelul,” if the cautery seems like a razor, then put it all ablaze on that “thelul” and cut; and let it stay there until the cautery comes to the base of the vein, so that the blood does not come out; do this once or twice, and if there is much flesh, cauterize each one as we have said; after the cure of openings beneficial as long as they are healed; and if you cauterize with a large cautery on the “alchatim,” it will have more help.
de plaie mal curee	of a poorly cured wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot bear cutting or opening, which we will recount in its place, there comes such a sickness that it can only be cured by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When to any comes fistula, and it is filled and gives putrefaction and corrupt moisture, then the doctor should provide at once a subtle tent, and keep that you know at once the tent how much it has of length. 
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	After heating the cautery which resembles a razor, and putting it into the fistula according to the quantity that the patient has entered there, and re-heat the cautery as long as the corrupted flesh is burned, once or II or III, according to the quantity of need; and take care not to burn the nerves that are nearby, and the large veins.  
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	If the fistula goes to the body of the bladder and intestine, then guard these parts, and do not make those fuers than in flesh, and think that it is not pierced; after cure the place as long as it is sound, and if the places are saielez, and the matters are removed for a long time, then know that the place is completely sound; and if the matters are not removed, know that the place is bad, and corrupting the bone at its root; and thus like one of these that we shall say in its place. 
de la maladie des reins	of the disease of the kidneys
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When pain from cold comes to the kidneys, and of great windiness, and does not take any semen [from a woman], then it is necessary that you make cautery on the kidneys on one side and the other with the cautery chisel which we have said before; and if we cauterize them in the middle, there will be three cauteries in a line, and they will do more help.
de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is soft and weak from cold and moisture, so that the patient retains urine, then make a cautery on the part outside above the bladder, where the hairs of the groin begin, one on the right and one on the left, and let each cautery be as long as two finger widths; and make one cautery outside the back, or two if you need it; and let the cauteries be pointed according to the shape mentioned above.
de la marris	of the kidneys
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the kidneys are cold and moist, and do not allow conception because of this, and the flowers are corrupted and their ends are slow; and when they arrive, there is great pain: therefore it is necessary that one make three cauteries around the waist, as we have said about the cautery of the bladder, and two cauteries outside the back; and let the cauteries be pointed, as we have said.
de la hainche	of the hip
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the viscous moistures descend to the hip joint, and for this reason it moves from its place, and the sign is that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and it is found the location of the viscus department, then you should cauterize the patient on the hip joint at one cautery resembling a circle, and mark in front of the location around the hip as it turns, so that the hip is inside the circle; and if it is the cautery such as the one with which the stomach was cauterized.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if this cautery is not present to you, then make three cauteries of the olive oil large, and let the cautery be as perfect as all the others; and cure until it is healed.
de la dolor de la hainche	of the pain of the hip
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes in the hip joint, and it is from cold and moisture, and the patient is treated with what we have said in the division and the cure does not work, and the illness is old: therefore you must purge the patient of gross humors with fetid pills, or other good-seeming pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	After the fire cautery; and the manner of the cautery is according to II manners: that is to say together medicines ardent, and cautery of fire. 
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	Fire cautery is made in many ways, one of which is as follows: that you cauterize on the side of the hip III triangular cauteries according to this form, and make it good depth and width, and have between each cautery a space the size of a finger, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped. Sometimes one makes cautery in the middle on top of the hip, for which there are IIII according to this form: 
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you see fit, you cauterize with the circular cautery that we have mentioned before in the dislocation of the hip; but make it in such a manner that the circle contains the whole hip, and all the spaces of the core be burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And this is how it is done for sciatica when the pain holds in the hip and does not reach as far as the thigh nor the leg. 
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if it comes to the thigh and leg, make two cauteries there where the patient says that the pain holds him, and one cautery above the ankle four fingers, on the left side a little; and be the cautery cuticular, or be the cautery of the thickness of the heart; and if the patient feels that the pain extends to two fingers of the foot or near it, cauterize there where he feels the pain three fingers or four with the cautery which is called "finger." 
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if this trade is necessary, if one does more; and if he knows that the pain is below the knee towards the thigh, then he makes cautery with the cutellar or circular cautery, and be careful in all your cauteries that you do not leave the cautery there so long that you burn the nerves and the large arteries, and that you do not make more nuisance and contraction to the patient.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I myself have seen many who had cautery on the ankle of the foot, and left them until the leg was completely swollen, and the foot also, and it was pierced and corrupted all the foot. 
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After a solution of belly from which he had death. 
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pain is in two parts together, make cautery in one and the other, according to this manner.  
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And the sage said in the cautery of the hip, from this is the manner, make such iron and be at the head also as much as a thimble of finger, or a little less, and be by entrechetres and be from one entrechetres to the other of space the quantity of a knuckle of fist; and be the entrechetres toward II parts, and be also like nuts, and there is the hip of iron well made; and this is the form: 
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be heated until it is all red and feels hot, and then put it on the bone of the diseased hip, and let it be turned on the healthy side; and cauterize once 1 cautery reont and let it for 3 days; and then make a plaster of butter, and leave the wound open long time; after the cure of ointment until it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we should use little of this cautery because of the fear of its regret, and we rarely see who uses it; and nonetheless these are good cauteries, which can bear it, and where it is needed.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	The cauteries of medicine burning are that you make the instrument at intervals in which descend the edge of the door, and be of iron or steel a length, and in the height have it two, and have between each the quantity of the thickness of a finger; and be open above and below, and join together according to this form: 
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	After put the bolster of the hip on the patient lying on his healthy side, and after your hand very above the bolster of the hip; after place between the two circles of the hot awl which be heated at the fire one part, and let him for an hour of time, and suffer the patient the heat and the burn of it. 
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	For there is found medication also with fire; and when the medication has passed, raise your hand with the instrument and raise the buttock gently, and leave thus for III days, and put on butter until that which is black from the scalding is removed; and let it be for III days that rot draws out of it; and this would be the last aid after the cure of dressings until it is healed. 
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument; et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	And if the pain has extended to the thigh or leg, then you make the instrument that holds it according to what you have done in the hip augmentation; and this is the manner of the hot awl, and I have written it or treated of the rectification of medicine. 
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take alkali and quicklime, as much of each as possible, and grind them together, and put them in a new pot.  
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	where there is a small opening of fire where the point of a razor can enter; and puts one pot over the other well sealed, and puts on top alkali and charcoal and sweet water, until there is a good amount above the powders as you will take it well grasped in your hand; and leave it so until the sweetness descends like water and stool or whatever is sealed, then take all that sweetness, and throw it on charcoal and alkali as before. 
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	And then if it will be very hot and is administered in many works of medicine and cauteries of other members because it does the work like fire, and there are other medicines with which one cauterizes well the hip just as the testicle and honey anacardi and chalz with soap, all these things mixed together. 
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Galens tells us of a cure by which a man was cured of the pain in the hip and sciatica, and it helped him greatly, and said that they did no other cure for him, and he was healed at one time when this cure was done to him, and he bathed as he teaches here afterwards.  
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	And say in this manner that you take the litharge green fresh and dry, and grind it much with a point of grease, and put it on the hip and thigh and leg where the pain holds, and apply it; and leave it for three hours and by the quantity that the patient feels no more burn.  
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then make it enter into the bath until the body of it be a little aroused, and make it enter into bed, and the pain will go away altogether and will be healed. 
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And knows that no one should use a cautery of such medicines unless after the evacuation of the body.  
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And Dioscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with iron filings, it helps a lot; and it must be done in this manner of cautery.  
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take a cloth and soak it with old oil, and put it on the hollow which is between the thumb of the foot and the other one called the foscile. 
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	After taking wool from a dry goat, and embroiling it in fire until it is charcoal, put it on the wool, and let it rest until it is extinguished; and do this again, and never cease doing so until you feel by sense that it comes to the hip, and that the pain is ceased; and this manner of cautery is called "cautery of goat." 
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain of the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether by fall or percussion or by too great evacuation, or by similar appearance of cold matter spread, none of these appearances are suitable for cautery, except for that which comes from the infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary, after what the patient is purged of fetid pills or other similar things, that one makes on his back, where the pain holds, three lines marked with charcoal, and in each line 5 cauteries or more according to the virtue and quantity that the patient can bear; and let the cautery be made according to the cautery which is called "point"; and if you see fit, make 3 or 4 cauteries on the middle clavicle cautery according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	Many times this disease comes to small children, and the signs of its beginning are that they have a tight abdomen when they lie down, and fear; and you find in the lower spine of the back and on us the appearance that comes upon the other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you view it being cured, cauterize it with this cautery according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	So that the cautery pricks each part of the spine equally.  
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see it so, cauterize around the spine with the burning cautery two lines or three, and let the points be near each other. 
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After curing the place as long as it is healed according to what we have said, and guard that you do not administer cautery in a glibness which is in a spam of nerve.  
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain of the joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When the pain of joints comes from moisture that is spread to each limb of the body, and when the pain comes in the feet, which the wise call "gout" properly, and when it is from a cold cause and cures with medicines cannot cure it, then it is cured by cauteries in this manner: make the mouth of cauteries around the joint of the foot, and let the cautery be olive-shaped according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if there is need that you seize upon the face of the foot, then apply the cautery to the whole cautery as one claims "point". 
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if the pains come as far as the knees and other joints, and this happens many times, then to each knee make III cauteries or IIII of each part, with all olive oil cautery; and if you have need of more, make more, but do not hold your hand away from there than when the center of the fire is burnt. 
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend to the knee and back, administer the cautery that we have said in our chapter. 
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are in the hands, so make poins around the foscile II lines; and if there remains no pain in the two, so make poins on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come up to the elbows or shoulders, so cauterize each part, and make good government to the patient and think medicines. 
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you give him good governance and cleanse his phlegm, he will recover with God's help. 
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the hip
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When a rupture comes in the groin, and the testicles descend to the hips and it is new, if you see him cure it, that he does not move that day; and that he uses things which hold the belly, so that the bowels descend from his belly; after that make him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to hold his armpit as long as the testicles are repaired, and pull them to your heels, and then set a cautery of this shape:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	until it is white and it feels soft 
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then reset the bones to their place; and the minister holds his hand on them so that they do not return backward; and work well the thighs of the patient, and put under him a cushion and the sergeant on the thighs, and the other on the hip which holds his hands; then place the cautery on the sign with your whole hand, and hold it straight and until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, begin again once more until you come to the bone; and be careful that the bone does not protrude when you make the cautery; that you do not burn it; and that by this the patient does not die, or other harm. 
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that when you do not come just to the bone with the cautery, your work is worth nothing. 
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And it is necessary that the cautery of children be subtle according to the measure of them, and of large people also large according to their measure; after III days cure their place of the cautery of butter as much as the scalding is removed; after the cure of other ointments until it is healed, and lie the patient XL days on his back until the wound is well soldered; and it is necessary that his nurses be tired for a long time, so that the boil do not emerge when he will want to go into rooms. 
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after forty days, when he wants to get up, one administers a good splint to him, and wear it for another forty days; and have good rest, that he works little and wards off too much repletion of drink and eating, and of too much braiding; and if he does this teaching so is healthy entirely. 
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I shall say here afterwards the cure of tailoring in its chapter. 
de la routure dou ventre	of the rupture of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When ruptures come in other bellies and are known, and you see that they do not grow anymore, then make the fire cautery according to its quantity, and be it at the third of the heart; after the cure according to what we have said; and none of the ancients have said one must cauterize with the cautery at III angles according to this form. 
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	But first sign the place of incision and make a line across the breadth above the rupture, and another below, and keep your hand steady on all the cautery clavicle. 
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauteries are lighter and milder. 
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of ancient pain in any limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes in any limb, either from a fall or a blow, and this pain lasts for a long time, and the cure of medicine is not effective, then it is necessary that it be cauterized with the cautery called "point," and let the cautery be according to the length of the limb and its smallness and its weakness and its virtue and its location of twists and its pain. 
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If he is healed by the first cautery, it is good; if not, recommence the other cautery on that one, for such custom is that he must heal in the member that is closest to him, for which it is necessary that you make the cauteries as long as the patient is healed.  
de meselerie	of melting
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The boils are helped sometimes by cautery with great help, and even the malady that comes from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy. 
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	When you see the patient being cauterized, take heed if the patient is at the beginning, and if it is cured according to what we have said in the division, and do not remove or delay, and you doubt that the corruption does not spread throughout the sick person, then make V cauteries on his head: I am putting the head to nine, and the other towards the front to the end of the hair; and II on the II horns, and I behind on the top of the head; and let it remain so long as the cauteries come to the bone, and as long as the peels issue forth so that the vapors of the thick humors can escape from them; and cauterize on the mice according to what is in front.  
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the melting is spread everywhere; and it clearly progresses, then it is necessary that you cauterize it with these cauteries that we have said on the head, and .i. cautery in the middle of the neck, and .ij. cauteries on the spine of the neck, and .vj. cauteries on the spine of the back, and .i. large one on the hip and .i. other on the side, and .ij. on the .ij. shoulders; and .ij. on the arms, and .ij. on the tendons of the leg, and .i. on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and beware of the nerves that are on the heel bone, so that you do not burn them; and sometimes it is done cauterize on the bone of the thumb, and .i. other on the bone of the stomach, and .i. other on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And know that when more cautery is made, the more it does help, and moves it profits; and know that the patient feels no pain from the cautery as healthy people feel it, for that reason because the body is already totally corrupted. 
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is necessary that the cauteries be large and small according to the limbs and joints, according to what you will find in the ways of iron. 
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After curing the place with a mixture of flour of almonds with honey and other treatments until it is healed. 
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When inflammation comes in any limb and is cured by medicines and oils and plasters, and it is not healed, then I make cauteries on the limb according to the size and smallness of the limb; and let the cautery be a point entering into the thickness of the skin; then cure with ointments until it is healed. 
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And at times one makes cautery by hand and by foot and on the back, at the exit of the nerve that numbs the limb, and thus is removed the swelling; and nonetheless let no one intervene unless he is knowledgeable about the members and the exits of the nerves moving the body.  
de albaras	of  bars
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease that is called "albaras" is serious and the means of medicine avail nothing, then cauterize it with a cautery a small hole according to the quantity of the species of the heart, until the blanching is removed, and its color has changed; then cure it with flour of rice and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and blood of colon and blood of alondre, each one part; and mix all together, and bind it with a cloth, and leave it at the place as long as it is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The cure of syphilis by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When an ulcer comes at the beginning, and you see it arrested, then cauterize it with a cautery which seems like a circle, all around the edge of the ulcer. 
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And nonetheless the wise men say that one should make a cautery also in the middle of the sore; and nonetheless this does not seem good to me, because I fear that it will be ulcerated and corrupted, and I have never wanted it to happen any time; and a more right thing is that it be cauterized around, with the cautery which is called "circule", as we have said in much of cauteries. 
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling that cannot be cured
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When someone has a disease called "adubelati", and it is slow to die, or because of the superfluity that it makes, or because of the blood of the patient when he is decrepit (that is to say too old) and he has little blood, or because of the weather; and you see it hasten to die: then cauterize it around with many small cauteries by pricking; after leave it thus. 
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For she will hasten to die. 
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it becoming worse with all the cauterizing, then heat the cautery from this shape:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And place your hand in the midst of this malady which is called «adubelati» until the cautery has pierced the heart, and let the cautery be such that the patient feels it burning in such a manner that the course of the rot is raised. 
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After the cure until it is perfectly healed.  
li cure dou feu par fer	The cure of fire by iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	One other manner of sickness there is which is called "corroding", and it is nothing else than a corruption of limb, for it devours the limbs as though fire eats dry lines. 
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this illness in a place that can suffer fire cautery, then sharpen the cauteries small and large, according to what is necessary for the place where the illness is; after cauterize all parts until you reach all corruption, and nothing remains of it, so that everything that is corrupted is removed. 
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then let it be for three days, and put on the cauterized places softened crushed with oil until the scabs of fire are removed, and all the corruption. 
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the cure of blemishes generates flesh. 
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if you see after three days that the healthy flesh does not grow, it is good; and if those do not, re-begin the cautery on those which are remained corrupt. 
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this malady has sometimes been cured with the application of a hot cautery in place of fire; but nonetheless, the cautery is more helpful, and I have already said the treatment of the application of a hot cautery in the section: take it when you need it. 
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	From the roots that come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Many times it happens that by fire a disease is born in the feet called «closed», according to our understanding, and it is a very bad thing that discolors the foot.  
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cautery for this illness is according to two manners. 
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	This is to know cautery of fire, and cautery of hot water. 
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Fire cautery is that you heat the iron like a feather of vulture, and be made of good iron to the measure that it can bend the nail from all parts, and that it has subtle edges; after that put it hot on the nail, and turn your hand all around the nail until it comes to the bottom of the nail; and leave it so III days until it begins to get rotting; then I make a plaster of wild mallows ground with silk, and leave the plaster on all night, and the nail will fall and be uprooted from its roots. 
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure the place with ointment hindering flesh until it is healed. 
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if they are converted by fire the body, and many times happen in hands and feet, it behooves you to bring them cautery of hot water; and is in such manner: take a cane of iron or steel, or a pen of vulture, and put on the nail and the small hole, that is to say, for calluses; and put the cane so that it prickles all around, then put a drop of hot water, and hold your hand well, and press your hand turning so that the edge of the cane comes to the root of the nail, and may find the hot water way deep to the root; and suffer the patient a little the burning of the hot water an hour; then let him so, and it will disengage all at all its roots. 
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	Thus do one after another, as long as you eradicate all those which are in the body, then cure the openings that generate flesh.  
li cure dou trembler	The cure of trembling
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some tremble from cold of nerves, or from quartan fever or another, it is necessary that you make to them .iiij. cauteries or .iv. on the spine of the back, .i. cautery between each spine; and .i. cautery or pez, and .i. on the stomach at the olive cautery; if leave will the trembling, and hasten will the healthy from the cold sickness.
des pustules puans	of pus-filled pimples
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	Sometimes apparent by fires the body bathed, or pimples painful, which come from large corrupted matters. 
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	If it is necessary at first when they appear that one makes cautery on each head of the pustule: a subtle cautery of myrtle wood, so that its point be seized by fire, or of long aristeloge root, or of the lentil cautery. 
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And sometimes the cauterize one at the beginning when they appear, according to this manner, and they cannot grow back from them, but are disrupted the superfluities that come from them, and are healed; but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood. 
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many times there are great hemorrhages from the artery that is cut at the wound that comes to the outside, or in the incision of the abscess, or in the cauterization of the limb, and similar things; and it is a very grievous thing to stop.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And nevertheless when this happens to anyone, hastily put your finger index upon the wound of the vein, and strain it much until the blood be quieted under your finger, and that no drop issues forth more; then place on fire the olive cauteries smaller and larger as many as they are all red; then take one, or greater or lesser according to the wound and its location where the artery is cut, and put the cautery upon that vein where you hold your finger, and hold the cautery there until the bleeding be stayed.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it jumps forth when you lift your finger from upon the vein, and the cautery is extinguished, then take hastily one other of the cauteries that are on fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease to make these one after the other until the vein is stretched; and guard that you do not burn the nerve which is beside, and that another malice does not come upon the patient; and know that when a vein shortens from the artery, one cannot well stretch it even when the artery is large, unless by one of the four ways that we have said: or by cautery, or by extraction when it is not treated, or by strong binding of thread, or by medicines put upon which have power to stretch the vein; and let it be bound and strained firmly.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who will bring a stretching of the lier tightly with straps or to put things burning upon it, or other similar things, if it does not profit so much.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to anyone and he has neither mire nor medicine present, then he must put his finger on the wound of the vein as we have said, and stretch it well until it is stretched above the wound and above the vein; and do not move the finger, but often moisten it with cold water that it be very cold until the vein is congealed and thickened and stretched; and make in front those things which he needs of cauteries and medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of the cures of the stones
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter all the illnesses for which it is necessary to use fire cautery or hot medicine, and the incisions and causes and instruments and shapes of the cauteries; and I have put that chapter from the head right down to the feet, and in this chapter I will go by the same way for those things that are more easily found than those you want.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And therefore, my dear child, as I begin this, it is necessary for you to learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of the cauteries, and for that reason it is necessary to take greater care.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you that you do not undertake folly. 
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many kinds of people come to cures. 
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	if they come from those who have gotten so sick with their illness that they die easily because of the hardship that they find in their illness, and the greatness of their evil; and of these one must have fear. 
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And of these there are some who tell you their meaning, and say: “Wait, I am healed”; and the patient is deceiving. 
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	It is not fitting that you consent to those who come to you with this manner, but put more trust in your honor than in your desire, and do not operate foolishly but wisely from those whom you are certain of, and whom you can have praise for; and use prognostication and indication in the cures of your patients so that health may be converted; and these will help you to acquire a good reputation, glory, and memory of length. 
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Most dear son, Our Lords give you good understanding and righteousness, and if you wish to aspire to the holy inspiration of his hand, Amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Or I have ordered you this chapter in devising by chapters, according to those that it is before or chapter of cauteries, that I have devised them from the chief until feet, for those that you find more easily those that you will need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	the chief full of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this sickness comes many times to children at birth, and when the midwife strains too hard the head of the child; and some time it comes from a reason unknown.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this sickness outside of children, and to all that I have seen it hastened death; and for that reason it seems to me that it is better to leave the work in such cures.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw one child whose shoulder was full of water, and the head grew larger each day until he could not bear it; and it seemed so much moisture that he died, and this moisture is gathered beneath the bone on the scapula, between the heart and the bone; and the work is such if the moisture is between the heart and the bone, and the abscess is small, that you cut in the middle of the head a wide slit; and be as long as two thumbs, as far as the moisture goes; and see here the shape of the spatula:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more swollen, and the abscess is larger, then make two slits in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is under the bone, and the signs that you see the edges of the head are open from each side, and the water leaps out when you press it with your hand inward, and this does not return to you: then you must cut in the middle of the head three slits according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision extract the moisture all outwards.  
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After you have strained the fissures of cloth and powders, and put wine and oil there, and let it so until the fifth day; then untie it, and cure the wound with bandages and ointments, and let the chief bandage be restrained, and then feed the patient dry meat from moisture as long as the limb is fortified and healed.  
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another manner of incision is that you look where opens the greatness of the abscess, and its assembly of fluid; for sometimes it is in front; sometimes behind; sometimes on the right; and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Cut therefore where the abscess opens, and its filling of fluid, and widen it according to what you have power; and guard that you do not cut the artery; and vein blood flows, so that the patient dies from the loss of blood and the evacuation of moisture.
de reume	of rheum
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When it happens to anyone a malady which is called "catarrh" at the eyes or in the chest, and the sickness is old, and the cure of medicine does not help, then the final cure is that cautery with this one on one covers the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	It therefore happens that when you see them covered, the patient must make his head back; then rub their place with a rough cloth until the arteries appear, then hold the patient's neck to the whole cloth; then look where the vein beats, and the veins of one and the other are after the ears, and so they are placed again; then sign the veins of the flesh, then cut both with a sharp spatula from II part, as long as the cut comes up to the bone, and it should be by the wide part of the head.  
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see, thrust the spatula under the artery and cut it above, cutting also as two thumbs across.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, it throws out blood continually upward.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open at the feeling, then you must measure the quantity of the space of III fingers, then seize it and make until the bone; and what it is necessary to put out blood is VI c/, and by chance a bit more or less, according to what the patient can suffer, and the repletion of the artery; then look at the wound: if it remains above the bone point of the syphac, then you must cover it so that pus does not come, then restrain the wound and tie it, and the cure of ointment until it is healed. 
de emigrainne	of migraine
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When old migraine comes, and acute catarrh, for the moistors of tears and the heats in the temples and old-fashioned foreheads and similar things, and it is medicated by means of cures of medicine and all that does not benefit them, then we extract the arteries of the temples and cauterize them, as we have recounted.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of their extraction is that the patient makes rear the hairs of his temples, and attends to the artery which opens in the temple, for it opens well by its beating, and is rarely found outside than in certain men who are too cold; and if it is found, strain the neck of the patient with some cloths, then rub the place with some rough cloth, and raise the place with hot water until the artery appears manifestly; then take the spatula of which this is the form:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	Then scrape the skin lightly until you reach the artery, then treat it above the incisions, and carefully separate the threads that are under each part; and if the artery is subtle, turn it with the point of the awl, then cut that part according to the quantity of the two bones. 
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if it is not cut, it does not leap at all throughout.  
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And treat the blood of .vj. c/, up to .iij.; and if the artery is large, it is necessary that you tie it in .ij. lengths with a strong double silk thread so that putrefaction does not come before the suturing of the wound, and there comes bleeding; then cut off the superfluity which is between the .ij. ligatures in the same hour, and then, if you wish, cauterize it with the cutellary cautery until the bone until the joints are cut; and this is the middle work, if the patient does not have fever and he is of warm complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the cautery is help to end the moisture: for this cause it is of greater help to moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	Where it is necessary for the extraction of arteries that one fills the place with old cotton and puts on top well-made tents; and when they are untied, let them be cured with dry medicines that make flesh grow, and with tents, until it is healed; and if without a ligature of the artery as much as you work on it, then hasten to cover by cautery, or you employ the place of vitriol and strain it to your hand that the wound is stained; and if you do not have these present, put over the place your cloth until the wound is frozen, and raise the place with cold water until the bleeding stops, and be restrained as it should be; and what is more helpful and lighter in the extraction of the artery is that you cauterize the vein of this cautery trenching at .ij. parts, but let the trenches be well spaced to keep their heat for longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instrument is too thick, it holds less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And must have between the two knives one, and it must be of great width, and then when you have marked the two joints, and you place the red hot iron on them until it comes to the bone, and cut the vein in two joints; and be separated between the two shoulders because it is not welded by this cautery at all, and this is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	Tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.
