When the tears from the eyes flow down the veins that are on the forehead above the face of power, and no benefit comes from medicine in doing so, and you see the face of the sick person shrink, and feel on their forehead a motion as if they were shivering; and where the eyes are swollen and wet so that the hairs of the eyebrows fall out, and the eyebrows are dried up, and scorched by the heat of the tears, then there is need for this cure.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And they called it "contused cure" in the old times, and it is that you do behind the patient who has this disease the hairs that he has or front, then he makes III incisions on his forehead equally according to the length of the forehead; and let one of the incisions be as II should entirely remove the forehead down to the nose, and the other II along the ribs above the papers, and keep yourself from the incision of the arteries that are on the II ribs above the papers; and move your hand away from the continuation of the II jaws, and let each wound be the quantity of III does across the joins; and have prepared a piece of sponge and many cloths for wiping the blood, then put the sharp spatula with the II parts as it is here the shape:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	from the incision which is below the temple to the second incision; and scrape all the core that is between the two incisions to all the flesh that is on the bone, then make another part from the middle incision to the other second, and then extract further this spatula.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If it is put in the first notch the instrument which is called "cultellary", and is very sharp on one side, and on the other side is blunt, not sharp, and this is its shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And put the rib cutting towards the flesh near the heart, and the rib side towards the bone, and the point until it comes to the middle fissure. 
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut all the vessels that descend from the head as the eyes so long as the incision is continuous to the one who opens the heart, and then another part make in the middle cut to the other end; and then take out the blood evenly, and express their place for the taken blood; then put in each cut a tent of old cotton, and put on cloths moistened in wine and oil and asile, and keep that no abscess come there; and at the third day untie the lien, and then administer much boiled water, then the cure of basilicon ointment with rose oil, and other cures as one cures wounds, until it is healed. 
dou reume des eulz	of the eye
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When any person comes with acute catarrh, and you see the eyes red and small, and the vision weakened, and the membranes burned; and the hair falls out, and where it is felt there is a sharp pain, and the patient sneezes; therefore you know by these accidents that those matters and this catarrh come from many veins, and the cure that is there, such is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And it is that you command the patient to rear their forehead, then make a great fissure in the middle of the forehead, and another one through the brow. 
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And begin from the cut of the left temple to the right temple, and let the incision reach the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move in the feed; and when the bone is uncovered, wipe all the blood with a sponge, and then suture between the two lips of the cut and put old cotton there, and linen bandages; then bind above with cloths moistened in wine and oil, and keep yourself from a hot abscess; when it is removed, it is necessary that you rub the bone until pus begins to arise, then cure it with drying things, which make flesh come up. 
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take two parts of wheat flour, and four parts of colophony, and make a plaster from it; and administer it on these wounds to harden the cartilage throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of stopping up the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that which falls into ears is one of the four things: or grains, or beast, or stone of mine or something similar as iron; or seed, like lentils, beans, peas; or flowing thing like water and oil and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When it falls into the ear stone or another manner of thing that does not join to the ear, nor grows in the ear, then put the ear to the sun. 
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the stone, if there distill any drop of violet oil or sesame oil, then administer extraction; and cause him to sneeze by condiment, and plug his nostrils when the sneezes come, and put around the ear pieces of cloth or wool; and keep the ear upwards. 
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Many times comes force by this cure; and if it does not come force, then administer an extraction with fine tweezers, for that is the form: 
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it comes out with tweezers, it is good; if not, administer extraction with a fine single-edged tool; and if it does not come out with that, make a small snare of thread and insert the head of the snare or through the opening of the ear forcefully, and stop what surrounds the snare with soft wax so that the wind cannot enter with the snare; then pull it out carefully, because many times it comes out as we have said; and if it does not come out in this way, take a little glutin (birdlime) and put it on any instrument which is pointed for this purpose, and place a bit of cotton around it; then press the glutin onto the stone or whatever it may be, and pull it out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not jump from all these things that we have said, then hasten to split the ear so that an abscess comes out and spasms; and the manner of the splitting is that you first bleed the patient of the cephalic, and extract blood according to the measure of his virtue, then make the patient sit between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small cut at the root of the ear in the fat where it depends; and let the cut be like a crescent moon, as far as you come to the stone, then the bone according to your power, and suck it carefully with your mouth; and treat until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is grains that are inside and it swells, then administer extraction; and if it cannot issue, then administer one spatula thin according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and administer incision to that grain.  
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not do this when you think that the grain is moist because of the moisture of the ear, until you have made many pieces of it; then extract it with subtle pincers and a suction device, as we have said, so that the extraction be aligned. 
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the ear ache therefore when it falls in the ear it is necessary that the patient uses a first of externals remedies, and fill the ear with old cotton. 
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And lie down on that same ear where the water is. 
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If she jumps forward because of this, it is good.  
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If it is not so, take many stones according to the length of your thumb, and lightly heat them in the fire; and put them in the patient's one ear opening, and hold up above, from his feet on the other side, and place a stone upon the stone which is in the ear; and do not cease making this from stone to stone until the water flows out entirely, and so it will be completely drained; and if you see, take a reed, and put one end into the ear, and the other end hold it in fire until the most tender part of the reed is burned; then reheat another piece of reeds until the water flows out completely, as we have said in the stone.  
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of the beast, if it is of small body, as a flea and similar things, cure it as we have said in the division; but if it is of great body which one can feel, then administer extraction with pincers; and that is the thing more light to remove which is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms in the ears, when you cure it as we have said in the division and where we treat distillations, and the cure does not help, then it is necessary that you look at the ear in the sun: if there appears any worms, then treat them with subtle pincers, and if they do not appear, then take the cauterization of which this one is the form:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And be narrow below and wide above. 
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And put the most subtle chief in the ear according to the quantity of the suffering of the patient, then succeed forming to all the dog; do this often as many worms exit.  
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not obey to this, so stuff the ear with cotton as I have said in the stone; and if they do not come out further as we have said, so administer distillations that the ancients have proven in the incision of worms, and you will find them who treat distillations; and if distillate your oils and your medicines in the ear to all this instrument, for this is the form as you see: 
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And let it be of silver or iron, narrowed below to one small opening, and wide above for distilling; and for pressing inside the distillation one instrument of iron well made for this purpose, and if you wish take a razor and wrap around the point neatly with cotton; then put your oil or your juice, and that which you wish of your medicines in the chain, and let the chain be in the ear; then put inside the razor all the cotton, and press your hand moderately until the oil is distilled or at the end of the ear; and let the patient feel it inside, and let the distillations be one pock heated by the fire, then as it is distilled in the ear; and guard that it not be too cold, for the medicine would not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of stopping up the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without a hole in their ears; and this same thing happens to men through the stoppage of a wound, or of flesh born inside the ear, and these stoppages come sometimes from inside the ear, if one cannot see them; and sometimes they happen .i. pock deep inside the ear, and one can see it well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	That one which comes from inside, if one cannot see it, is of bad healing in many cases, and in this one sees that you must put the ear of the patient to the sun; and look inside: if you see the inflammation apparent, then the work has total these spatumile of this thing is the form.
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And be sharp and trenchant in front and behind all plain, so that it does not blister the ear; if the inflammation is of flesh born or core of the ear, then hold it with fine pincers, and cut it lightly, until that flesh is wholly removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the suppuration is in the ear, take a subtle razor light and heat it a little at the fire, then put it into the body of the ear. 
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the inflammation that the patient feels greatly in the ear, pierce lightly, and keep that you do not wound the nerves of the ear; then put in the ear a tent according to the width of the opening, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment. 
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this for no day until the wound is closed, or you take a tent and moisten it in rose water, and powder on pulverized vitriol; and if you see the ear inflamed, then it is necessary that you withdraw the tent and move another tent moistened in cerate which is made of rose oil and wax, until the inflammation is removed; then cure it as long as it is healthy.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding occurs, dip a sponge and wrap it in cold water, and put it on the ear, and use other cures which remove the bleeding that are or treat distillations.
de la char des papieres	of the paper of the writing
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This is the healing for those eyes that come from paper when they are moist and dry, so it befits you to extend them with tweezers and pincers, and the tip of a spatula from their roots; then put on top of it pounded vitriol.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if it does not come out with this method, then cauterize them with a subtle lentil-shaped cautery, and after the incision is made, the cauterization takes effect; and many times they disappear, because nothing remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return at all.
de la gresle	of the groin
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times come in papers of the eyes things that seem glassy in their form and hardness, and for this reason this disease is called "hailstorm," and it is an assembly of moisture great in the paper above and below; the work is such: take ward if the hailstone moves from one side and the other, and it is a light thing to know; then make the wide, then the peel of each part lightly, then take it with tweezers, and cut. 
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you cannot cover it without feeling a bit of the paper, do not worry the patient; and if the tear is large, sew it together, and treat it until it is healed; and if it is small, do not use force, because the flesh restores it quickly and creates flesh. 
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the hail is descending into the inside of the ear towards the upper part, so turn the paper over, and being the hail to pliers, and the cut and press on one side and the other; and if the paper is removed by the incision, it does not grieve anything; and when the hail is cut, leave the eye of salted water, and cure the place of that which prevents cartilage until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a fat that is engendered in the tissues of the papers above, and this happens more to children than to others, and grieves their eyes greatly, and they come to have catarrh in the mornings, and cannot look at the light of the sun because the tears hasten to their eyes; and for this they lie down on their faces afterward, and sleep on them, and are their papers below their eyebrows moist that the inflammation and appearance has covered with exinach which opens in the eye.  
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the place to your thumbs and feel the separation between them.  
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of the work is that the patient puts his head on your knee; and then take one drapeil of linen, and prepare a tent in the manner of a circle according to the quantity that contains exina from each part, then put it on top; and press with your fingers on one side and the other, so that the exina is assembled within the circle; then make in the middle of the moistor with the spatula cutting a fissure of the width, and not be more than the wound that one makes in the vein; and make the leather in depth until you come to the exina; and in more disorders comes exina from the fissure, according to the form of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Extract therefore with a whole piece of cloth between your fingers on the outside, and turn your hand right and left until it is spread; and guard that you do not add in the fissure, until you come to all the spatula up to the eye, that you do not bleach it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the exit does not open at the beginning of the split, so lightly pry the split until it opens; then extract as we have said, then moisten cloths in oil and vinegar, and put on top, and restrain with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if there are such men who grind hay and put it on to corrupt the moisture that is lodged. 
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then care for it until it is healed.  
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it comes to the place abscess hot, so the cure of plasters soothing until it is healed.  
des poilz des papieres	of hairs of papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When in papers hairs are born adjusted other than the natural ones, and are envelted, they harm the eyes, and bring various diseases like accustomed tears and softening of the papers and albuginea, as much as this is the cause of the destruction of the eyes; and the cure is according to .iiij. manners: or by cautery whole fire, or by medicine ague according to that which it is before or chapter of cautery, and is done or by incision and suture or by canes, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It is necessary that you put the head of the patient on your left hand, then turn the paper of the eye with your right hand; if it is converted, it is good; if not, put a needle with one thread above; and whether it is near the edge of the paper where the hair grows near these hairs, and bring one thread above all the paper, and turn it to the razor; then make in the part below the paper, below the hairs adjusted, at all the spatula, from the great tear up to the small; then extract one thread, and put under the paper a small tent of cotton and drapery, then sign above the paper a figure of an enche, like the leaf of myrtle, and however it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity that you see raising the paper which is divided at all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if it happens to someone who needs it, cut a large quantity of the paper according to what the paper is softened; then make across all the spatula on the II lines that you have marked, and commence from the bottom a great tear up to little; and let one of the tears be near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then put the incision into one of the two angles close to the heart, then peel it completely; then assemble the two lips with a stitch of a needle with all fine wool thread, and wipe the blood, and make air out the superfluity of the threads on the two eyebrows with nothing sticky, if you want to do this; and if not, take no care, then leave the stitch and the threads until III days or IIII; then cure the wound without stitches with dry things and constricting, because the paper revives by the touch of the wound and the joining of it, but the stitch is changed (as the ancients said), and this work without fear; and if in another way: and it is that you mark the paper with a figure which is like the leaf of myrtle, as we have recounted, to III incisions according to the shape which is here. 
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then cut what surpasses the small forces equally according to the form which is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you do not have power to hold the pliers, and the thing is not equal, take a needle that has the thread, and put it in the middle of the figure; and put the other thread next to the big tear, and the second thread next to the small one, and assemble between your two threads equally; then raise your hand equally, and raise all the skin on what you have signed, as we have recounted, then assemble the two lips of the wound by stitching, and cure it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with cerote and similar soothing ointment; and sometimes it happens that the hair of the paper are converted: so it is necessary that you use what we have said about the incision; but the stitch in one and the other is more artificial. 
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure of the slings is as follows: and that you convert the paper and the fold inside according to what I have said, and then make .ij. slings by art, and .ij. subtle ligaments as long as the paper and the width of the spatula are; and cut the .ij. heads from .ij. parts where you hold the threads; then assemble one and the other subtly on top of the paper above the eye, and strain the .ij. slings from the .ij. parts that form; and let it remain like this for some days, and the skin that is strained will die and shrink and bear itself, until it comes out by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it delays, if it is cut with some force, then cure it until it is healed; and when the wound is sewn up, and the paper has been lifted, and the hairs will no longer prick; and this is the form of the II cannons that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	the works are such that you prick an awl, and it puts one thread of silk soft and fine; then assemble the heads and tie them together subtly, and let the length of the threads be a palm long; then order in the chase another thread of silk brightly, and tie the chief of the thread; then put the patient's head on your hand; and let it be toward the sun so that the work is clarified, for it is a subtle and small work; then put the needle to the whole chase in the root of the hair close-set, and make it pierce the paper smoothly until you draw it upwards from the natural hair; then extract the hair up to the chase, and put into the chase that hair, if there are one or two or three or more; then extract your hand until the hairs come out all the chase in the paper with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the chase is treated and the hairs do not come out with it, then you will draw the chase down to all the thread that you have ordered it, until the chase comes out of the hole above and you see it by the vision of the eye; then you will draw the chase and the thread, and close the eye and let it be closed for two or three days, until the hair hardens in its place and the flesh grows above; and if the hairs are small, accompany one long hair from the natural cheeks, and let it rise with that one or you leave it, until it is lengthened and then lift it.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the rot of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this illness which is called "aleacrati" or rot comes to the eye, there are two ways: one natural, and the other unnatural. 
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens by suddenness of wound, or cutting or cautery, and by similar things.  
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the manner of the work in it is that you split that suture, and loosen the lips of it, and put inside tents of linen, and tie it until it is healed; and it does not become that you use in the cure of it of things that dry and restrain.  
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do this, the illness returns worse than the first; but there is a work of softening things, like fenugreek; and the rose of water or high and flax seeds are cooked, and diacoylon oil melted in any oil, and envelop a tent, and cure with this. 
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your cure is that you take care that it does not close again according to the form that it was before; and these operations that we have said are nothing but remedies for this disease, so that it does not return according to the form that it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the char that comes in the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This illness which is dislocations is truly called "axacrati", and it is natural and accidental. 
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accident comes from wounds and cuts and cautery and similar things; and the way of the work in this is that you pierce a needle, in which it has a double thread, and put it into the flesh, and make it pierce from the left tear to the right, so that the thread comes out to the two shoulders of the flesh; then the flesh on top of the entire needle, and the cut with the spatula wide. 
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the figure of the paper returns according to what is due, it is good; if those are not, then take the razor and put it in the split, and turn the paper, and make splits where it costs inside the paper; and be the heads of the two splits at the two angles of the incision that you have cut, and make one angle so that when they are assembled, the figure is like the figure of a letter which has the name "I griesche"; then remove that flesh, according to the quantity that its cost is raised down from what follows the paper, then adjust the two parts separated, and the seams with a thread of wool; then care for it as we have said about softening medicines, and bandages, until it is healed. 
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the ailment comes from a cut or suture or cautery, it is necessary that you make a plain incision under the hairs of the papers, and according to what is said above; then sever between the two leaves of a tent, as I have said; and one must do the work according to the form of the illness, because it is very diverse in form, and the wise masters equip everything with all their power how they make it return to its natural form; and the patient himself, according to what is necessary for the work and instruments in many dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	of the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this suture happens to humans in such a manner that the paper above is joined with the white of the eye, and it cannot move or do its natural works, then it is necessary that you put the point of a razor under the paper, and lift it up; and the being as pinches, until you cut what is hardened at the spatula, which should not be too sharp nor too trenchant, so that the patient may not suffer that the spatula too sharp does not blind the eye; and be your incision, which you scrape off that assembly, lightly, so that the paper returns according to its natural form; and it heals all that assembly, and do no times in the eye salt water, and the lev of sweet water, and of colliers; then put between the paper and the eye a tent of linen, and put on top of the eye wool moistened in yolk; and after the third day use the colliers and things so much until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the angle of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the angle is in .ii. manners: it is nervous and similar to one hard syfac, and another which is not nervous, but is similar to white moistor frozen, that when one touches it with iron and one cures it panre as pinches, so it cannot; and one and the other semblance commences towards the great tear, and crosses poc and poc until it covers all the view and all the light and the movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of the incision is that the patient puts his head in your hand, then opens his eyes; and lift the paper with your hand, then coil the angle with small doubleure, and the stem upwards; then take a needle, and put one hair of horse, or of sheep, or of ox, and one strong thread; and double the point of the needle one poc and put it into the angle, and pierce it with all the needle, and tie the angle with a thread and the stem upwards, and scrape all the hair the edge of the angle that follows the prunele and silk to the hair until the head, then cut the remaining in the root of the tear with all the subtle spatumile and as small forces, and leave the char natureil or tear, so that by the incision does not come the body of tears acostumeement; and no times estent the angle at the oncine solely, and to the thread, as we have said; then the scrape one has with all the subtle spatumile souef of this is the form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And guard that the spatula does not touch the fleshy cloth and break it, and that the prickle be not pierced; and after the incision put in the eye a bit of crushed silk, and of the collar made of lead, and let it remain until the next day; then cure it as is fitting until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the fingernail is not nervous, and you cannot put in the needle, and the pincers cannot enter, many times this semblance of a fingernail is cured with medicines; and it grows as I have recounted in the division, and if you see it covered, then work the eye of the patient, and take the spatula light bit sharp according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And raise the fingernail subtly, and if you see that it does not decrease and the reason is rapid, then distill from your mouth into the eye collar made of lead and red collar and crushed silk, and stop the eye until the next day; then begin the other work according to this same work, as long as it is all removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing is contrary to you in the eye, such as a pus-filled abscess, then milk it, and cure the abscess first until it is clean, then restart the work as before, until it is clean.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh from the tear harms the eye by great annoyance, then suspend it to the eye socket and cut off a part, not all at once, so that no more tear comes; then distill in the eye red collyrium which is made of litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh which grows on the iris
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	The eyes of some men are born sometimes red, and cover the eyelid and restraint on the papers and turn them to the fire, and seem like a rose of a balustrade; and the work is that the sick man puts his head in your healthy one, then the worker opens the eyes, and coil all that flesh with needles suitable for those, and the sustain it with force; then cut the first flesh, and go on cutting to the shaver until the end, and keep that you do not blind the eye during the work; and let the incision be like the spatula that we have said in the incision of the angle and as small forces of which one removes the sebum, as the form after this chapter demonstrates; and when the incision is accomplished and all the flesh is removed, then apply the oil of basil or you distill red colic and similar medicines corrosive, and put on the eye fire cotton with yolk of egg, so that it be assured of a hot abscess; and if there remains nothing, and the blood cloth mounts over your eyes, and you doubt a hot abscess, so leave the eye and cure the abscess of things soothing a hot abscess; then return to your work until it is healed, and thus do as many flesh are adjusted in the eye by this semblance.  
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But nonetheless it behooves you to heal the cure of each weak oil of the natural way; and of the accidental way, in the work of iron; and do not put your hand in any of these works as long as you see that this member is suffering from that work.
des voines des eulz	of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	Veins are red that are covered over the eye, and take from sight their work and weaken the eye all days. 
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	It is therefore necessary that first you look at the eye, whether it is in place or not, and there is no other ailment besides the eye; therefore, the coil in this manner: instruct the patient to put their head on your shoulder, then suspend those veins throughout the entire neck according to your knowledge, and let the needles be doubled subtly according to this form: 
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And let two lines be by degrees in one body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then coil as forces those veins subtly, and wipe the blood hour after another, until you see remove those veins from the eye; and guard that you do not prick the eye with the points of the spatulas, and make this work at the hour of midday before the sun, and be very fervent in your work so that you do not cut further than those veins; and when you will have done this, if distill in the eye kohl green and red to corrupt what is remained of the vein.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you do not have power to gather all these in that hour, then make a plaster on the eye of things soothing the pain of the eyes, and let it for some days until the pains are appeased and is assured of a hot abscess, then begin again according to this manner which is before until it is healed; and this is the form of forces:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The mire are called "arissati" fistula: when you cure it with cautery and medicine burning according to those that I have before said, and it is not healed, then there is something in it that you cut on the abscess, where it should die, and treat all the moisture that is there, until the bone is uncovered.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is uncovered, and you will see the corruption and the blackness, then take all the instruments of which this is the form; and it is called "sharp chief," and it is made from fire iron one chief point, and is pointed like a file as it is in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And put it on the place of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your two hands, and press your hand a little until you know that that corruption is removed; and do this several times, then restore the place with drying medicines.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the wound is sutured and flesh grows, and the body of the bow is sutured, and it remains thus for 40 days, and it does not renew and is not suppurating, know that it is healed; if this is not the case, then there is no other remedy than to bring the fistula back to the opening according to this form: and it is that you uncover the bone a second time with iron, and with sharp medicines, and when it is uncovered, take the forest according to this form, and let the head of iron be at 3 angles, and let the shaft be thinned until the top as you see here.  
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place it on the bone next to the lacrimal bone, and keep your hand away from the eye socket, then turn all the way around until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it through that which comes in his eye if he holds his hand on his cheek; and then restore the place of dry medicines as I have taught you, and when the flesh is born and hardens the parts, then the matter goes to the cheek; thus it is an easier thing for the patient. 
de l’issue de l’oil	of the eye's issue
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyes are open fully and there is no disturbance in the nose or diminution, then you must bind the patient; then heal, then put suction cups or a heater without hurting to suck, then put on the eye one linen made of wool, aloe and frankincense and sarcocolla, and then strain the eye, and plaster it with bandages and cloth; and the manner of the cloths is that you take cloths soft enough, and double each in four, and then put one on top of the other according to the quantity that the eyes need; then strain by above a strong bandage, and resume suction cups to suck without hurting; then remove the suction cups and leave the eye strained day and night, and if the linen softens, then you must strain it much; then remove the linen after the day and night, and if you see the eye healing, it is good; if not; then resume the plastering and bandages and linen and suction cups until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	of the displacement of a web woven
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When a disruption comes in the woven web, then it opens and comes forth like pieces of resin, as if one were seeing; therefore, if you see it covered, the work is such that you thrust a needle into the root of the lower part until that above, then thrust another needle where there is one double thread from the part of the tear; and make it pierce, and leave the first needle according to the disposition; then cut the place of the double thread and tie one part of the web together, and restrain it well, then extract the needle and put on top a small piece of wool in abundance of an egg; and leave it until the threads fall with the web, then cure the eye with comforting things until the wound is healed; and at no time is the wound restrained by the web on each side with a circle of cloth, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eye gives a great appearance, then pierce it with the sharp instrument that comes from within the eye, and correct the albuminous moisture and bring down the eyes, and enter into them immediately; then extract it until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	of the bulb of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This sickness which is called «alcunnati»  is nothing other than a bow which is assembled in the eye, seeming like water descending, and it is not water; and the manner of the appearance of the work is that you make the patient sit upon the prepared and straight seat, then take the head between your hands from II parts, and move it so that you see the bow come upwards to your eyes; then be ens fichie, and do not descend and let it be disordered the light, and the patient sees things as he used to; and if it does not descend below, know that it is water, and if the descending of the bow is not arranged as we have said. 
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you make the patient sit between your hands, then take the subtle spatula and make on the cornea of the eye, a point by the continuation of the conjunctive with the cornea and the crown, until the bow is issued; and when it is issued, you distill in the hot water mixed with honey, or water or fenugreek that is boiled and honey, then be cured of another cure until it is healed. 
des aigues de l’oil	of the waters of the eye
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have seen the likenesses of swords in division, and what is necessary to examine; thus we work according to health.  
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It is necessary that you make the patient sit between your hands crossed, away from the light of the sun, and tie their healthy eye and hold it very tightly; then place the paper of the eye in your left hand if the eye is left, or in your right hand if the eye is right; then take in your right hand, if the eye is left, the instrument which is called "almagda", or in your left hand, if the eye is right; then put the point of the instrument beside the crown by the width of a fingernail in that white part of the eye to the part of the less tear, then push the instrument that is called "almagda" virtuously, and tighten your hand until it pierces into the white part of the eye, and feel that almagda comes to the empty thing; and it is necessary that the measure of the way almagda be at the perfect measure of the space which is from the pupil to the end of the black; and this is the crown of the eye; so you will see the bone in that paper for the clarity of the cornea, and then put the instrument until where the liquid is, then express it out one way after another. 
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If the water descends now, let the patient see it before him and the instrument in his eye. 
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After repose I little, and if the water comes back up the second way, put force with the instrument, and when it is ens fixed and it does not go up, straightaway withdraw the almond lightly by turning your hand poc and poc; and then put back in water a little of seil gemme, and leave from that the oil inside. 
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put with a vessel of oil or soft wool soaked in rose oil and an abundance of egg white, and tie it with the healthy eye. 
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those who are of our time, put on top a kind of mortar with abundance of egg. 
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if almagda cannot enter the eye because of its hardness, for there are some men who have their eyes too hard, then it is necessary that you take the instrument which is called "alberit", from which this is the form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And pierce therefore the conjunctive alone, and do not go too deeply in by force, but make it subtle, then put almond, as we have said; and at the completion of the work equip the patient with the doctor following, in which he sleeps on his back in the dark place; and be devoid of all movements, and eat light meats, and do not move his head neither to the right nor to the left, and let him be tied according to his disposition up to the third day; then untie him in the same dark house, and probe his sight, and let him see some things, and then put back the bandage until the seventh day; and it is not necessary that you do this during the hour of the cure or after the incision now, but it is necessary that you align this, because the water rises quickly.  
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	When the abscess comes, that you loosen the eye before the seventh day, and the address of those who assuage the abscess; and when it is calmed, then untie the view and put on its face the orilliet to cover any day, and be in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then he goes from the house little by little, and converts himself to his case; and know that none of the disciples should interfere in this case. 
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from the Yrach, who told us that in their country they make almond perceive, so that one sucks the liquid, but nevertheless I have never seen any in our land, nor have I ever read it in books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the appearances of the forms of almonds, for those who do not know them they see them; and be of pure rain.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And let the head of each of this same subtlety, and the last one in three angles acute.
de la char sor le neis	of the bone upon the joint
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	At no time are born or made various joined parts, because of which some seem scorpions with many feet; and if there are such ones where the flesh is discolored of a bad hue, and then some flesh of good color. 
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In that case of these chariots which is swollen and not cracked, it behooves you to make the patient sit between your hands against the sun; and open his nostrils, and place the oncine in those chariots, and the trail out; then cut what you can sustain with the subtle sharp spatula on one part, as long as you know that this chariot is completely removed. 
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if any thing remains that one cannot cover, open it all i.e., with instruments subtle and lightly so that nothing remains; and if without the swelling or abscess is caught, secure it as it is fitting; and if it are malignant abscesses, hasten and cauterize them until the blood is stopped and all the matter is removed, then pour on nettle or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the nose works and moisture comes up to the palate, know that it is healthy; and if the moisture does not pierce as it should, know that there is flesh in the bone above, so that the instruments do not come to cut: therefore, it befits you to put I thread of linen a bit thick, and be soaked with hands ours, and have between each knot a space I must or less; and put the patient’s shoulder on the thread in his nose to its end, and pull in odorating until it comes through the nose into the mouth; and many times do children thus at school, and it is light thing to him who wants to do so; then hold the head that comes out of the nose with one hand, and the other head that comes out of the mouth with the other hand, and know one after the other being as those which are or thread. 
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do this as much as you know that the new ones have corrupted that flesh, then treat the wound, wipe the blood, and moisten the wound in Egyptian ointment, and put it back straight to the head as before; do this III days or more, until the ointment corrodes all that remains of flesh; and then put on the head a bandage of plank for some days until it is healed, and if it needs drying medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument for purging the head, to which one distills oils and medicines onto the head: 
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And let it be of silver or iron, resembling an open lamp, as a caine, and conduct it so; and if you see fit, make a closed caine, and let the instruments be full for purging the head; and have one handle to the head for holding it when one heats the oil or any liquor.
de la char sor le neis	of the bone upon the joint
