Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times a sickness is born upon the joint called "telul," and it grows and becomes large, so much that it is a terrible thing to see; and for this reason you should cut it at the beginning, and extract all bone, then put on its place the cautery or burning medicine; and if one delays in cutting until it is large, beware if it is hard, with dark color, of poor feeling: do not touch it with iron because it is an inflamed abscess, for when one cuts it once, great harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is soft to the touch, not dark colored, and you see that one can cut it all, then reassure the patient and cut it without fear, and cure the place with dry and restraining things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the joint is cut and closed
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when the solution of continuity comes in one of these working cartilages, it profits little, for in no humans. 
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is therefore necessary that when this happens to anyone, it is seen if the wound is fresh in all its blood; and then adjust the two lips together with a seam, then treat it until it is healed; and if the lips are already dried on one side and the other, it is necessary that you scrape all the parts of their core until they heal, then assemble the two lips to a seam, and restrain them, and powder above powder of dragon's blood, and ground incense; and put on the powders a piece of strong plaster or another adhesive plaster, and leave it until it dries out by itself, then treat it with ointment until it is healed. 
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of the suture is that you assemble the solution: or by needles, as we have said in the suture of the belly; or by thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	To men's mouths, abscesses hard occur within, similar to grains of millet, smaller and larger; therefore it behooves you to turn the lips, and cut on each one, and take with tweezers and cut it in each part; then put the place after incision of powdered vitriol, until the blood is stained; and then the salve of this, and cure the place with dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	Of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times flesh grows on the gums, that the ancients call "albulus"; so it behooves you to support it with tweezers, and cut it at its root, and leave the wound or blood; then put on the place powdered vitriol, or other astringent and drying powders; and if that flesh returns after the incision, and many times it occurs, so cut it a second time, and cauterize it: if it does not return after the cautery; and these are the forms of the instruments for cutting.
des sordens	of deafness
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes they are gathered at the head of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, sores which are ugly and rough; and sometimes the tooth is black and yellow and green, as long as the corruption comes to the gum, and the teeth are putrid; so it behooves you to make the sick person sit between your hands, and his cheeks be in your palm, and clean the teeth or the sores that appear, until nothing remains there; and thus do of the blackness and the greenness, and the yellowness and the other stains, as long as they are visible; and if one removes what is at the first reason, it is good; if those do not, then begin again on the second day and the third, until you have all cleaned; and know that teeth need various types of instruments to clean, according to what the work shows you, because the scraper with which one cleans outside the teeth has other forms than that which one cleans between the teeth; and these forms and others be prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It behooves you when you cure the tooth of its pain that you tarry with drawing as much as you can, because one should not do otherwise; for it is a substance very high until such time as one has no excuse to clean.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Therefore when the patient is constrained to endure suffering, it is necessary that you be certain of which tooth aches. 
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Many times the pain suffers the patient, and thinks that it is a tooth of Saint, and draws out the good tooth; and all way does not depart him the pain because of this, as long as the evil remains, for we have already done it to his elders; and when you are well certain of the tooth hurting, then it behooves you to scrape around the tooth with every little spatula strong to ward the gum from all parts; then the moves to your two or with tweezers subtle at the first pinch and pinch, as long as it is well dislodged, then confirm the tweezers well; and let the head of the patient in your holy between your knees, and hold him well so that he does not move. 
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After the tooth is extracted straight without breaking it, and if it does not come out easily, take one of these instruments and gently insert it on each side, and move it like you did at first. 
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is pierced and broken, it is necessary that you fill it with cloth where the holes are; and if you restrain it subtly with pliers, that it does not break when you restrain it; and it is necessary to work very skillfully around the gum to displace the tooth.  
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And therefore warn well that you do not break it, and remain a part, and return to the patient by the malice of the root greater pains than the first.  
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And guard yourself that you do not do as the ignorant healers do, who by their haste and their boldness break sometimes the cartilage, and bring them not what we have recounted; but they bring often by the opening of these great illnesses for the roots that remain there, or for the cartilage that they break, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is pulled, wash its place with wine or oil and salt; and if bleeding comes from it, which often happens, apply to the place vitriol ground; and if that does not help, cauterize it. 
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments, for which one must sharpen the teeth first, should be with long points and thick handles, so that they do not double when you pull the tooth; and these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And be of thick members so that they do not bend when pulling, and be made of well-tempered iron, and be toothed for better grip.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains in the breast, it is necessary to put upon it moistened cotton wool in butter for a day or two. 
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	As long as the eyes are moist, put the pincers called "algefri" in them, so that the eye seems like a bird's beak; and inside be made as if with a file and this is the form: 
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these tongs, then it is necessary that you uncover the flesh around the root, and there put the instrument which is called "althali", that is to say, a spatula, of which this is the form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And let it be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root jumps out with these, it is good; if these do not, then help yourself with all the instruments, of which the forms come after here:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one helps oneself with this instrument which has two prongs, of which this is the form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other iron tools which are in front in the shape of teeth, and of this instrument which resembles large pliers, of which this is the form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let this instrument be such that it cannot break, and know that many instruments are made of teeth; and also other instruments, which are not all counted; and the wise masters subtle find by themselves their instrument, according to what their works and the disease show them, for there are such diseases that the ancients do not teach any instrument for the diversity of others; and if one breaks a bone or another bone, or can, then seek the instruments that are needed, as I have said to you, and help with gestures, by this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be thick and well-fitting to hold the bone so that it does not escape but can be held and removed; and then restore its place with medicines suitable for this, and if there is rot in the bone, and it is small, then the king has all these instruments:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the teeth appear not according to the body's natural shape, and the form is ugly, and even in young women, it is necessary that you know if the tooth is new after the tooth, and is not in its right place, and cannot be smoothed or filed; then raze it; and if it is attached with the tooth, then take this instrument whose shape is here, and is like a small beak, and let it be of tempered steel, sharp at the tip:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the coping piece by piece in hands a few days for the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the others, and if it appears that one can be filed, then file with a similar file as this is its form.
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is also like the file with which one makes needles; and in filing the tooth piece by piece in hands a few days gently, so that it does not move until it falls; then make it smooth at the end without any burr, and if the tooth is too sharp and it pricks the tongue, then file the roughness until it is equal, so that it does not prick the tongue nor corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the tooth loosens
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the front tooth moves, either by percussion or by falling, and the patient cannot press on it so that he does not bite, and you have cured them with restraining medicines, and this is no good; if it is necessary to restrain it with a gold wire, because the silver wire becomes green and spoils, but gold never changes; and let the wire be neither too thick nor too thin, according to the quantity of the space between the teeth; and if you see the teeth crowded, take the wire and put it double between the two healthy teeth, then place the chiseled piece between the loose teeth, if there is one or more, until you come sagely to the healthy tooth on the other side; then begin the covering again to the point where you began, and strain your hand subtly and wisely, until it does not move at all; and let the thread be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape. 
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then catch the bones of the thread with pliers and assemble them, and put them between the healthy tooth and the one in its place as if it did not press down on the tongue. And then let him stay so tight as long as he can, and if it comes undone or the threads break, bind it again with another thread. Thus remains and serves until all its time, and this is the form of the teeth and the figure of the arrangement of the two healthy teeth, and the two broken ones, as you see: 
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls out, then it is put back in its place, fresh to fresh, as we have said; and let no one interfere who is not wise and patient, and sometimes the shape of a tooth made of deer bone is made, and it is put in the place where the deficiency is, and it is restrained as we have said, and it remains and serves thus for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cut the ligament of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	At no time is this ligament which comes from under the tongue or nature, that one is born thus; or by accident of a joined wound; and the work is such that you operate the mouth of the sick person, and have his head in your hand, and lift the tongue; then cut the nervous ligament wide, until the tongue is dislodged from its place, and if there is stiffness or anything else, and this is from the joining of a wound, so put the awl and cut wide that ligament; and keep that the cutting is not too deep, for the artery which is underneath; and when you have done, then raise the cold rose water and of fresh water, then put under the tongue a tent of linen; and bind the sick person each night, that the places may not join. 
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if bleeding occurs, place broken glass on the spot; and if the bleeding persists, cauterize it with a small cautery, which is good for this purpose; then treat it with another remedy until it is healed. 
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it of dark color or black or hard, so that the sick person does not feel it, then do not touch it, because it is a chancre; and if it is declining to be white, and there is moisture, then put the awl, and cut it with a fine spatula, and deliver it from one side and the other; and if the blood does not stop in your work, then put on top ground vitriol until it is bleached, then return to your work until you have extracted everything; then lift the level of honey and seal, and cure it with other cures until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	Of abscesses in the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes within the throat come boils called “godath,” and they are properly called the two almonds, and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, then take care: if it is a hard abscess of small size and fuscous color, then do not touch it with iron. 
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is thick, do not touch it with iron, also for the discharge of blood; but let it alone until it is dead, and then you will divide it, or it would break by itself; and if it is of white color red, and the root is subtle, have the instrument prepared to cover, but first look if the abscess chills rests and is appeased.  
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Therefore make the patient sit in front of the sun, and his head be on your lap, and he opens his mouth and you place the serjans between his hands, and press the tongue down below all of the instrument, for this is the form; and let it be of silver or thin iron like a knife: 
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	You press the tongue to the entire instrument, and you see the abscess, then take the needle and place it in the almond, and thrust it upwards as much as you can; and do no thing with the cloths, then cut with the instrument, for this is the form, that seems a force; and however the head are curved, and one side to the other, and are very sharp, and is made of iron or lead:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you don't have this instrument present, then cut it with pliers, for this is the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And be sharp on one side and the other side no; and when you have cut one of the almonds, cut the other according to the same manner, and after the incision gargle the patient with hot water, and water and thus, and if a discharge of blood happens, gargle the patient with water, or peels of pomegranates that are cooked, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the blood is stopped; then care for it until it is healed; and at any time abscesses are born in the throat other than the two almonds, cut them therefore like the two almonds.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman of an abscess that was inside her throat, that is to say the abscess of little size; and I had well nearly closed all the throat, so that the woman could not expire through the passage which was obstructed, and could neither eat nor drink, and would be dead if she remained thus one or two days. 
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so high raised that it had been put two reigns by the two openings of the nose.  
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I had therefore immediately, and placed one in the one incision, then I drove the tool out, and into a large portion of bowel; then I refilled the other part in the other puncture of the two, and worked the mouth and pressed the tongue; after I placed the instrument in these abscesses, and scraped a part, and there came out only a little blood; and thus was opened the duct of the throat to the woman, and began now to drink water and then wine, and did not cease to cut this abscess for a long time; and the abscess grew again, and filled the place that I had emptied, until it became very large; then I enclosed it and cauterized it within the throat: thus it remained without growing; and I left those parts, and know only what God did with him after me. 
de l’uve	of the grape
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the shape of the grape is described, and it is plump and long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is rather large and round, it is called "grape". 
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not benefit, and you see that the pus of the abscess is calmed, and it is subtle, then it is necessary that you cut it; and the one which is round assembled and is not long; and it is sanguine or of red color or black, then it is necessary that you drain the incision of it. 
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great peril for the patient.  
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	It is therefore necessary, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, by its whiteness and its length, that you make the patient sit in front of the sun, and press the tongue with the instrument which we have made remembrance of before; then place the needle in the grape, and draw it out, and cut with the one of the two instruments that I have said in the incision of the two almonds.  
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is necessary that you do not cut more than the superfluity which is beyond the natural limit; for if you cut more, it grieves to the voice, and to speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the II almonds, and cure until it is healed. 
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear of being cut, then it is necessary that you use an instrument to the cauterization of the senses of fear. 
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cautery is sharp acute. 
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And it is that the patient puts his head on your healthy hand, and then presses the tongue to the instrument that we have said or chapter of cautery, and confides with a sharp live sock, so that it is not too thick nor too clear; and in employing the end of this instrument, for this is the form: 
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And have or chief a hair where one puts the medicine, like the handle of a spoon, and put the instrument on all the medicine over the grape; and let the patient be lying on his side, so that the saliva and the muscle move from his mouth of the medicine inside, so that it does not descend to the throat, and the windpipe; then hold your hand on all the medicine and press it onto the grape, the quantity of half an hour, until you see it burn and the mordications of the medicine be calmed; and if you see, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and put the instrument with all the cotton into the channel above, until the cotton hardens on the grape; and do this often, until the cauterization is perfect, then leave it to dry, and wait after four or five days. And if you have need to recommence the cauterization of the medicine, then commence it again, and after the cauterization wipe around the grape, with cotton dipped in butter, and purify that which is around the medicine; and be washed with cold water, and be cured with gargles until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision, unless the cautery; if it is cured by fumigation according to this manner, take calament and ysop and origanum and rue and camomille and avronne and similar herbs, and assemble them all or any of them in 1 pot, and put it inside, and make boil; and the pot should be well glued with strong earth, and inside the pot have 1 instrument made according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And be it of silver or of iron, and be the one of the shoulders put into the mouth of the patient until the vapor mounts to the eye through the vein, as long as the eye is mortified; after, it often recommences, until the eye dries, and keep that you do not make this at the beginning of the arrival of the hot abscess, for many things happen; and do not make this except at the decline of the hot abscess. 
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, then take a dog and put in its head a crust of egg, so that the mouth of the patient does not become too hot; for the crust of egg does not let the vapor burden the mouth, and it is a good cure altogether health. 
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times a bone or spine of fish or any thing is lodged in the throat; so it behooves you therefore to draw out what you can see, and press the tongue to the sun with all the instrument, so that you see move the thing; and what does not appear to you and is returned into the throat, it behooves you to make the sick person vomit until the meat is cooked in the stomach; by adventure if it will withdraw the thing by vomiting; or the sick person swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a root of lettuce, or 1 morsel of dry bread; and tie to the sponge 1 thread, and then swallow it; and when it will come to the place, it will be lodged, and then you will draw out further; and if it does not come out by what we have said, take 1 instrument of wood according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instruments be curved at the head so that it may more easily enter into the throat, and have the head held high lifted; and beware that you do not touch the epiglottis, that all does not come to life, nor push in the bone within; and it is better that the patient pushes the instrument, for because he feels where the thing is hoarse; so he pushes down, or he draws it out with all the instrument equally, as long as it is far.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the throat's cut
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	At no time is medicine used to the bleeding wound, as I have said in the division, by the cure of medicines; and when these do not help, then look in the throat of the patient in the sun, then you press the tongue with the instrument that I have told you. 
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the hemorrhage, treat it with every small pincers, or subtle forceps that are fit for this. 
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if this does not work, then take a cat's head, and put it in the throat of the sick person, then put where the neck of the cat is hot iron, and do this often. 
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient has water every day.  
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take full I vessel of cold water, and operate the mouth, and put it in without swallowing, and move it with your hand often; and as soon as the patient feels the water, he will fall. 
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not fall as we have said, then fumigate the patient with asafoetida, with the instrument that I have said in the fumigation of the grape; do this many times, for it will come down without tarrying. 
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the manner of fumigation is this that you take a pot where there are burning coals, and let it be covered with a covercloth pierced in the middle, and in that one is put the head of the instrument; then you throw your fumigation, and the patient puts the head of the cane in his mouth, and closes his mouth so that the smoke does not come out, but comes up to the throat; and the throat will now flow, and if it does not flow, then you begin again fumigation many times; and suffer the patient thirst, and eat salty things and others, and do not drink water; and then it is necessary for it to flow by this government.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument with which one treats the throat is, when it can be seen, similar to tongs bent so as to enter into the throat; and it has the appearance of a bird's beak, and it has sharpness from lime, so that what it takes, it cannot leave; and see here the form:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapter on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Many resemblances of abscesses are, according to those that remembrance comes after in this book, and they differ in perforation and size; and it is in two ways, one being in its own likeness, and the other from moisture it holds.  
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second manner is for those eyes which are on the body.  
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscess of the head is different from that of the base, and the abscess of the fleshy part is different from that which comes in the joints, and each has its judgment in the work.  
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if to abscesses one must not pierce until the bow is mature according to its completion; and if to such ones it is proper to pierce when they are crusted, and do not die according to their completion, as abscesses which are near joints.  
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come near joints, and it is left until it is fully rotten, by chance the ligaments and nerves of the joint are corrupted, which is the cause of contraction in that limb.  
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	Ou the abscess is near the principal limb, and if you delay the perforation until it is ripe, it will harm the principal limb; or if it is near the foundation, pierce it so that it is ripe; and it is not fitting that you pierce an abscess crudely without complete digestion, except for the one which is near the foundation, lest it burrow inward, become elongated, and a fistula come forth; and may not heal in a great time.  
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary that you know the time of piercing the abscess which is ripe according to its completion, and that is when the pain is appeased, and the fever subsides, and the lessening of the pain and the redness, and of the swelling and the softening of the head of the abscess, and the other signs; and it is necessary that you make the piercing where it is most dependent from the abscess, and where it opens outwards; and be the piercing long in the body, and if the abscess is on the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all places equal where there is no crease.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In these that fall, according to which limb. 
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in a fleshy place, it is better that you let the perforation remain until it is confirmed in complete digestion, as we have said. 
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	Because if you pierce him in front of these, the body from his sperm will be elongated and it is full of much filth; and perhaps harden the lips and the depths of him. 
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if to any abscess that are pierced according to the breadth of the body, according to what the members need.  
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And you must make in small abscesses, small openings; and in large abscesses, large openings, and many cuts according to the appearance of the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses where it is necessary to carve out the core, and cover; when it has become as I drapes, and is withered, then you must do as with buboes: and if there are such that are cut in III angles, and if there are such that are cut like the leaf of myrtle, like abscesses of the angles; and if there are such where one makes a round size, and other sizes and similar cuts. 
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	He who has no head, such as a superficial abscess, it behooves you to pierce him through; and when the abscess is large, and it has gathered much pus, and you pierce it, do not drain all the pus in that hour, but drain one part; then plug up the abscess until the next day, then drain nothing directly; do this many times, little by little, until the pus is gone altogether; same if the patient is of weak virtue, or a woman bearing, or small child, or old man decrepit. 
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the spirit sometimes jumps out with the exit of the bowels, which by chance kills the patient, and you don't worry about it.  
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid therefore this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, wipe the wound, and see if the wound of the abscess is small; and if it is a flat cut, administer bands of linen or old cotton; and if it is a large abscess, and there are many openings, then it is necessary that you put in each one a bandage so that it comes against the other; and if you have struck into the abscess part of the skin, and you have raised it around, then it is necessary that you fill it with old cotton or lint scraped from linen without moisture, and tie it until the third day; then bone, and cure with ointment until it is healed. 
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if bleeding occurs in your work, so administer cold water and oil, and wet the bandage, and place it on the bleeding area many times. 
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the flow of blood persists, administer governance and care, and the powders that I have said in this book, and if it is in winter's time, and the lesion or abscess is very nervous, then it is necessary that you put upon it tents and cloths moistened in wine and hot oil; and if it is in summer, and the lesion is fleshy, then it is necessary that you put upon it cloths moistened in water and oil, or in cold wine and oil, until the third day, as we have said; and then unbind the abscess, and wipe it, and cure it, as it is fitting, until it is healed.  
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this it is necessary to know universally in the treatments of abscesses: for I have told you how one must go before the treatments of abscesses, and see here the chapter.
des soros	of sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	When there comes pus from the head and they are in manners of ours that are in nets, like the joints of a chain, and many such similarities.  
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are some that are fatty and such that have moisture as well as pulses; and there are some that are hard and stony at the waist, and there is no doubt if the artery does not oppose it. 
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the works of the waist are that you prove to all instrument which is called « entromissoire », of which its form comes after, what thing it contains. 
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, let it be covered from above with something long. 
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is dried, one should scrape it without leaving the hair that contains the moisture, for it returns as soon as one leaves it; then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is present; if not, in water and salt, and apply it to the wound, and leave it until the next day; and remove those which are left of the night. 
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then begin the cotton again, as before, on the second day, and the third, until you know for certain that it does not remain in the wound; then treat the wound with ointment as appropriate, until it is healed. 
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess holds in the fat, then cut it according to this form, long; and lay your forceps on it, and flay it from all sides, and put all your care into drawing out the pus where it lies; and if the artery does you contrary, then do what I told you after.  
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also do for the abscess if it is suppurating, and as to cutting and curing as I have told you.  
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the incision on the purulent abscess and the moist one is lighter, because they are of little blood. 
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if to some of these abscesses or chiefs where there is no moisture, and of these fut I abscesses that I copied or chief of an old woman; and found the abscess as a hard stone, rough and white, and cannot break; and if one had broken any, one would have done it as well as a wound.  
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses coming or chief, it is that those who come to the chief of children and at the roots of the ears, the opening should be always at the lowest point, so that pus may flow out; and care as it is appropriate. 
des scrophules	of scrofulas
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times these abscesses happen in the neck, and under the arms, and in the groin, and sometimes come from other places or parts of the body, and are bad, and are joined together.  
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrophule is properly within its side, like the nut and the abscess of the head, as we have said; and the appearances of these scrophules are many. 
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and if there are bad ones who do not want to obey health. 
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In that therefore you see of good disposition at the touching, and is seeming to the color of the body, and moves of each part and is not harmed as nerves of the neck nor to the artery nor to the conduit, and is not too deep; so it is fitting that you cut it from above, and the scabs from each part, and let the two lips of the heart be in one, if you have need of it, as we have said in abscesses of the head; and the treat piece by piece, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve nor the vein, and not be too spatula thick nor trenching, that the hand does not escape, and do not see too far ahead, that you do not cut what you should not. 
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or artery, and it does not allow you to work, put in the wound powdered vitriol, or any powders that restrain blood, and restrain the wound; and leave it until the abscesses are appeased, and the wound is softened, and begins to rot.  
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the wound is cleansed, return to your work, until you accomplish it; then examine with your index finger if there are any small pustules, and cut them and remove them. 
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a great vein at the root of the scrophule, it is not fitting that you cut that scrophule at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread, and let it hang by it, without annoyance; then apply the wound of old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then cure. 
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut all the scrofula, it is necessary that you assemble the two lips of the wound, and sew them now, then there is no more superfluity for the size of the scrofula. 
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	If it is necessary that you understand to cover the root of it, and draw out pus, and apply the cloth as we have said.  
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scrophules that hold superfluity, pierce there where it opens more; and pierce it as that before said, depending, then administer bandages with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what is remaining of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, apply the ointment cure to form flesh, until it is healed. 
de squinance	of scrofula
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients said and spoke of the cutting of the throat; but I never saw in our land who did it, and this is the writing of their word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	To those who have squinance, it is necessary that the opening of the throat which is called “epiglottis” be cut; and one does not help with those, because all the veins and the prominences of the patient are at those who have abscesses hot in the mouth, or in the throat, or in 2 almonds.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the illness is in the channel of the prominence, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid the destruction that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It is therefore necessary when we want to cut the epiglottis, that we cut it below III circles or IV a small fissure through the, between II circles or by the quantity of the fissure of the syfac, not in the cartilage; and these are so suitable for the section of the epiglottis that there is no flesh, and the vessels are long of it.  
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is fearful, it is necessary that he stretch the skin of the throat to the whole neck, then fends the throat until it comes to the windpipe; and escape the vessels of blood, if you see anything, and then cut the syfac, as we have said; and demonstrate by the section of the phlegm of the windpipe which jumps out from the place that is broken, and by the lack of voice; and leave the wound open a piece. 
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour is passed for which one doubts strangulation, assemble the .ij. lips of the wound of the heart, and sew together alone sense the cartilage; then administer medicines that make flesh grow, until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim says that one does not do this juice until the throat is completely choked, and the patient is judged to death, and the fault the lung.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Therefore, cover the epiglottis so that the patient cannot breathe and they breathe through the wound, and thus are kept from death; and for this, ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the evil of the disease has passed, and it has passed in three days or four. And then they commanded to sew the wound and cure it, until it was cured; and I will tell you what I saw. 
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a young lady took a knife and stuck it in her throat, and cut part of the channels of the windpipe; and I was called to cure her, and I found her as dead. 
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the blood that was issuing from it, and well that it had not wounded a vein nor been led except by the throat, and the veins were exiting through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I bandaged it, and thus I treated the wound, until it was healed; and nothing happened to the maiden except that she was hoarse of voice, and returned afterwards to her disposition; therefore I say that in cutting into the epiglottis there should be no fear. 
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called "throat hernia", and it is a large abscess in the color of a vein, and it is mostly in women; and there are two ways: natural and accidental; the natural one has no cause. 
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accident is according to II manners, of which one is similar to fat to us, and the other manner is similar to an abscess that comes from our artery; and there is fear, and it does not come together to work of doing outside than in this which is small, and prove it and seek throughout the intruder: if you find it as I say fat, and cannot to any vein, so cut it, as one cuts the fat, and treat it all its head, if there is any; and surround well soon, and cure it as it comes together, until it be perfectly healed. 
des nous	of us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	Many ways there are to us, of which I will say all the appearances; and now it befits that I say all the difference that is between ours and that which is issued. 
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that dislocation is sometimes accompanied by fever and heat, as long as the fever has passed and putrefaction is complete, then rest the fever and heat.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With the new ones there is no heat nor fever nor pain, and contains the substance which is its own sac and is according to the color of the body, and begins also like a blister, and becomes large; and there are according to two appearances, or greasy, or moist, and much of color as I said in the division. 
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the care of the wound, that you feel and inquire first of all the instrument which is called “entromissoire,” according to what its form will be in the chapter that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the manner of the incision of the abscesses from us is that you prick or more moist place than you find in the abscess, and turn your two points and points, until you know that the instrument has pierced the core, then it should be according to the size of the abscess; then extract the introducer, and take care that what will jump.  
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If moisture runs short, whatever color it has, do it as I said about other abscesses; and if after the introducer none comes moisture, know that it is fatty, so do it in a cross, and take it with tweezers, and scrape it lightly on each side and keep the coat where it lies so that you draw it healthy with the outside; and if you can't draw it healthy, then draw it piece by piece so that nothing remains. 
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	If it stays there nothing, it returns to us many times; and if it remains a bit, and the wound does not grieve him, apply powders corrosive acute to the wound, and strain the wound, and put above things soothing plasters hot, and cure of other cures until it is healed; and if the swelling is great, stitch the two lips of the wound, and cure of those who generate flesh. 
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the vein beating is contrary to you or another urgent matter and you apply the place of crushed vitriol, and leave it there for two days or three, as long as the wound weeps, and rests the boiling of blood; then return to covering those that are remaining from the other.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	See here the forms of the introits instruments, and are of III manners: great and middle and small; and there is III squares which are called «albaret», and I which is called «breb», and there is of III manners: great, middle, and small, to surround the abscesses of fistula; and are also like the needles with which one sews the sorcerers, and are of citrine copper, or iron, or silver, and most worthy those that are yellow, and are more proven by black pitch to surround the fissures of fistula; and are of III manners: great, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the breadth of the openings. 
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The forms of the forceps are of many resemblances, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and there are forceps that have II curves of III manners also; and there are forceps that have III curves, and are also of III manners; and there are forceps that have II curves, and forceps of one curve only, and are of III manners; and all these are necessary in their place. 
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The chief of these are trenching tools, and there are some that do not cut more than one way, with which we scrape the flesh, so that one does not wound the vein or nerve; and of these instruments are the lancets reposed in handles, so that the patient does not feel them at the opening of abscesses; and they are of three ways: great, small, and medium, as you see; and one uses them only in flesh places, such as legs, arms, breasts, and groin, and similar places; and sometimes one makes another instrument small, resembling fisticuffs scrapes, according to this form, with which one drains blood. 
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and one puts it never in the place that is healthy to cut open the veins, and arteries, and never around according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to rot, until they appear like breasts of women; and they remain disfigured and swollen, and whoever wants to cure them, should follow this form from this line .b. up to .g.: 
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Then scrape the fat, and apply medicine to the wound, preventing flesh from growing, then assemble the two lips of the wound with a suture, and treat it until it is healed; if the wound grows downward and becomes enlarged as women's do, make two incisions on the ribs above, by two similar incisions; so that one holds onto the other at the end of one and the other, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from this line .b. up to the line .g.; then scrape the skin that is between the two lips, remove the fat, and administer what we have said about stitching and powders, and what is necessary for the treatment, until it is healed; if it is not healed, or the incision is not completely made because the patient does not want to rest, or because of the bleeding, then you should fill the wound with cotton moistened in corrosive ointment; and leave it until it softens the remaining flesh and fat, then treat it until it is healed.
