des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the buttocks
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come under the buttocks are kinds of hard scrofulous nodules that have crusts, and some contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those therefore who contain moisture ought to be cut according to this form, from the line .b. up to the line .g. 
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus that is in the abscess is emptied, then apply to the wound old cotton, and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and treat with ointment as before until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is of the appearance of scrofulas, then make it as we have said in opening scrofulas, and if the wound reenters the fold, then administer cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	Of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is cut and the skin that is above it is sewn together, often abscesses come; and just as much it happens to an inflamed vein and abscess; and if one knows this well for the artery, then the abscess extends longer; and when you feel it with your fingers, you feel tightening; and when it is for the vein, it appears red swollen; and it is foolish to cover this abscess, even when it is under the shoulders and elbows and neck and in many other places, and it is very large.   
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is then necessary to avoid the cure of iron, and the one who is chief must also avoid it, and in the one who is swollen of artery making from above the skin of the long; then work the size as incisions, and depart beautifully the artery from the cloths, until it is uncovered; then put under the one a needle, and make it pierce up to the other side, and restrain the artery with a double thread in II leagues, according to that which I have taught you in the extraction of the II arteries that are in temples; then point the place which is between the II links of an introducer as long as the blood which is there comes out, and be clean the abscess; then administer the cure that generates bowe, until the lien chills; then cure those of ointment coming to these, until it is healed; and if the abscess is for the size of the vein, it is necessary that you tie with your hand what you can of the abscess to all the skin, then put the needle under the place that you hold in your hand, and make it pierce, and have I double thread, so that you pull it from the other side; then tie the abscess, as I have told you, or link of one of II parts as II chies of the thread; and if you doubt that the threads are not coming out, so put another needle to all I thread under all the abscess at the incision of the first needle, and restrain the threads in IIII leagues; then cut the abscess until the superfluities come out, then cut the superfluity of the keur and leave those who are tied; then put on I drapeil moilliet in wine and oil, then administer him cures of tents and ointments until it is healed. 
des apostemes des ners	of the abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Just as abscesses come in the artery and vein, abscesses also come to the nerves when they are bruised, or by too much work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this happens more often in the shoulders and hips and in all their parts where there are joints, and it is the grief of abscesses, and its color seems like the color of the body, and is in many dispositions without pain; and when one restrains it, then the patient feels pain, and it is not well within the body, but below the heart; and moves well from all sides, and does not go forward or backward, nor down nor up, and the one that is in joints should not be covered with iron: for fear it would go contraction; and the one that is on the head or on the forehead, makes the skin to the spatula. 
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, hold it with tongs and cut it at its root; and if it is large, suspend it with a hook, and flay it, then scrape out the pus and sew up the wound, and treat it until it is healed.  
des grosses boces pendans	Of large boils hanging
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	Sometimes it happens in the bellies and nowhere else, and is a disease that is called "fungus" because of its appearance like mushrooms, and the roots are subtle, and the heads are large; and there are some small ones and very large ones; and I saw a man who had two in his belly that were more like mushrooms than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had thin roots, and they were slightly split, and pus flowed out of them.  
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I cut them and found in one XVIII ounces weighing, and in the other VI З., and the works on incision is that you look if the patient is moist, and the color of the artery is white and moist and of subtle root; if it cuts with the spatula wide, and be in your presence the cautery to the fire. 
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For at the hip there come often too great hemorrhages of blood, and if the bleeding does not stop, then hasten to cauterize; and if you see the patient frightened and fearful of the incision of iron, take a thread of linen well made, and tie it with the limb as we have said, and let him wear it for days; and then restrain it, and do not cease restraining the linen thread until it has closed the limb, and dries by itself without labor; and if the roots are large, be afraid to cut all at once for fear of the belly, but you can well cut half, then cauterize it so that it does not re-open; then cure the wound, and keep that you do not cut the thread which is of pale color and of poor sense and of milk.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is an ulcerated abscess, and I will come to the cure of ulcers after this.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the wound has become
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the boil comes from cautery of a wound or fissure of the skin, and is on the belly and in some of the boils, as they happen in other sores, or of blood that comes from veins or arteries according to what is before, or of windiness; and if it is from the rupture of the skin and the exit of the boil, then the color of the abscess appears similar to the color of the body, and it is a light thing without pain, and open with diverse issues. 
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is because of the exit of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when one presses it at its edges, it rebounds, and then returns, and perhaps it is tightened, and increases greatly at the entrance of the bath and for strong labor.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is for moisture, it is a light thing, and open well when you press it with your hand, do not constrain it; and if it is for blood, it opens by these signs the abscesses thick and hard, and are fixed according to a quantity; and if it is for windiness, it is soft to the touch, and the work is that you see whether its appearance is for the blood of the artery, or of the vein, or windiness. 
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	So you must leave the cure. 
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear in it, as I have told you in the chapter of abscesses, for the artery and for the vein. 
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if the appearance is for the intestine or the boil, then it behooves you to command the patient to hold his arm, and be outstretched straight, then seize all around the boil; then command him to grasp firmly between your hands, then go around the place that you have marked with the spatula, then extend half of the abscess above to the entire incision; then tie it around with a strong thread, or a strong silk cord firmly, and let it be bound well; then work the half of the abscess extended on the ligature, and put your index finger, and feel the intestine; if you find it caught by the ligature, then untie it, and put the intestine out from the inside of the belly; and if you find the boil, then take it at the incision, and cut away the superfluity; and if the artery opposes you, or the vein, then go well around, then return to your work and take II needles, and put II threads through them, and put the II needles around what you have made in a cross that you make perceptible; then strain the abscess in IV places on the needles, and if you see it, remove the needles, and leave the place as long as it will ripen, and let the dead matter discharge by itself; or you cut it when it is subtle and ripened, then cure it as it is necessary, and cover the abscess as we have said; and extract the blood or moisture that you find, then cure the place as is necessary, and close the place. 
dou chancre	of the ulcer
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division the likenesses of ulcers, and how one must work on them by medicines, and how one must shun the cure of iron; and let us say the ulcer is born in the marrow, and great caution to be had in its cure, and they said the ancients that when an ulcer is in a place where one can shave it like an ulcer which is in the nipples, and in the groin, and similar places, and one must remove it entirely when it is at the beginning; and when it is large and old, it is not fitting that you approach it, for I have never been able to cure any of them; nor has anyone else ever cured any before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the work, when it is in a place where one can remove it, as we have said, is that you purge the patient once of black bile; then let him bleed if he has a manifest repletion, then make the patient .i. a good place to do the work; then cut your incisions or ulcers, and shave the hair on all sides, and the bone on all sides leaving nothing; and let the blood flow freely, and press well the place with your hand or any thing, and if the running of blood goes contrary to the incision of the artery or vein, then cauterize it until the blood is stanched; then cure it further until it is healed.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have said in the division the similarities of dropsy, and in what manner the assembly of water is made, and the signs of each similarity, and the cure that is made by medicines, and that which is cured by iron; thus it is illuminated only; and one must not touch iron in these two similarities: that is to say, tympanites and hyposarche, because it is a mortal thing; therefore when you medicate this likeness of dropsy that is called "illuminated" with medicines, and the cure does not benefit, look at whether the patient is weak, or if he has another illness besides dropsy, such as coughs and flux of the belly and similar things; if one does not touch iron, because there is doubt; and if you see the patient of strong virtue, and he has no other illness but dropsy alone, and he is neither too young nor too old, then you must do this: lift the patient straight up on your hands, and the ministers press the belly pushing the water to the lowest part of the hip, then take the spinous spatula according to this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And be trenchant of the two parts. 
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	at the point, and all way that it may not be so deeply inserted that it can come to the intestine when one inserts it; and do not let it bleed; then see if the dropsy is located toward the intestines: If so, you should make an incision below the ribs III on the right; and if the dropsy is due to the liver disease, then make your incision on the left side of the rib III; and if it is due to the spleen, then on the right, and do not let the patient lie on the incision that the superfluities do not flow to that weak place; then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and bring it up, and raise your hand to the entire spatula between the skin and the fascia as much as when you are scraping to the quantity of a fingernail or less; then pierce the fascia until the spatula comes to the vein, and this is the point of the fluid; then draw out the fluid, and insert this instrument from there which is the form:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it is similar to a silver dog, and it is of iron or an archot lighter, and in the part below I have a small hole; and one side costs III holes; and II on the other side, and I on the other; and the head is cut like a pen, and this is the form of the incision with which the scribes cut the pen. 
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	At the top is the alemele, so that when the instrument comes to the point, it descends now on the instrument; empty therefore half or a third part, because if you empty more than it is due in this hour, by chance the patient may die from the resolution of his spirit of the weapon, or he falls faint, or he approaches death; but empty according to the quantity of his virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the virtue of the patient signify, and his pulse; then treat the instrument and hold the point, and it is now held by the heart which stops the opening that is on the syfac, of which I have spoken, that you pierce in this manner; then begin the instrument the other day, if you see the patient suffering that, and treat from the point a little quantity; do this each day, and guard yourself from overflowing until there remains no more than a drop of point. 
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you doubt about the patient, and you give him much water, so cure him with earth or sand hot, and with much sweat or bath and in the sun, and keep him from drinking; and cure him with medicines drying until he is healed, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of the water, as I said before. 
de l’estopement de la verge	of the stopping of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	At no time are children born who do not have a hole in the penis, or the hole is small, or it is not in its place. 
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is necessary, he must immediately perceive to all the spatula very subtly according to this form:  
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Then put or pertu the clo subtil of plonc, and tie it and hold it so III days or IIII and when he wants to make urine, let the clo be removed, and make urine, and then put it back; and by adventure it does not come off at all, for the urine that comes out will not leave it closed.  
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	He whose wound is small, if it is medicated with the cloth of plantain, as we have said, then it will widen.  
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have the penis in their place are pale, because none are born with the penis at the head of the shaft, so they cannot urinate until they raise their penis; and they cannot ejaculate because the matter cannot come to the urethra, and this is a serious illness. 
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the manner of the work is that the patient lies often on his back, then they place the head of the penis and the scrotum as if it were the width of a pen, so that the opening falls in the middle, as it should; and beware of blood loss which comes many times, and if it happens, then the stanch from those who stanch blood, and cure the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	of the pimples of the member
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times come this blemishes in the member, and is an appearance of ugly flesh; and there are malignant and non-malignant ones; so it behooves you to prick them with .i. one sharp needle, and scrape and clean all, then put cotton moistened in Egyptian ointment; then cure with diafinicon ointment until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the ulcer is malignant, of bad color and pus, then you must bring a cautery to it. 
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have grasped it, and if the bandage is in some part within the hair and part without, then it befits that you remove the bandage which is within first; and when it is soldered, then cure the outside. 
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you treat it together, be sure that the head of the shaft is not pierced, and blackening and corruption come in its shaft and where the anus; so it behoves to remove all that is black and corrupt, then put upon it the poultice of honey and flour which is made from the bark of quince trees and chickpeas, then treat it with other treatments until it is healed. 
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if bleeding occurs, administer the lunar cautery according to this form: 
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cautery helps with two conditions together: that is to say, bleeding and corruption; and if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, it is necessary that you insert or lead a chain of wool into the penis, and urinate the patient among; and when the skin is tight at the head of the penis which happens to those who have not been circumcised, or there are wounds or abscesses, then it is necessary that you scrape it with a pointed instrument, until the ligaments are loosened, and the head of the penis is free from all sides; and if it is a painful thing to consider this, it is necessary that you scrape it with the spatula any point at the head of the penis and of the skin; then separate well between the two, and put in the subtle linen cloth moistened in cold water, that it does not tighten again.  
de la circoncision	Of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not like other wounds in terms of healing; however, when we perform this operation by our own will, and properly on children, it is necessary that we make the best work, and the easiest to heal.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not perform circumcision on their children, because they did not use it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have wanted the most part of the masters and the healers who made circumcision about one and a half, and with force, and with a whole novacule; so they cut the skin because there are two skins, and by adventure if one cuts the top and leaves the bottom.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or it is necessary to cut, and the pain is double, and at the purification which is about one and a half, the point of the member is not safe; and at the purification of the angle by adventure escapes the iron, and the work runs, and many times they are born as if they do not need purification and I have wanted it.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	From the purification which is done with force to all the length of thread I have found the goodness of the experiment, because the forces cut justly as well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you press your hand, so that it is equally sized in I [word unclear], but that the filaments are well placed within the skin; and so that the manner of the first work is that you make the child think, if they understand, that you are only making them tie the filament around the rod only, then let them enjoy themselves in every way that you can; then let them be between your hands straight, and place the forces between your hands or under your feet so that the child does not see them, nor any of the instruments; then bring your hand to the rod and blow or heart, and move it upwards until the head of the rod is inside; then cleanse it well of the filth which is assembled there, then tie its place with a double thread, then tie it below I poc to the other lien; and hold it as II do by the second lienure at the pouch and at the index finger, and cut between the II liens, then lift the heart upwards gently and move the head of the rod; then let blood run drop by drop, for that is the cure; and put powder on and over the powder I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit with oile roset boin and fres, and leave it there until the next day, and cure it of other cures until it is healed. 
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the forces to the mundification is this: the two shoulders should be held and be pointed, and the shoulders are also as large as the hands equally.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of the mundification is when the kernels inside are at the incision; therefore it behooves you to extend it to your finger, so that the pus makes an abscess; and cut it equally, and if you cannot hold it with your finger, then you hold it with tongs, and then cut.
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they pierce for three days, and that which is below the shaft is swollen, let it alone until the abscesses are calmed, and lightly scar it; then cut it as much as you can move, and guard yourself from the part of the shaft, it will do it no harm.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cure therefore the place of things suddenly wound with powder, which we have said or treated of powders, and if one cuts the kernel beyond measure, and it goes upwards, it will do no harm; cure it therefore, as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The retention of urine is from the stone, or congealed blood, or bowel, or new flesh, or similar things, which we have said in the division; and if the urine is not released, and you see the retention by the stone which is in the urethra or neck of the bladder, then it is necessary that the patient be bent on his knees; and his feet be placed on his back, and extend his belly from the part above his back, and restrain the patient's legs as much as he can; and then the neck of the bladder is constrained to the expression of the stone above, for which reason the urine is released; and if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then it is necessary that you administer extraction with all the instrument which is called 'syringe', for this is its form: and let it be of fine silver, light-headed, like the feather of a bird; and let the tail be one palm long and a half, and let it be fine at the head. 
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And the manner of the issue of urine is that you take a double thread and tie it to the head I piece of wool or cotton, and put the head of the thread inside the syringe; and cut the superfluity of the wool and put it up to the head of the syringe, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and aubin of egg, and make the patient sit on the seat, and raise the bladder and penis with moist oil and olive oil and warm water; then gently put the syringe into the penis, until it comes to the root of the penis, then double the penis upwards towards the body; then push the syringe forward until the bladder, and feel the patient coming up to the empty thing, and this is not done according to this order for that that which conducts or where it goes is twisted; then keep the thread all wool piece and piece, and the urine follows the wool, then remove it, and make the correction of the urine; and repeat the syringe until the bladder is emptied, and the patient be aligned. 
des maladies de la vessie	Of the bladder illnesses
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When scabs or blood comes in the bladder, or there is rottenness assembled, and you see distilled water and medicines, so do to all the instrument which is called “clepsydre”, and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed, and if it has III openings: II on one side, and I on the other, as you see; and the leus chevez because the medicine is such that it stops the rod well without addition, if one can drain the moisture, and put out when it is necessary; and when you want to place your medicines in the bladder, put the chief dou keusteur in the moisture, and draw with the drawing tube which is inside; if you draw the moisture to the kesteur, and then firmly push back the drawing tube inside; so the moisture will enter inside, and come to the bladder now, so that the patient feels it; and this is the form of the subtle enema by which one enemas the bladder: so it is here.  
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And it is made of silver or lead, and the head is higher; and below to the chest where the linen falls; then take a sheep bladder and put in it the moisture that you see to clysterize the bladder, then tie it between the two breasts forming a good double thread, and warm the part with that moisture on the fire; then insert the end of the clyster into the anus, then strain your hand on the bladder with all the moisture coming out, until the patient feels that that moisture has arrived at the bladder; and if you do not have the bladder, take a piece of parchment, and make it into a circle, and pierce it roundly in the center; then insert the strong thread into these holes, then assemble the circle as one assembles the dal, and put inside what you see of oil and moisture and water, and tie it to the instrument; and do like you have done with the bladder, of pressing with your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder. 
de la piere	of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have just said in the division the ways of stone, and the extraction together with medicines; and I have said the difference between the stone engendered as reins, and all the signs, and in what stone one must work with a cutting tool; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell it to you clearly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is engendered in the bladder often happens more frequently to children, and it is a sign that the water jumps from the bladder similar to water in its subtlety; and it appears with gravel, and irritates the patient's penis, and he feels pain many times, and then urinates; and after many of these jumps the foundations are formed; and it is light the healing of children until they are four years old, and it is very painful in the elderly, and is as moderate for those who are between young and old; and the cure is lighter from those who have a large stone than from those who have a small one.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the cure, it is necessary first to cleanse the patient by clyster, to draw out all the filth which is in the intestines. 
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For he encumbers at times to seek the stone. 
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the feet, and unbuckle and move them down so that the stone descends to the middle of the bladder, and it comes out once from its place; then make him sit between your hands properly, and his hands be below his thighs, so that the bladder is entirely declining downward; then push and touch inside; if you feel the stone in the space, then hasten now to cut above the stone. 
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not fall upon touching all, then moisten your index finger with oil from the left hand, if the patient is a child, or your middle finger, if the patient is an adolescent; and put it in its base, and feel the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, move it to the neck of the bladder; then press upwards with your finger, and put it out towards where you want to cut. 
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the minister to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to extend with his right hand the scrotum upwards, and with his left hand remove the skin which is below the scrotum in the area where the incision is made; then insert the spatula cutting downwards, for this is its form:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And place between those who are between the buttocks and the base, not in the middle but at the side of the left hip; and be right on top of the stone, and your two sides should be either base or foundation, and let the waist be like a cross so that it is wide outside, and inside narrow, according to the quantity of the stone, not too large; by chance the press so the two that are base or foundation, that it jumps out without work; and know that there is such a stone where it has angles, and margins: so it is hard to insert; and if it is like those that are below, resembling a gland, and round, whose exit is light.  
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	To this one then where it has angles and margins, make the size larger; and if it does not jump, it is necessary that you extract it with pliers which are also like a file at the head, in order to force extract the stone so that it does not escape; or you put underneath it the subtle curved instrument at the head; and if you cannot manage it thus, then enlarge the hole of the wound, and if there is no cutting, strain it with vitriol; and if there are more than one stones, put the largest first at the neck of the bladder, then cut above, then the trail further, and the smaller ones afterwards if there are more.  
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, it must be sown, and make a greater wound. 
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For two things happen to the patient: either he dies, or the urine comes back through where the leys cannot sew; but nonetheless force yourself to pull it out, or to break it with pliers, until you pull it in pieces; and when you have completed your work, apply to the wound incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and bind it, and put on top a bandage moistened in oil and wine, or in rose water and cold water, to soothe the hot abscess; then set the patient back on his neck, and do not untie the band until the third day.  
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you untie it, wash the area well with oil and water, then treat it with ointment of diaphana and basil oil, until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if abscesses come in the wound and corrosion, and blood clot in the bladder, and due to this, the urine is held back, which is known in such a manner that without jumping with the urine: therefore, you must put in the wound, and extract that blood, because if it remains, it will corrode the bladder, and burn it; then raise the wound of water and ease and silk, and help him in all the ways that you know, until he is healed; and it behooves that all the hours that you cure him, that you bind his two thighs, and assemble the medicines on the place. 
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small, and it is in the urethra, and stuck there, and urine cannot issue; so the cure of this that I say thus, that you may cut it many times, and excuse the cutting by this cure. 
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already tested this thusly. 
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take one piece of iron according to this form and have it shaped into three angles on a stick:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take a thread and tie it around the shaft below the stone, so that it cannot come back into the bladder; then put the forefinger into the shaft lightly, until it reaches the stone; and turn the finger in the stone, poke and poke, until you can feel the stone on the other side; soon the urine will come, then press your hand on what remains of the stone which is inside the shaft. 
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is then broken and thrown out with the urine, and the patient heals; and if you cannot do this for any reason that prevents it, then tie one thread below the stone and the other above, then make the rod right on the stone between the two threads, then pull it out, and untie the thread, and cleanse the congealed blood that is in the wound; and treat it until it is healed. 
de la piere des femmes	of the stone of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It happens that a stone is engendered in women, and if it happens at any time, it is a grievous cure, and is forbidden for three things: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a woman well knowing who discovers herself to the midwives, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third manner is that by chance one cannot find a woman well knowing in this art of hands; and the fourth manner is that the stone of the woman is more deep than the stone of the man, for which it is necessary to make a deeper cut, and great fear there is. And if necessity demands this, it is necessary that you take a midwife well knowing, and with pains one finds her, and if you do not find one, point so much as to cast mire subtly; and present him with a wise woman in the life of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and command her to do what you command of the inquiry of the stone; and look well that the woman is a virgin: therefore it is necessary to put her buttocks or foundation and seek the stone; and if she finds it, she confines it below her buttocks, and recommends to her that she put her buttocks or with the patient, and seeks and presses her left hand on the bladder forming. 
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she finds it, it is necessary that she moves it from great to small from the entrance of the bladder up to below, until it comes to the root of the thigh; then cut above the stone in the root of the thigh opposite the middle of the buttock, where it is seen to be appeared, and feel the stone in that part; and do not move its two parts above the stone or below, and let the tail be at first small; then put the bottom into the waist, if you feel the stone so close to the wound as long as the stone can possibly go out, and know that many kinds of stones are: namely, small and large and rough and smooth, long and round, and which have veins.  
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	If you know the similarities to know the outcome.  
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the vein holds, put on vitriol ground, and hold it an hour until the vein is hardened; then return to your work, as long as the stone is hard, and have the instruments that I told you in the extraction of the stone for men to help you in your work; and if the vein fails, and it is from the artery that was cut, put the powder on the place and restrain it with strips and bandages, and do not restart those, and leave the stone and do not milk it, lest the patient die; then cure the wound. 
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is appeased, and the wounds are healing, then return to your work as long as the stone is out.
de hernie carnouse	of a fleshy hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Watery ramice is nothing else but an assembly of moisture or white syfac, which is under the skin of the testicles, which contains the egg; and it is called "syfac", and sometimes is properly in the membrane of the egg, if one thinks that it is another egg; and this is the skin of the testicle between the white syfac that we have said; and these do not have any other poc.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this ramice is of weakness that comes to the testicles, and it is expanded that matter.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And sometimes it comes from percussion on the bones, and this moisture has many colors: whether it is declining to jaundice, or it is without red, or black, or aqueous white, and this happens more; and these are the signs to know this assembly, because if it is white as we have said, then the abscess is ripe, I poc long as the figure of an egg, and does not open the bones, because it has moisture all around.  
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if there is moisture in the own cloth, then the abscess is reamed with part of the egg, and for this reason one thinks that it's another yolk; and if the moisture is between the skin of the scrotum and the white silk, then one feels it well; therefore when you want to know the color of the moisture, you expect at all the intropositor quarrel, from which its form is before. 
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to this therefore which comes after the introducer, judge of what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we treat it with iron, it is necessary that the patient be healthy according to his power and the fullness of his body; then he lies on his back, on something a little high, and puts under him many cloths; then sits on his left side, and commands the minister to sit on his right, and extend the rod to one of the two ribs near the heart of the sides; then take the spatula light, and cut the skin of the sides among them until below the armpit, and be your cut straight dividing the skin of the sides up to the white fascia, and the eschar gently according to your power; then pierce the white fascia full of water at the wide opening, and extract all the water, and then put your dressings, and extend the fascia upwards; and do not touch the heart of the ribs, but only the fascia; cut all or in pieces equally the side of it subtly, that if you do not cut it wisely, it will return the water; and if the work has been well done by you, put it back in its place when you have completed the work of the fascia; then assemble the two leaves of the ribs at a seam, then cure it like other wounds, until it is healed. 
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the uvula corrupted by another disease, it is necessary that you tie the vessels that are suspended, fearing the flow of blood; then cut the tonsil to the whole suspension, and remove the uvula, and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if the water is assembled in two parts together, know that these are two branches; so cut the other part as you did the first evenly, then wipe away the blood, and put in the wound linen swab half soaked in rose oil; and put outside another linen swab half soaked in wine and oil, and put above the two pads, and put a doubled cloth on top, and tie it above the whole band according to this form: 
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two cloths, and use them of wool batting according to this appearance and be assembled by stitching in the groin of the breeches, and one of the heads pinches above the foundation to the back, and the other at the part of the armpit; and the other of the chief above the two angles, and let all be assembled the restraint in the buckle of the brazier; and sometimes is medicine this ramification of cautery in place of a blade of iron, and it is that you pinch the knife cauterization subtle, and cut the skin of the testicles, and be heated as we have said, so that the white substance that contains the water is uncovered; then take the cautery according to this form, and pierce that substance at once, and scorch it with this subtle cautery hot: 
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And the cut in all ways that you can, as long as you reach everything; and keep that the fire does not touch the eye; and know that this work is more safe; and move guardians of bleeding, and moves that the works of size; and if nothing does to you contrary, or abscesses or bleeding or other thing, so cure what does you contrary, according to what is before said.  
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the patient is fearful and does not want to endure this work because of its horror, so administer a perforation as I told you, and it is that when you are well certain by the meanings that we have said that watery root is there, then make the patient sit on a raised seat; then pierce the abscess in the part below throughout all the spatula wide, and put the perforation through the length of the body; and let the opening be wide so that all the water flows out; then put cotton on the place, and bind it, and leave to drain the remaining water, then cure it until the wound is healed; and if the white cloth does not allow the water to flow out of the mouth of the wound, then you must put a pen or instrument with which one treats the water of the hydrophics, of which the form is mentioned above; and enlarge the hole of the wound, and know that the water returns, and it assembles after six months or until then, and when it is assembled like before, then the patient will pass his days. 
de l’aposteme des coions	Of the abscesses of the testicles
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	Know that in the cutting of this branch there is fear in many positions, so it seems to me that one should leave it; and I will tell you the work and appearances of the abscess. 
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say therefore that many abscesses come from the body, and even the buttocks; and this is by much cause.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	This is to know by superfluity sour and acute, which is spread to the veins, or from percussion; and is the color of the abscess according to the color of the body; and finds no pain, and is a grievous abscess; and by adventure are some abscesses grievous fearful and stony, and of dark color, and sometimes comes from our artery, or from inflammation of vein.  
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When this is by an artery, it is known by the disposition of a hot abscess, when you press it with your fingers; and it does not behoove that you touch it. 
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	He who is made of the inflation of vein is known by his disposition to the expression of touch of the two, and one can well make the cut on this resemblance, and on the other chariots; and that you chop the heart of the coins, then the egg is on top, and the train is further from the white so much, and deliver the suspender from all parts of the egg.  
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the egg is already cooked with these new vessels, then it behooves you to draw out the egg and its yolk; and if it is stuck in the stomach or in what is within the vessels, then it behooves you to deliver that entire membrane, and roundly cut it. 
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the bone is or its rear, then it behooves you to cut it all and extract the egg, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your works are accomplished, then apply the wound with wool moistened in rose oil and wine, then cure it with other cures until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	Of the abscesses of the testicles
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess wrapped in a covering resembling a  sponge, with the softening of the boils, and the patient moves gruffly when he goes; and the cure of this disease is as scary as before, and nonetheless we will tell you the work of it, according to what the ancients did. 
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	It is necessary that you make the patient sit on the elevated seat, then put the suspensory of the loins down to your thighs, at all the vessels which are near the penis, and the masters tie them, and stretch them; then cut with the sharp spatula wide through the middle of the vessels, until they are uncovered, and then scrape from each side, as we have said in the extraction of the arteries that are in the temples; then put a needle where there is the double thread, and tie it to the first place where the vein has come, and tie it straight to the other end; then cut them in the middle directly, according to the length of the body, and drain the corrupted moistors; then cure the wound as the others where one incurs a bow, so that no vessel drips which nourishes one of the loins; for by this there comes no evil, and if to all the vessels comes blood, it is necessary to drain the loins to all the vessels; so that the members do not lose their nourishment because of the incision of the vessels, and dry up and cannot be helped.  
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the hip
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The events of this branch are by the section that comes or there it is extended on the belly in the part of the angles, for that the intestines descend from that rupture to one of the corners; and this rupture is either where the hernia is, or from the extension of it, and come these two ways of bad of causes: or percussion, or jump, or brays, or lifting of heavy weights, and by similar things; and the signs when it is the extension of the hernia are that it happens slowly and slowly, and does not come suddenly; and is the abscess even up to the navel, for that the hernia presses on the intestines. 
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.
