And the signs are when this is of the section of the gut, that it brings at the beginning sudden pain, and the abscess appears diverse, beneath the skin close, and this because of the issue of the intestine and the body to the outside of the gut.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the bowels with the intestine, and are held in, and causes great pain to suffer to the patient, even when it is pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these cures of iron there is fear, for that reason it behooves to avoid them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And the manner of the work is that you command the patient to bring the intestine into his hand inside the wound, if he can enter it; then support it on his neck between your hands, and lift the hips; then hold the heart above, and cut all the skin of the groin from the long side; then put inside the folds of the waist spines according to what you need to open the wound, and such that blood may issue; then scrape the subcutaneous fat which is under the skin of the groin, until the white fat is uncovered on all sides; then put your index finger into that which follows the groin, into that which is between the white fat which is under the skin of the abdomen, and between the second fat, and depart from what is behind the abdomen, and between the second fat; and then move with your right hand inside the heart of the groin, and hold the white fat on top to your left hand, and lift the abdomen towards the waist; and command the minister that he extend the abdomen upwards, and untie what is behind the ligament; and examine with your fingers if there is any intestine wrapped or white fat hard, and if you find any of these things, put it back into the belly; then take a needle which has a large thread made of X threads, and put it in the back part of the fat, which is after the skin of the groin; after the waist, then cut the chies that appear from the threads, until there are IIII threads; then assemble them one above the other in the manner of a cross, and tie the fat, about which we have said that it is under the skin of the groin, with a strong thread of II parts; then wrap the chies of the threads, and tie them together in II parts, so that none of the vessels that nourish them can enter inwards, except an abscess may come; and put the thread straight according to the first long thread II fingers of it, and after these II threads leave the fat which is under the heart of the groin the size of a finger; and after all the others according to the roundness that the egg carries; then cut in the part which is under the skin of the groin, as much as the sinew, and the bowel, as we have said before; then put moistened wool in oil, and put it into the wound, and put the thread that we have said.  
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And at no time is cauterized the white buttocks that we have said, after the incision, out of fear of excessive blood loss.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this happens many times, and let the linen be left until it dries; and if it delays in drying, so it is rinsed with hot water, and put up as we have said, until it dries; then cure the wound with other cures, until it is perfectly healed.  
de hernie carnouse	of a fleshy hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this branch I never saw anyone who dared to do the cure with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients said that it is made like the branch which is assembled with the vis, in such a manner that you tie the vessels, after the cut above or lightly below; then cut in the middle, and cure the abscess of him who operates, until the vessels bleed; and cure it as we have said, until it is healed. 
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	At no time comes rupture in the intestines, as we have said, and opens the lesions; and do not insert any of the intestines into the openings, and if there are inserted, it is little, and repairs all hours; and yet, if it remains too long in this point, it grows the wound or syphilis, until the intestine is inserted; and this happens because of the extension of the syphilis that is in the intestines, as we have said, for it is extended, then softened and inflated the lesions and open; and the cure is by cautery, as we have said before; and at no time is cured by iron in this manner: and is that the patient lies sideways on his back between your hands, then cut the lesion of the rupture inflated with the width according to the quantity of III fingers; and then extract the syphilis which is under the skin that it has, then take the rait and put it on the place apparent of the syphilis; and press it to the bottom of the belly, then sew the II lesions appearing of the syphilis above the head of the rait, and sew one and the other; then extract the head of the rait, and do not cut any of the syphilis nor extend the weft or anything else, as I have told you in the cure of the ramice of the intestines; then cure by the cure of the wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the threads, purify and care for the wound, until it is healed. 
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The sfaca is constrained, and has no appearance in the break, and the cautery is moved in this place, and closer to salvation.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the testicles
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the testicles is softened in some men, because the sacs that are inside are softened, and it is visible; and it is necessary, when one wants to cure it, one makes the patient lie on his back, and he cuts the skin that is softened on the natural skin; then assemble the two lips to a seam, and if you see, sew first the superfluity of the softened skin at three or four stitches firmly; then cut between the seams, and treat the cure as other wounds, until it is healed, and remove the thread.
dou chastrement	of the confinement
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	Know that cauterizations are common in our law, and for this reason it would please me not to speak of them in this book; and it is necessary only for two reasons: one of which is that the doctors should be able to answer when they are asked, and know the cure; and the other because we often need cauterization of some animals to help us, such as goats and sheep and calves and other animals. 
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I therefore say that cauterization is done in two ways: either by attraction or by incision. 
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In that which we do by attraction, let us seat the beast in hot water, until the joints are softened and pliable; then grasp them with your hand, so long as they are set and you no longer feel them. 
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Of the chastisement of the tail: it is necessary that you hold the beast, and press its skin of the buttocks with your left hand, then tie the suspensory, and cut above each orifice in a cut, when you will have well scorched them; and leave no prick of the syfac and the subtle syfac which is on the vessels; and this manner of chastisement is more effective than that which is done by attraction, because in attraction it happens sometimes that nothing remains of the buttocks, because the beast desires lust; then care for the wound until it is healed. 
des hermofrodites	Of the hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermaphroditism is according to two manners as men: the one if it is between the two genitals opens as the figure of nature of a woman, or it has hair, and sometimes in short it urinates.  
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other manner is in women, and above the dagger also as a staff and they couple.  
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the treatment of man and woman is that you cover all the stitched wounds, and cure them like other wounds; in the second manner, for men whose urine leaks through the skin of the scrotum, there is no cure. 
de la tentigene	Of the tenting
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	A wart is a bump raised on the natural part, as long as it is too ugly to see; and some women have them as big as a hand, and that is the cure. 
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	It is necessary that you remove the superfluity of the wound with your hand or fingers, and gently cleanse it; and do not scrape too vigorously, lest bleeding occur, then cure it with other remedies until it is healed; and on another sore that arises at the mouth of the ear, and the temple, and by chance jumps out, and is according to the likeness of a cow, and for this reason they called it in ancient times "cow disease." 
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If it is necessary that you cut it, as we have said the tendon, and care for it until it is healed.  
de erratique	of erratic
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	Erratic it is when the nature of the woman is not perceived, or the opening is small; and is natural by birth, or accidents by disease that has come to it; or it is by a charmed thing, or by subtle or thick syfac, and is made in the mars, or in the ribs, or under, or wherever; and defents the conception, and the childbirth, and by adventure the flowers to have; and the knowledge of this one is by the gaze of the belly.  
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the stopping is near appearing, so whether to your two or the thigh. 
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is dou syfac subtle, and it is near the II books, then hurry, and do this: put your II thumbs together, and the woman be on her back, with her legs spread apart; then hold the II books, so that the subtle syfac be round, and cover the openings; then take wool, and moisten it in oil, and put it on the place, and lie the woman down so that she cannot move. 
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the sty is hard and thick, then it is necessary that you cut it with a spatula resembling a myrtle leaf. 
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the stoppage is of flesh, then suspend it with a cord and cover it; and take medicines to staunch blood, such as dragon's blood, incense, along with honey of egg; then administer a poultice of broad plantain, so that the wound may not close; and thus be prolonged, and administer a linen tent, dry. Then be cured with other cures until it is healed. 
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when in the marsh comes a new birth, it should be covered according to this manner, if it is not boils that are festering.  
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For an abscess which is on the mare, one must not touch with fire. 
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that without custom, and when hemorrhoids are old they become hardened; and we have said in the division the resemblances of them, and the signs, and I will say here those which resolve cure.  
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and the piles, when they are driven into the flesh, and they do not appear to the touch, except by the cure with iron. 
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those who are at the mouth of the marsh, one can feel them, those one can cure. 
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	It is therefore necessary that you put the woman in a cold house, then is the altar held by pliers, and the head cut at its roots, then powder of restraining medicines such as acaice and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then put her feet to the wall for an hour, then put her in cold water; and if bleeding occurs, make her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate bark and gall and similar things, and then take barley flour, and she confides with honey and ease, and with it I make a plaster on her back. 
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it stays still, it is good. 
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If this is not the case, then apply suction cups to the back and breasts without hurting; then take linen, and moisten it in juice of plantain or juice of elderberry with old wine, and apply it to the place.  
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess rests, care for its place with ointment until it is healed; and the one called "albathir" is red, and is similar to the sharp chief, so it must be covered as I said in the previous text; and then the cure until it is healed.  
des apostemes de la marris	Abscesses of the margin
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many manners of abscess come in the marshes, such as chancres and fiery abscesses and herpes and estiomes and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscesses, and more other diseases that I have said in the division. 
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is therefore necessary for me to say in this treatise the hot abscess that comes in the marshes, which is not like abscesses that boil; and if you want to know the work of fire, look at whether the abscess is warm at the beginning of its coming, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red if you can see it. 
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Therefore do not hasten to pierce it, but let him rest until the pain is appeased; and then have the patient sit on a seat, and have small seats where he leans, and support his back and bring together his legs at the parts away from the leg; and let his hips be spread out, and place his arms under his knees, and tie them well with a good linen bandage; then push him towards the right side, and there administer the instrument which is used to work the mouth of the jawbone, for this comes after with the form; and it is necessary that when you see administering this instrument, you insert the point first in order to know the depth of the jawbone, so that what goes into the instrument does not go further than it should, and that it does not damage the patient; and if the instrument is larger, then it is necessary to cover the depth of the jawbone with cloths, so that the instrument does not harm him; and it is necessary that he put the cone of the instrument on top, and that he holds the instrument.  
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess opens, and one makes it soft with their hand, then it is proper to cover it at the chief, at the spatula left; and when the bowel is emptied, then it is proper that you put in the wound tents moistened in rose oil, or in green oil; and put the tent further from the wound to the edge of the marsh, and put over the marsh and over the knife with a clean cotton net moistened in water or mallow are cooked; then cure after II days of ointment coming to this, as long as it is healed; and at no time raise the marsh and the wound by clyster of water and honey, and then water or roots of lilies and lungwort are cooked; then return to the ointment. 
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is set back into the flesh, then it befits you to guard against cauterizing with iron, but treat it as we have said in the division. 
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	The first thing is to the midwife that she knows the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs of it are when you see the woman push down, and desire to smell her rear; then haste the child to be born by force; therefore know that this childbirth is according to the natural figure, and is the head first, and the second with him; and when you see these signs, it is necessary to press lightly on her belly so that the child comes quickly; because when he comes out on his head, then the second one comes with him, and the mother is relieved of her superfluities by good purification; and this which comes otherwise does not come naturally. 
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it comes sometimes upon its feet, and comes to be above the body or shoulder, and the hands, or where it comes upon its belly, or loin, and is turned by chance upon its neck, and by other bad figures; so it is necessary that the healer be wise and subtle in these things, and beware of error and deception, and I will show you all the figures how one should help them. 
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes on its head by natural birth, and the woman giving birth groans loudly, and the strength of her is weak, then have her sit on a saddle, or the women hold her; and anoint her with oil or fenugreek that is cooked, and then put the midwife between her thighs with the little spatula whose form is here:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	and split the secondine, and cut at its nail until the moisture that is inside comes out; and take hold of the belly of the woman until the child descends, and if it does not descend, then it is necessary to give the woman a clyster of fenugreek with sesame oil; then make her take and sneeze from condiment, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: so now will come the child. 
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if the two hands are issued, it is necessary that you put them back gently little by little; and if they cannot enter, then place the woman on the seat, and raise her feet up; then tilt the seat to the ground, and hold onto the woman so that she does not fall during the tilting; and if the hands cannot enter, and the child dies, then cut off the hands at the neck which is before put in, and extract the child, and reset it equally. 
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	of the issue of the child on its feet 
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes upon its feet, it is necessary to push upwards; and then turn it back and forth, until it is equal; then pinch its feet and extend them back and forth. 
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	Let him jump up to his hips, if he is ordered to take, and let him make it sneeze with the condition; if he jumps higher, God willing.  
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it is not so as we have said, then turn it back and forth, until it is according to the natural figure.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it is easily set.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not come forth as we have said, then take muscillage of altee, and oil of sesame, and gum melted, and grind all in the mortar; and put on the nature of the woman inside and outside this ointment, then make her sit in a warm bath until below the ribs; and when she is softened below, make a collar of mirr, and put it below, and let her lie for an hour; then make her sit on the seat, then make her sneeze and strain her mouth and nose, and gently take hold of her belly, for the child will now jump.  
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	from the issue of the child on his knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this form, she puts her hands palm to palm; then it is supported on its neck, and its feet are hung down, and it lies on the bed; and she folds her hands palm to palm, and then takes hold of the hands above the belly, and removes the cushions below, until it is prepared downwards; and if the child does not jump, she takes its feet and moves them gently, then moves the belly upwards, then puts her hands; and she moves the child palm to palm; and commands the woman that she must prepare herself as long as the child issues. 
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the birth of the child which comes out with one hand
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	It is necessary to engineer bringing back the hand: if one cannot bring it back, make the woman get up and walk; if she cannot walk, make her lie on the bed and straighten her legs; then administer the poultice that I have recounted; and if she doesn't give birth, make her sit on the stool, then study to bring back the hand; and turn the child according to the natural figure, and make her sneeze, and command her to keep straining as long as the child is coming out. 
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	of the issue of the child upon its neck, and having spread its hands, and its face turned toward the back of its mother
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	It is necessary that the knight holds his hand, then turn it back and forth, and lightly; and when it is equalized, he places on its natural muscle of elevation and oil, as we have said, then he commands her to move back and forth; and when you have done this, place her on her seat, and command that she squeeze; and she will sneeze. 
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	In this same manner to all the secondine
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes to this manner to the whole secondine, so cut the secondine at your finger, until the moistors are emptied; and if the child can rest on his face and on his neck, then cut from the hood, that it be not held back, and kill the child; then put the child inside, as long as you have put it as it should, and command the woman to avoid any time: then she will lie lightly. 
de l’issue des gemelz	of the separation of the twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or four; and this is not a strange thing, and it happens.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	Two are strange things and do not live, if they can be named; I know these, that they are multiplied, and are detached by the nature that divides them, which is attached to the bud; and sometimes they go out as naturally as all others, as we have said. 
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they come out strongly, then the care as we have said, and let the  bail be subtle, and make quickly and lightly what she does; and make so as it is worth moves to salvation. 
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Sometimes they are formed in the marsh I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, or more up to XV, and are all formed in the shape of a child by the measurement of his glorious sage, and it is necessary that the bailiff knows all this, because by chance some things happen; so do according to what is necessary. 
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat the woman of the dead child or belly, as I have said in the division, and it does not come out, and you are constrained to work with your hands; so it is necessary that you know if the woman is of healthy virtue, and has no accident or she has fear of death; so it is necessary that the woman be laid on her back, and her hips inclined downward, and her legs raised; and the minister the braid from two parts, or she is tied to the bed so that she is not treated in the descent of the child; then rub the mouth of the womb with moist oils with mullein of altee and fenugrec and linseed, then oil her hands with these oils and these mulleins; then put them in the womb gently, then want the place where she puts the instruments to be suitable to those, and take guard if the fetus is appeared that it descends on its head; so put the instruments in her eyes or her neck or her mouth or in her palate or under the beard or in the throat or near the ribs, and if the descent is on feet, then put it either with a knife and at the middle of the ribs; and it is necessary that he holds the instrument in his right hand, and puts the curve between his two fingers of the left hand, and puts it to all his hand gently, and puts the instrument in any of these places that we have said, until it comes to the empty thing; and this is the form of the instrument:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then fit the two ends together, or the third if you need it, so that the extractions are equal; and then move them equally in one direction and the other, to see if they fit, and let the ends be toothed to hold them together, as is the form here.  
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if a part remains there, then seize the bail with some of its oil, and place it in that part, and draw the other part; and if none remain there, then put this one-chine or higher up, and do this until he pushes out all of them. 
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes in front of the other, and it cannot be brought back by squeezing, then you must wrap it on the drapelet, until it is whole; then cut into the joint of the sole or at the knife, and thus you must do in the other hand, and as II feet. 
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the child's head is large and it is narrow at the opening, or if it has a sharp point assembled, then you must put the pointed spatula between your two fingers and make the point and extract the sharpness; or you will use the instrument which is called "almidach," so that its form comes with the instruments or chapter which is after this one; and in the same way do the same if the child has a large head naturally; and then pull the bones with pliers, and if the head jumps out and it is forced, then split it, as long as the moisture which is or worse at the issue; and if it cannot issue, then cut it into pieces as much as you can; and if it is swollen in the belly or below the ribs, then you must pierce it until the moisture runs. 
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is on his feet, then the traction is light, and the delivery through the mouth of the womb is easy.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if it is in the belly or the breast, it is necessary that you extract it to the cloth wrapped around the hand; and make the belly or the breast, as long as the moisture that is there cures; and if the other members are pulled out, and the head remains, then put the bail with his hand into the marrow, and lead it up to the mouth of the marrow; then put in the needle or II, and lead it further; and if the mouth of the marrow is retracted by the abscess that has come, it does not need to be worked on, but moist and fatty things must be administered; and administer plasters, and siece in soft and moisturizing water. 
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the child is on its side, and you can put it straight, then administer what we have said in a living child; and if one cannot do so, then the body be treated by parts, and leave nothing of the spine. 
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, if it comes to boils, those that come in the marsh; and if blood discharge comes, then put it on sharp wine restraining, and administer other remedies. 
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose belly one child had been dead, then conceived one other upon that, and refused death the others.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After long time there came an abscess in the belly, and inflamed so much that it opened, and began to great suppuration.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to the cure, and I thought long time, and could not suture the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put on a plaster of strong attraction, and there came out one bone, and after some days another.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was amazed greatly, for this reason because the belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	If I thought that it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I saw the wound, and in treating the bones, until the woman was in a better point; and she lived long time so, and it rose again a little bit of bone from its place; and I do not remember this chapter for except that when the master finds a strange thing, that he should know how to help.  
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring the bone back to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Here after comes the form of the presser, which is what we have in the books; and to two turns at two shoulders of the two limbs.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	However, the horns should be more subtle of the restrictor, and it should be made of ebony or boxwood; and the mouth of the shaft I must be wide, and the margin of the trees I must, and long one palm and a half; and between the two limbs should be two adjustments of this same shaft, which are fastened in one and the other, of half a palm long or a little more; and these two adjustments are put into the mouth of the marrow to open when one turns the two horns. 
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, more subtle and lighter in appearance, is made of ebony or boxwood, according to the resemblance of pliers; and it has two heads with adjustments, as you see, an arm long, and two wide; and when you see opening the mouth with the entire instrument, so have the woman sit on the bed, her feet dangling and her legs open, then put the two adjusters together in the mouth, and hold the head of the instrument below between her hips; then work your hand on the entire instrument, as you have done with pliers equally, according to the quantity that you see opening the mouth of the vagina, until the woman does what she wants. 
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	This instrument is all surmounted, and their likenesses are multiplied; and when the mirror shows them well, so much more hasty is the work, and higher as to men for their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	So do not despise the instrument that you have not shown it well, because its need is not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the secondine is retained in childbirth, it is necessary that you command the patient to retain her arm, and then make her sneeze with condiment, and restrain her hands at her mouth and nose; and if she jumps because of this, well is it. 
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If it is not so, take a pot and make it pierced or covered, and put in it herbs that can open the mouth of the marsh, such as calament, rue, anise, chamomile, cassialigne, and centaury; all these herbs, or any of them, be cooked or put in water on the fire; then put one end of the pot in the mouth of the marsh, and the other chief in the mouth of the marsh, and keep it until the vapors come inside the marsh; then make it sneeze, as we have said.  
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the second one sneezes hastily.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if it remains after this cure, and there is no more strength, command the midwife that she moisten her left hand in oil of sesame or in mucus of aloe, and then put it into the nature, and pull the second one; and when she will have found it, she grasps it and stretches it little by little straightly, so that the thread does not fall during the extraction; but there it must be moved lightly to right and left, and then pull; if it comes and becomes unstuck. 
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the mouth of the marsh is tight shut, we have said the cure of sneezing, and fumigation of herbs; and if it is not of all that we have said, so guard that you do not use the teat; but it is necessary that what is at the mouth of the marsh, you tie it to the hip of the woman, then clistet her with ointment tetrapharmakon; if she will bear it and put it back, and come forth; but nevertheless, when she bears it, it comes a bad odor to the stomach and head, and bleaches the sick. 
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	So it is necessary then fumigations suitable to this: none of the ancients have experienced the use of fumigation of watercress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument for which one uses to fumigate the woman in order to hold back the flowers and the second-born is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is to be seen like a dog, and one puts the head subtle in the nature, and the shoulders wide over the fire; and let the fumigation over the coals, and the tinder as long as it is burnt, and begin another. 
de percier lou fondement	To examine the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born without a piercing of the foundation, but they have been stopped by subtle sutures: so it is necessary for the midwife that she pierce that suture with her right tool and not pierce it with an acute spatula; and guard the wound so that she does not touch it; then put soft linen moistened in wine and oil on it, and the cure of ointment until it is healed.  
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it doesn't close up again, then put a piece of cloth there, and leave him for five days, and remove it when the child wants to go into other rooms.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes this stoppage comes from a swelling of a wound or an abscess; so it is necessary to cover that swelling; if it be cured, as we have said of the cautery of lead.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula of the foundation
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from under the foundation are nodules, and larger ones that come from near the foundation outside, or in the space between the two parts, if it is a fistula or several; and when this nodule is old, it works, and even moist moisture white or subtle bows, and sometimes these fistulas are pierced; and they are known by those who have them or by ejection or airiness when the patient defecates, and perhaps one jumps. 
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if the fistulas that pierce to the bladder, and to half of the penis; and reach to the junction of the hip, and to a point of the groin.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one knows the fistula passing through the base, and not passing through; and it is that you put your right index or base, and thrust a fine needle of iron or steel into the fistula when there is no twisting. 
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if it has tortuosity, there you put a tent of fine lead, or horsehair, as long as you feel the tent or hair at your point; and if you do not feel it, and it does not come from the opening or windiness or blood, as we have said: know that it does not pierce; so hurry to cure. 
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is pierced up to the bladder or to the urinary duct, if it leaks urine and cannot be closed by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is pierced to the junction of the hip, then the tendon comes to the place; if there is no twisting and invention of pain around the spot, it is that there is a bow here, and there is no medicine or treatment by ointment; and in these fistulas piercing there is no cure except labor, and vanity of fools who intervene. 
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In that which is neither recent nor old, there is hope for healing by iron, as I have experienced, and it is that the patient lies between your hands on his back; and lift his legs up to his hips, and have his hips inclined to his belly; then put a tent of linen, or of wool if there is tortuosity, until you know where the tent comes. 
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels it near the foundation, then you should put your index finger there, so that you feel when it tugs; and be uncovered or you feel between your finger the syfac or flesh, then you know that it is pierced; if you do not work on it one cannot heal it. 
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	One says that one can cure well none, but this happens little; and the help that one makes, if it is well-cauterized according to the width of the fistula, as it was said before; and it puts all hot into the fistula, until it comes close to the foundation; and do this two or three times, as long as you know that these charlatans are burned, which are like an owl's feather; and then the cure with damp tents in butter, as long as those chars exit, then the cure with ointment encircling flesh and soldering. 
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If so he is well, good. 
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If this is to be healed otherwise it cannot be cured; and if the probe goes in between and does not reach the point which is the foundation, and between your finger and the probe a thick covering of flesh or fat, and you see the fistula after the covering of the heart; so cut from the beginning of the fistula, and push forward the probe before the tent, and then the cautery afterward, until it reaches the head of the tent; and will be delivered the tent, and it will fall away; then destroy those fleshy formations that seem like a feather of an owl, and nothing remains of them.  
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the sin goes taut, and cuts between you and the work, then cauterize it with fire or sharp medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the fire cautery assembles II good things: that is to say, the burning of these attached hairs, and the stopping of blood and the drying of moisture; then the cure of wet bandages in butter or in crushed herbs, as long as the wound lies open, and if the hairs are burned in the wound; then cure the wounds of the eyes with hard dried dressings, and they are the dry medicines. 
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes to the very bottom and is separated from the body, you put your finger or foundation in it, and inquire there.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tent, and between it is the cloth or the syfac or chars, or where it is near to pierce, if there is no other way but by faith and hope, by the administration of one of the III manners: or you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut it to the bottom, or if you can put tents and cure as first; and do not go too deep in advance, that you do not cut the tenement which holds the foundation, and come the excretions by its will; then cure it, as we have said; perchance it will be healed, or you remove that covering and the world once she is cut from the bottom, or by tent or by another appointed instrument; then clean the char fault which is in the wound, as much as you can; then study to restore the wound, and to leave the fistula in the part outside the foundation: it will be a lighter thing for the patient.  
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes fistulas are made in this manner: and when you put the tent into the fistula, and it is near to the foundation of the skin above, then take a tent pierced at the head according to this form: 
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And it puts one twist of thread into two, and puts the tent on all the thread in the fistula until it is at the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is pierced in the margin of the base inside, then extract the thread of that which is pierced, as if you were pushing your hand or foundation; and treat the head of the thread, and assemble the two heads together, and bind one to another, and leave it for a day or two; and restrain it at no time, until the threads have cured those scars which are between two, and fall off; then cure the wound until it is healed and sound.  
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, make it pierce in all the ways that you can, if it is not too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it does not behoove to make a stitch closure if it is too deep, and then heal it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form of the pointed spatula with which one makes the fistula is very much so, on one side and cut; and on the other side not, for that one does not cut what one should not cut, as you see here.  
des emorroydes	of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhoids are according to II manners: or they are inside the foundation, like a grain of resin, and there are small and large ones, and in short, they are blood, and there is one or more, and they are outside the foundation and at the head of the foundation; but those that are outside have little moisture, and in addition, or a little of citrine water or a little of blood, and they have the color of the body; and the cure of those who have them inside the foundation is that you order the patient to stretch for them to go into chambers, as long as the foundations rise from him, and the threads appear; then hurry, and the can take with tongs, or you hold it with your finger, then cut it at its roots; and if the tweezers cannot hold them because of their moisture, take them with the cloth, or cotton, or a piece of chamois; and extract them with your fingers, then cut them, and put hot powders on them that are in place of cautery; or you cauterize them as it is said in the chapter of cautery, then cure the other cures until it is healed; and if the foundations cannot rise, then give the patient a harsh and sharp enema to wash what is at the foundation, so that it can come out openly; when the patient is sick, and if the threads are outside the foundation, the cure is lighter; and it is that you take them with your finger or with tongs, and cut them, then cure them as we have said, until it is healed, and that he fears the incision by iron.  
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary that you administer the suture in this manner: take one thread, and put it in a needle, and then pull the thread upwards and make the needle pierce from the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread below the needle, and so be of the wide; and tighten the thread firmly, then knot the thread, and remove the needle, and do this for all the others, and leave one to correct the superfluity of blood; then put on top of the foundation a cloth moistened in rose oil or in cerote, and put it on top of the foundation, and instruct the patient that he rests; and then let him rest until it dries, and when they are dry, cure them with ointment and other cures, until it is healed. 
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	Of the drying of the veins or foundation
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there occurs drying of the veins in the intestine, and by constriction of nature, and when the illness is old and medicine is of no avail.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary that you scrape at the point of a spatula or with your fingernail the bark above, which does not leave it moist; then treat it until it is healed as it should; and if it cannot heal, begin scraping more forcefully than before, until it heals well, and is scraped; then treat it until it is healed.  
dou fremit	about trembling
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Ants are a small appearance false near the body, and it goes much in through it; and sometimes it finds them cold, and feels like dead frost, and comes throughout the body, and more to the hands than other parts. 
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is that you take a thread from a goose feather, or a very strong vulture feather, and put that thread on the boil, until the purple circle touches the boil all around; then turn your hand over the whole thread until you cover the whole boil, and put it in the center, and pull out the boil by its roots. 
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, so do this of a hound's of iron or iron according to this form, and be subtle below and trailing above.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	Nor let it pierce, for to keep the two, and move pressing And if you see, so cauterize the fringe, as it is before or chapter of cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the clyster
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Never is a clyster made of silver or brass, or molten iron or mesh; and never is it made of these instruments small and large, according to those to whom they are administered.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those then who are administered in the care of children and who are feeble and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the clyster small and large if it is above wide, or the belly is tied in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and there is a detachment where the belly is tied, as you see, and the shoulder is pierced inside; and on one side there are two holes, and on the other one; and the belly is where one puts the medicines of an animal bladder or parchment, and it is pierced all around with small holes, and between each hole there is a space of I, then put in these holes I strong thread of twisted thread in X or whichever way around, and assemble the belly like a kid; and when the medicine is inside, tie the opening before with a strong thread, then do a clyster; and this is the form of the circle: 
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And be the medicine neither too hot nor too cold, and anoint the chief of the clyster with oil or egg yolk, or something similar, then insert it gently; then the minister squeezes the ministers with his two hands together, until it is all wet, then extract the clyster, and raise the legs of the patient to the side, and if the medicine wants to issue, so let it go as much as it can; and if he sleeps one whole night, then it is more help.  
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you give him an enema for the disease of a falling belly, and the medicine is eager to work, let him restart it until he is healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are either at the base or an abscess, so be it the enema as subtle as for a child; and this is the form of the subtle enema upon which the skin is held.  
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have said in the division the cure of wounds; now we will tell you the cures of hands and medicines, according to accomplishment.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to what they are made, and according to the places or where the wounds are made, and from what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.
