Things by which wounds are made are by cutting of stone, and sword-making and knife, or lance or shaft or stake, or similar things; which are made according to the parts of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or on the head, or the chest, or the belly, or the liver, and similar limbs; and I will tell you the cure of each wound, and I will begin with wounds of the simple head, because remembrance will come in its chapter.  
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes or chief, and the bone is not broken, if you take care it is of kidney stone or similar things, and the skin is immediately broken and the wound is large, and you doubt greatly an abscess hot: so do immediately bleed from the cephalic even if it comes little blood from the wound, and be the bleeding on the contrary of the swollen part; and avoid the patient's repletion of wine and thick meats. 
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he does not want to bleed, let his food be less abundant, and drink no wine, nor eat meat; and put on the wound, if an abscess comes there, cotton moistened in rose oil only, or in styptic wine; and if there is no abscess, if it is fresh with all its blood, and it is not moved by the air, powder, which I will say a little later; and if it has been moved by the air, put on some ointment, until it is healed. 
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like a sword cut and similar, and the lips cannot be brought together with tents, then assemble them with stitches, as I shall say for the wounds of the belly, of the stitching.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is open to bone, and it holds only at one point, then cover it; then cure the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat large meats such as beef and wheat cooked, also poultry, and similar things. 
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find a rotting skin and it doesn't reach the bone, then cut off all the rot and throw away the pus, then cure it; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, which cannot be stopped without cutting, and it cannot be stopped by medicines, then tie the artery, and if you find it displaced, tie it with a thread; and if this does not help, then cauterize it. 
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light: and that you put in this powder which heals as soon as the arsenic has been applied.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the manner of the powder is this: take incense one part; dragon's blood II parts; quicklime III parts, and grind the powder finely, and apply it to the wound, and keep it fastened, until it dries well and joins with all its blood; then bind it well, and leave it untied, if it does not swell; for one removes the medicine only when it is healed. 
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And no times is this made with only quicklime, when one does not have frankincense or dragon's blood, but that the ash has cauterized the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the art has moved the wound, even if it is in this way, then do not put on any of this powder; but put some softened dressings, or poultices made from barley flour and water and honey, until it lies soft; then cure with other cures until it is healed. 
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the bone fracture comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with subtle pincers; and I will tell you afterwards about the fractures of the head. 
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	The wound comes from the neck and it is simple, if it has no difference between it and that of the head, but if the nerves of the neck or the artery are cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the nerve, there is no other thing than to let the cure, and do not put anything restraining, because it harms the nerves and makes them withdraw; and do not put on the wound anything cold, because the substance of the nerves is cold, and the continuation of it is with the brain, which is the highest member; but let the medicine be warm, such as chalks washed in sweet water, and mixed with rose oil, and cucum washed also in sweet water, and other stones of mine according to this manner, and moist ointments. 
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, so stitch it and bind it with bandages, then tend to it until it heals.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and it is cut and full of bowe, then pierce or lower down; and if the artery is cut, and there is bleeding, then stop it, and tie, and cauterize if necessary is; and if the windpipe of the throat is cut, or the reins, and the conduct is kept, by which the meat goes, then sew the heart above the neck of the throat, and touch not the throat but put it back according to its natural figure; and then bind firmly, and leave it for some days, then cure with ointments until it is healed; and if the wound has made an impression on the bone, then take it out; and if there are pieces of bone, then pull them all out as you can, and those that you cannot have, then leave them until the wound suppurates, and be clear and align the issue; and if the wound is fresh, then powder on the powder that I said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there are bones in the wound and there is a fistula, treat it as I have said in my chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of a sword or knife wound
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a wound from a lance or sword, and the wound is deep, then consider if from the wound there is an escape of wind as the patient breathes: understand then that the wound is mortal; and if it is not deep, and it is fresh with all its blood, then do not put anything in the first hour, nor bind it so that the blood does not clot, and return to the heart, and kill the patient; but put there an attractive ointment, and tie it twice a day; and if you have no ointment, then put in the wound old cotton to suck out the moisture, and make the patient sleep on the wound for three days, or four, or more; if there comes no spasm, nor evil tremor of heart nor strangling of breath; and when you see good dispositions, understand that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Treat therefore with tents and other treatments, as long as it is healthy; and if it cannot heal, and works, afterwards know that there is a fistula; then treat the fistula as one should.  
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a sword or knife incision, and it is simple, or on the back, then the cure of those who are in front; if it is large, sew it; and if it is small, with powder, and if it is pressed into bone, and has broken pieces, then clean the wound, and take out the fragments if they are loose; and if they are not loose, let the wound rot, so that it will release the extractions; and for other wounds on other members, the judgment is as we have said. 
dou derrompement dou ventre	Of the derangement of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	A rupture of the abdomen is great and medium and small; sometimes from a large wound, the intestine or nerve of the intestines bursts out, which makes intromission difficult; and suturing is more difficult, and sometimes a small wound is worse than a large one because we put the intestines back in more carefully, unless we put them back hot on hot; because the intestines swell as soon as they feel the cold, and go back in with more difficulty, and for that reason, a medium-sized wound is worse, because of this, you must put the intestine back in its place than the others. And know that the rupture of the abdomen is according to four ways: the two common sutures happen in the suture of the abdomen, and the sutures of other wounds of the body and two other special sutures are common to other wounds; and all the same they are more proper with the suture of the abdomen, and I will say one by one and declare. 
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing from the intestines has come out, and it seems like something to put back, it is done in one of two ways: either because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen due to the cold.  
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in this manner: moisten a sponge or soft cloth with hot water only, or you cook in hot wine, squeezing and cypress and spice, and raise the intestine until the swelling is removed; and sometimes do this restraining it, and make it move only as to deflate.  
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling depart, moisten the intestine with water or alcohol and mallows be cooked, for by this is aligned the entrance to a little thing; and if it cannot enter, make a hole in the wound with the instrument of which one chops hemorrhoids; and the first cure is to move that tail, that no one should cut it except great necessity there is; and this is the instrument for splitting: so cut inside in the curve and outside no, and see here the form. 
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestine has jumped out, put it back in place according to the natural form in its proper place, if you have the ability, because this is good for healing. 
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is wide, and it is in the part below the belly, it is necessary that you make the patient lie on his back, and put his legs higher than his head; and if it is in the part below the belly, put the head and hip higher than the parts below, and also if the rupture of the belly is in one of the two parts, put your attention to what the injured part is higher than the other; and thus you must administer what I say in large and medium wounds. 
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	Small wounds are put together as you have seen it, then take in your hands the minister pitiful which holds all the tearing to its hand, and assemble the lips; and this is the common manner of stitches, and is that you prick an needle or more, according to the quantity of the width of the wound, then leave from the head of the wound a space, and there pierce a needle where it has the good strong thread; and pierce the two chiefs of the skin with the two chiefs of the syphac, which is below the skin inside, as long as you make it pierce from that side, and assemble the two chiefs of the syphac together; then the strain of a double thread around the needle of the two parts, then assemble the two chiefs of the wound evenly, and then leave a space, and there pierce another needle; then tie the thread as you have done the first needle, and do not cease to do this according to what you need needles, until all the wound is constrained; and let the needles be medium, between subtle and thick, for the subtle needles cut all the flesh, and the too thick ones cannot enter well: therefore it is necessary that they be medium; and it is not necessary to put the needles too far from the flesh and skin, lest they cut and open the wound before the soldering; and then cut the ends of the needles, so that they do not prick the patient when sleeping, and put tents or drapes at the ends of the needles for muffle and hold them, and leave them until the wound is soldered; and this manner of stitching with needles is more convenient in small wounds, because there suffice a needle or two for the second stitch. It is common, and is that you assemble the two chiefs of the skin and the two chiefs of the syphac together with a needle where it has the medium strong thread; and when you have pierced these chiefs altogether, then return the needle to the part where you began, in the manner one sews the drapes; and put a space between each stitch the thickness of a finger's width; this stitch serves the man, and I sewed a wound on a man’s belly, which was cut by a knife, and the wound was more than a palm wide, and it was from the intestines well two palms wide, and the wound was in the middle of the belly. 
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought back the intestine after it had been gone for twenty-four hours, and the wound closed up until the fifteenth day, and I cured him, and he was healed.  
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the mire had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle; and I did not cure him with ointment, because I was in the place where one could not find any, nor any medicine; and I put more sense above the wound cotton old II times a day, and I washed it with water of honey until he was healed. 
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Or I will tell you the II proper manners of stitching: take the needle, and put it from the outside part to the inside; when it has pierced the core straight on straight, lay the point of the thread where you have put the needle, or stitched, and make it pierce from the other side from the inside to the outside; and the understanding of this stitch is that you stitch as the furrier makes the pelts, and that you leave once the thread on one side, and take it back on the other, until the stitch is completely finished. 
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second manner of stitching, that the Galicians say properly, is like any font, which assemble the two parts together naturally, and apply one chief of the syfac to the other chief, in such a manner: stitch an needle or chief of the mirach prochiene, and make it pierce that place alone, and leave the two chiefs of the syfac; then turn the needle, and make it pierce from the outside part unto that within, at the two chiefs of the syfac; then make it pierce one and the other from the outside part unto that within, in two other chiefs of the mirach that are on the other side; and this is the middle manner of stitching and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galians thus says this word, and no one testifies it, one must sew the belly with II needles, where there is thread in each; and one must push one needle on one side, and the other on the other, in the manner of those who sew ropes; and know that when the rupture is in the middle of the belly, the suture is more grievous than the others places of the belly. 
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgements of the wound are such as the judgments of other wounds: and it is that when you find the wound fresh in all its blood, just as long as the arrow has moved it, so put back the intestine, and the cut; then put on powder containing resin, and if the arrow has moved it, put on any ointment that is present, until the wound bows; and tighten the thread, and be joined the sifac, and the mirach; then cure the wound as the others, until it is healed; and if you do not have medicines, so put on, immediately when it begins to dry, old cotton, and move it II times a day until it is healed. 
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you do not need other medicine in many cases where the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound does not communicate with the principal members, then it is necessary that you moisten a linen cloth lightly in oil of temperate heat, or in rose oil, and put it around the angles, and under the armpits; and if there is pain or rot in the bowels, and this happens often, then give enemas of black wine, and also if the rot comes to the intestine; and pierce it inside, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small. 
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine that is called "jeun" cannot heal when it is pierced, and this is because of the location of the veins in it, and because of the subtlety of the whole body, and the proximity of its nature to the nerves. 
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the sinew jumps from the wound, put it back as if the intestine, while it is fresh; and if it is old and has become black or gray, then you must tie the black part so that bleeding does not come from there because there are veins and arteries; then cut what is between the two bones, and place the two heads hanging from below the wound side outwards to align the extraction when the sinew falls, and the wound closes.  
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the boil
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is ruptured and the wound is small, it can be restored in some men, because I saw a man who was wounded or belly of a lance; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and it was infected and became a fistula, and in this there was defecation and flatulence; I put care according to what I could, and did not cease to suture until he was healed, and the ends joined.  
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw him sewn together, I feared that the patient had a bad thing in his belly; and he did not have any pain, but remained in better dispositions, and ate and drank; and some experimenters said that when he has a small wound in the intestine, it should be tied in this manner: take two strips of cloth with large heads, then assemble the lips of the wound, and when the strip covers the mouth, put it on the two lips, so that it strains its mouth upward; and then cut the head, and this holds so that he cannot untie it, then put another strip after in the same manner as before, until the wound is completely closed; and sew the wound.  
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	This chief if it is burned in the intestine and no nuisance comes to the patient, and one can bind the intestine of a fine thread which is cut from the intestine of an animal, in such a manner: take the head of this thread of intestine that it be very cleansed, and then tie to the head of this thread the thread of fine linen twisted, then put the thread in the needle, and sew the intestine, and wind it in the rupture; and this manner of sewing of fringes is not worse than according to the way of hope and confidence; and if the wound is great and wide, even when it is in one of the large intestines, there is nothing nor safety, except subtlety.   
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula or wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that any wound or abscess, when it opens, is universally called "fistula," and also when it is closed and retracted inwards.  
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And fistula is according to the truth knotty false hard and white, where one does not feel pain, and it is also raised like the plume of a bird; and sometimes in clear bowel, and other times thick; sometimes thin, and other times enough; and I have spoken of it in the division of wounds, that every wound that is not healed, and there is no flesh, it is only by one of the IX causes: that is to say, by the smallness of blood or body; or for its malice; or because there is hard flesh inside, and on the lips, that does not allow flesh to be born; or there is too much bowel; or the matter is rotten, and the matter is of bad quality; or the medicine is not good in the cure; or because the corruption is a manner of pestilence; or because the property in the region is late digestion, and late healing, and inflamed by nature; or there are veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the cures of medicines in the division. 
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Therefore it behooves me to make you know the cure for fistula which is done by work of hands.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Know that fistulas occur in all parts of the body; for there are fistulas that come to the large veins, and to the arteries, and to the nerves, or to the liver, or to the intestine, or to the bladder, or to any of the ribs, or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet; and so on that comes to the property of the main member, and to similar ones. 
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the fistulas that are in this manner are of grief cure, and there is nothing but labor, and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not come up to where I have said, and you have confidence in the cure, and you want to know it, then take a tent of rain or iron, if the fistula is straight, so it is desired; and if the fistula is crooked, so it is surrounded by a subtle tent of lead, because lead bends well around the tortuosity; and if the fistula has many openings and you cannot surround it well with tents, then clench it by one of the openings, because the moisture is passed from one opening to another, and it cleanses it; then desire it sagely according to your power, that you know if there are bones or nerves, and it is covered in depth, and ask the patient well of the pain that he feels when pressing with your hand, and the place where he feels it; and when you will truly know the place where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or nerve, or artery or vein, or in any of the places that I have told you, so cut according to what I have said, and remove the fault and the corrupted parts that are inside; then cure until it is healed, and if the fistula is deep and straight, then you must cut in depth, as much as you can, then put moistened tents in medicinal water, and put them to the head of the fistula, as long as the medicine corrodes the superfluity that is at the bottom; then put ointment in healthy flesh, until it is healed; and if it is not healed by these means, then cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted from the fistula, then cut it. 
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If a vein or nerve does not affect the principal members, as we have said; and if the bone is exposed, and there is corruption and blackness, then wash the wound as long as the corruption is completely removed, then cure with things that help the flesh as long as it is healthy; and if it is not healthy, and returns back as before, know that you are not yet finished: If it is uncovered and you wish to reach the bottom, and remove all corruption, then restore it to its place; and if it is thus healthy, then it is well. 
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If this is not the case, know that the corruption is too far along, that you cannot arrive at it; if there is nothing else than to let nature; and if there is a small bone corrupted, and you can extract it with tweezers, if the instrument suitable for this is used, and if there are many bones, then extract them all, not leaving any one; and if moisture opposes you, and there is no error or fear, then cut the moisture and flesh, and deliver the bones.  
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them within an hour, put on the wound something preventing rot, and let it until the flesh around the bones is rotten, and then they will have more easily the bones; and if it is a large bone, such as of the leg or thigh, so let it rest only the corruption as long as the blackness is entirely removed, then restore the wound; and if there is a great part of corruption, and comes up to the flesh of the bone; so it should be cleaned and covered until the corruption, and then cure it until it is healed; and I will tell you of a fistula that happened to the man in his leg, so that you may take example from it and help in your work. 
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	There was a young man about 30 years old, who had pain in his leg from a cause that came from inside the body, so that the materials came to the leg, and it became swollen with a large abscess, and had no outward cause to open; but the healers by their folly opened it so much that the abscess opened, and they corroded much of matter, and it became a fistula, and there came many openings that all rotted and moisture from the body; and many healers treated it for about 2 years, and there was no sage in the art of hands, until I was called to him, and saw his leg and the medicines with which they were treating him, and what corroded through the openings a great deal; and the body of the young man became red, and had a yellow color.  
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I placed a tent in one of these pits, and then searched all the pits, and found that some came against each other from all parts of the leg. 
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I therefore began and dug into one of the wounds until I discovered part of the bone, and I found it decayed and pierced, and the corruption came up to the inner bone; I saw what appeared to me of the decayed bone, and I thought that there was no other corruption except that which I removed; and I began to restore the wound with soothing medicines for a long time, and could not heal; and then I started again, and discovered the bone as before, and found the corruption continued in the bone, and I saw it, and then I removed it, and I tried to suture the place; but I could no more than I dug around a palm of the bone, and the traied was all its length, then I restored it with medicines; and it became healed and joined quickly, and it did not need to begin the work again except for the weakness of the patient, who cannot endure, and for the fear of death that I had of him. 
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	Because for the evacuation of blood it often happens, but he was healed entirely, and there was born in place of the bone a hard cartilage, and was of good disposition and had no pain or contrary to all in all, neither at walking nor coming. 
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it should be treated in this manner: take a linen cloth, and strain it to the head of the bone that opens, and command someone to extend it upward; and put another linen cloth thicker than the first linen, and tie it above the flesh which is above the bone, and stand the head so that you may draw the corrupt flesh downward, and uncover the flesh in the place where you wish to be, so that the bone does not break the flesh; and put a splint or a piece of wood under the bone to move the corrupt flesh; and it should be done as much as one can see and feel the corruption, and do it again. 
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is rotten and does not open, and the rot is in the middle or in one part, then uncover all the flesh; then put the tinder below, and then take it from one part to the other the corruption, and let the thread be as long as the corruption's point, as we have said; and if the corruption is in the joint, then cut the corrupted joint, and take the bone where it contains from the other side; and if the corruption is in the continuation of the two joints, then there is nothing else to do but to cut; and if the corruption is in the finger of the hand or in the finger of the foot, then that thing is very strong, but nevertheless you must inquire about that corrosion, how it opens for you; and purify it in all the ways that you can, but that the vein or the nerve do not oppose you; and know that the instruments to cut these bones are many, according to the position of the bones and the appearance of them, and their thickness and their subtlety, and their size and their smallness, and their hardness; and for this reason it is necessary to equip oneself with each kind of work its instrument; and know that the work will show you the instrument which you will need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the ways of the diseases; so think about the instrument which you need according to what is fitting.  
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The shoulder can be injured by internal or external causes; and when you have treated the decay with medicines, and they are of no use, then it is necessary to cover that limb up to the place where the decay comes from, so that the patient escapes by this from death, or by the malice, which is greater, of the fault of the limb; and the signs are that the limb becomes black, so that it seems as though it has been burned by fire, and after the blackness, then the decay of the limb spreads from limb to limb, and takes hold throughout the body; therefore hasten to cover it, and if it is due to the sting of venomous creatures, such as sea scorpions and vipers and similar ones, if the corrosion is at the head of the thigh, then cover it, and do not give it any space to come up to the hand. 
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it comes to the hand, cut at the joint, so that the corrosion does not come to the arm; and if it comes to the arm, cut with the knife; and if it passes the knife, it is death, and there is no further treatment except for the amount of its virtue; and thus do when the corrosion comes or foot: if it comes at the first joint, cut after the other joint; and if it comes at the foot, cut the whole foot; and if it goes up to the leg, cut at the knee joint; and if it comes above the knee, there is no other means than to let the patient die; and the manner of cutting or sawing the limb is that you bind it above and below, and extend some ministers one of the bonds down, and others ministers the other bond up, and you sever the flesh which is between the two bonds at a spatula wide, until the bone is uncovered; then cut or saw, and put on each side a piece of linen cloth, so that the saw does not touch the healthy place, and comes to the patient another lesion and abscess. 
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if bleeding occurs when you work, cauterize the place thoroughly, or put on some restraining powders; then return to your medicine until it is complete, then bind the member wounded with a suitable bandage, and cure it until it is healed; and I will tell you that it happened to a man in his foot: he had a blackness that seemed burned by fire, and that corrosion first came in his heel of his foot, until it possessed the whole foot; and when the man saw the corrosion, he hastened to cover the foot, and was healed; and long after the corrosion returned to his hand, and he came to me, and I put on him things that are effective after the purification of the body, and could not cease the corrosion; and he asked that I should amputate his hand, and I did not want to, because I had hope of healing the matter; and I also feared that if I cut off his hand, he would die, because the virtues of the man were weak; and he despaired altogether, and returned to his land, and hastened to cover his hand, and was healed; and I have recounted this for the sake of those who want to do something else, if they need it. 
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Sometimes an abscess comes in a fleshy place and stays so long that it makes a large assembly of flesh; and then it bursts and pierces, and the flesh jumps out, and remains its vessels, as if with a vessel; and the skin that is above is as subtle as linen cloth, and does not reach to the bone, nor to the nerve, and such a disease is called "Sain," and is not called "fistula"; but if it is so elongated that it comes to the bone by its opening, then it is called "fistula"; and the skin is that you cut all that skin around, and even when it is subtle, as with linen cloth; and it does not heal because of its corruption.  
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you have faith that the skin is hardened, and the corruption is not yet complete, and the skin is thick with flesh, thus treat it with a clyster: look if the breast is large, and the part within it is of foul odor, then clysterize with Egyptian medicine which is made thus: take asafoetida, oil, and litharge, equally, and put them in a vessel over the fire until the medicine is red, and becomes as thick as honey; and then take of this according to your need, and mix it with water and honey, and clysterize into the breast, and restrain the passage; and leave the medicine inside for two hours, then withdraw it by squeezing; do this many times, until the breast is cleansed, and the stench removed; and sometimes clysterize with water of ashes, when this medicine is not present, and that is to take ashes from grapevine wood, and pour water over them, then drain it, and clysterize, until you know that the breast is well cleansed; and if the patient cannot bear either the Egyptian medicine nor the water of ashes, then clysterize with water and honey or in which there is a pinch of pounded litharge; or you may clysterize with honey and sweet wine, for honey has the property of cleansing and washing, and the wine dries up the flesh; and when you have done this, and you are convinced that the breast is well cleansed, then clysterize with something which causes flesh to grow within it, and that is to take diaphana plaster, and mix it with rose oil and wine; or you may clysterize with some medicines and ointments, of whose properties I have spoken or in treating the ointments; and if the opening of the breast is small, and the nozzle of the clyster cannot enter, then widen it with an iron a little, and put inside a plug of Egyptian ointment, or basil ointment, until it is widened; and if the wound is too large, then cut it and leave only the place where the clyster can enter, and if the opening that smells foul is above, then cut lower than its level. 
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	For when the bow is in place, let no flesh be put upon it; and if you cannot cover the breast below as you wish, then prepare it in such a manner that the bow runs to the lowest point that there is, for when the bow is in place, let no flesh be put upon it; and if you cannot cover the breast below as you wish, then prepare it in such a manner: that the bow runs lightly downward, and do not leave anything of the bow; and take medicinal herbs to put on the wound, and stay on top of the linen cloth that covers the whole wound; then cut as forces toward the hole in the breast a little more wide than the first one; then place ointment underneath the other cloth according to the quantity of the hole, and place it on the wound of the breast to align the bow, and do not remove the large cloth except after many days once; and he who is upon the wound of the breast, often removes it to remove the bow, and know what runs from the bow, whether it be poison or pus or enough, or digested, or indigested; and take heed if the patient feels pain or no pain, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine is in such a manner extended and you see the nature that jumps on the wound of the breast, then know that the breasts will close, and approach health; and then untie it in the morning, or on the third day, and when you untie the wound, change the other cloth, and renew the ointment. 
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast lies bowed indigestible after many days, know that the breast does not heal well.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle venoms cut after a long time, if it does not despair of health, for health approaches. 
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	Car there are men who delay healing of flesh in their wounds, and those who do the opposite; and if a bow is indigestible jumps out of the chest after many days, know that the breasts do not heal well; and if the breasts are slow to heal, and are swollen, then apply drying medicines moist in substance and dry in virtue, such as diaphinit ointment, for there is much vitriol in it, and this is the last medicine; take diaphinit ointment, and make it with rose oil, and the juice of old wine equal in substance; then confit it and use it; and the same made honeyed mixed, when diaphinit ointment is not present, or take myrrh and aloes and incense, and grind it, and powder it on the honey when it is on the fire; and then glue I drapel, and place it on the breast, and at no time administer a long arithmologist, and roots of celestial lilies, which is also like flour of quince and centaury; and use either simples or composites: grind them, and make powder, and put it on the honey that I have said, and use; and if the cure is prolonged, and is not cured by this cure, then know that corruption is in depth, and makes an impression in the bone, or in hard limbs, or in members; so the cure of the fistula, as we have said before. 
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the ankle
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panarice is an abscess that arises below the nail of the hand, or the foot, or by chance in other places; and when it becomes inflamed, and one does not take care, then it comes to a bad abscess, and bursts and flows pus until it reaches the root of the nail, and by chance all of it; and comes the corrosion up to the bone, so that there is pungent pain, and the joint is broad, and the color is loose. 
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help, then it is necessary that you cut away all the superfluity that is hanging from the joint, then cauterize the wound afterwards. 
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cautery is a great help if the bone is healthy and the nail is healthy; and if the nail presses on the flesh, and begins to prick and bleed, then you should put the root under the nail so that it does not press on the flesh, and push it up, and cut that flesh subtly and lightly, and put on top of the remaining flesh medicines ardent and corrosive in order to remove everything; then care for dressings until it is healed. 
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corrosion is in the bone, then cut it and treat it, for as long as the bone is corrupted there, it cannot heal; and if you see that it will corrode, cut it as we have said before, then cure it until it is healed; and if it is broken, beaten, and feels great pain, then you must first heal it; then cut the angle of the spatula sharply by cutting across above, and guard that the cut does not come to the flesh which is below the angle, because the patient would feel too much pain; and if it happens, put something on it that soothes.  
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the sore is from the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The two joints that are born in the hands of some men by chance are all fleshy, and by chance there is some place where it has bones, and sometimes there is a nail, and none of them are born at the root of the joint, where the birth is in some of us.  
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	He who is born in any notch of the thigh does not move, and he who is born at the joint of the thigh, perhaps moves; the size of the one who is fleshy is light, in such a manner: cut it at its root with a broad spatula.  
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born at the root of the joint is grievous to cure: so you hold to be cut.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In the one who is born or will give birth at the end of our life, it is necessary that you cut first the flesh around until the bone, then cut the bone to a suitable place for him, then cure it until it is healed. 
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The wounds that come from two assemblies come by birth, or by soldering of a wound, or by burn of fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	If it is necessary that you cut that suture so that the parts may return to their natural forms; then place between two tents or cloths moistened in rose oil, so that they do not close again; or you put between two pieces of fine wood, until the ends are joined, as it is necessary.  
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If the joints come together with any of its two hands, then bind that joint as it is fitting.
des vils	of the villains 
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	Veins are large, swollen vessels full of melancholic superfluities, that come in more members of the body; and there happen more often in legs of those who go on foot and who work and carry, than others. 
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is therefore necessary that you administer to him once purging with coles, and then the herb of basil.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The cure of iron is in two ways: one is to cut and draw out the black blood; and the other way is that you open the vein and draw it completely. 
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The waist is thus treated in this manner: first, raise the leg of the warm water very hot, until the big vein is softened, then stretch the leg of the patient from above the hip to the part below the knee; then cut the vein in one place, or two, or three, with a wide incision, then evacuate and draw out the black blood by hand, from one end to the other, as much blood as the strength of the patient can bear; and then tie it up, and command him to stay with meat and drink black broth; and repeat the evacuation and the bleeding when the veins are full, and harm to the patient.  
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The raising of the leg is done in this manner: lay the patient's leg down, if there is much hair, then put it in water, and raise the leg with hot water until it becomes red, and the veins swell; and if you have no bath, then heat it by fire, and then cut where the vein is long from the thigh to the knee, or in the part below the ankle; then open the skin with the knife, and scrape the vein on each side, until it appears when touched; and you see it red and black, and when it enters the skin, it seems as a white cord; then push the nail under, until it is lifted from the skin, and then put it on the knife lightly, then cut it in another place above three fingers; then scrape the skin above the vein until it appears, then lift it to the raised point, as you have done, and put it on another knife, as you did first; then cut another piece, or more if you need it, then lift it, and cut at the heel of the foot, then treat and raise it up to the second cut; then extract from one cut to the other, until it is all pulled out, then cut it; and if you cannot draw and lift it, then put a needle in the whole strong double thread, and tie and pull it, and push it under the nail, and turn your hand on both sides, until it comes out; and guard that it does not cut, for if it cuts, it cannot be drawn nor lifted, and it comes to annoyance to the patient; and when you have treated it all, put a layer of wool moistened in wine and rose oil over the wound; and treat it until it is healed.   
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the vein is contracted and twisted and enclosed altogether, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must cut it twistedly, but do not cover it; and treat it as we have said before. 
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The form of the iron with which one cuts the vein is curved, and does not cut, so that it only cuts the vein; and it is thick curvature, for if it were thin, it would cut the vein; but let it be thick as we have said, and here is the shape: 
de la voinne civile	of the civic vein 
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is found in the legs, in hot places where no herbs or trees grow, and in land that has no moisture; and by chance it is born elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens because of rot that comes under the skin, as it comes inside the body from serpents and worms, trapped between skin and flesh. 
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are that it comes in the leg a very great inflammation, then it changes its color, and begins the vein to issue forth, as well as a root of a plant.
