Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the head of a limb is open, it is necessary that you wrap around a piece of cloth from one and a half to two inches, and tie it, and leave the cloth on the leg, and all times that there is a point at the fire, so wrap around the cloth, and tie it; and if it is too long, so cut a part, and wrap the remaining part, and do not cut it at its root, until it is all out; because if you cut it, it goes back into the flesh, and brings abscess and rot there, and bad illness; therefore for this reason, it is necessary that it be treated little by little to the top, and nothing remains in the body; and sometimes this vein when it is treated of five palms long, or of ten, and one man came to me, to whom it issued from ten palms long, and when you cut it, it throws out the root, and pierces it to the bottom, so that all comes out; and empty the matter that is inside, and administer to the place medicines to prevent rot any day, then cure it like abscesses. 
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And at times to this vein many rains, and even when it opens in the joint of the foot, or the foot, and there comes much of pus, and from which it flows rain; cure therefore as we have said before.  
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Of worms that are born between skin and flesh 
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This sickness is called in our land "ox disease," because it often happens to oxen, and is a small worm which is born between skin and flesh, and goes throughout the body going up and down, and one feels it well at the end of limb by limb, as long as it reaches the skin where it goes, and leaps; and it is engendered of rot of some humors, such as come worms and snakes and dirt and roundworms in the belly; and one doubts its malice, because when it goes through the body, and it goes up to the head, and it comes to the eye, by chance enters, and destroys the eye; and this happens many times.  
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it cured and treated, it cannot be done except when it goes: so it is necessary that you tie the place above and below with a strong linen tightly, then cut above and treat it further, and if the worm enters deep into the flesh, and you do not find it, then cauterize it with fire until it dies; and the greatest harm that it does is that it corrupts the eye, as we have said; and if you see it coming or near the eye, constrain under it the eyebrow shape, then cut above, and treat it further; and it behooves the patient to use purification of the body with medicines solutives for the humors carried out, and avoid eating meat that causes putrefaction. 
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain which comes from windiness 
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This sickness is called "vakirir" in our land, and is a pain that comes in some limbs, and then moves from limb to limb; and I have seen what I tell you. 
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and she uncovered her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; and soon after, I saw it rise like a worm to the shoulder, faster than anything, as if it were live silver when it moves from one place to another; the pain departed from that place, and went into the shoulder, and then a little later spread throughout the body, until it reached the other arm; then she told me that she returned to where it began in her body, as I saw. 
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was much amazed how she moved thus from limb to limb, for I had never seen this illness in this manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	However, I had wanted many to well have moved pain from one place to another, but I did not want it, as I saw it in the woman; and I thought that it was because the woman had a dry body, and her veins uncovered, and for this appeared that windiness constrained; and did not appear according to this reason to those who are delicious, and who have moist bodies and covered veins. 
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see to cure this illness, and the patient feels that pain, if it appears as we have said, then place the lie above and below carefully, and then cut above until the swelling constrained in its place is gone; and cauterize the place; and if you do not see it with your eyes, then cure with those who discharge the swellings, such as foul pills, and serapin pills, and similar others. 
des saiettes	of arrows 
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the places in the body where they lodge.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of them is that some have large points, and small, and hairy, and soldered; and those that have II angles, and those that have tongues, and those where there are pieces; and the one that falls in any member falls according to II manners: or in a principal member as brain, heart, liver, stomach, reins, intestines, bladder, and similar members. 
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it falls therefore in any place of these limbs, and the sign of death, which I shall tell you hereafter, appear to you: then it is necessary that you desist from the extraction of this arrow, for death comes afterwards in many cases; and when this bad sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then treat it, and cure the wound. 
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the brain when the arrow falls and pierces the bone, and jumps the soft part which is on the brain, is when there is scotomies and sode and esverting and reddishness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasms and permixtion of understanding, and vomiting of phlegm; and perhaps without matter from the nostrils, or the ears; and perhaps loses the speech and the voice; and jumps from the wound moisture white seeming to poults, and also jumps as burned flesh of char; and if this sign appears to you, so hold on from the cure, and treat the arrow if it is not in. 
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of the seventh when it falls or heart, is that it is near the left breast, and feels as if it were stuck in a hard thing, not empty; and by chance the seventh moves as the pulse does, and comes out black blood, and cold sweat and cold faintness: know then without doubt that death will come.  
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the seventh that does not move its lower part is that without plain foam jumps from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient turns color, and sighs loudly and seeks cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow falls into the covering of the hip, it is beside the small ribs; and throws great pain and great grief and sigh; and they move all the members of the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow falls into the stomach, perhaps it jumps out of the wound something of undigested meat.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow falls into the belly, and it jumps out a bit of straw through the intestine, there is no hope in the cure, nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow falls into the bladder, and the urine comes out and it flows, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other member, such as the face and the neck and the throat and the shoulder and the shoulder and the spine of the back and the leg and the hip and the legs, and the members seeming, are safe according to more dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or the artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you that it happened to me, for that reason you do it otherwise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to the man with an arrow that shot or entered at the root of the ear: I held it and pulled it from the other side under the fat of the ear, and it came out without any sensation at all. 
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And he treated with an arrow that the one shot in the fat of the eye under the paper under, and the arrow was replaced, and could not reach more than the tip toward the shaft, and was the arrow great as a turquoise bow, at all light iron without ears; the player was healthy, and did not come to him any bad accidents. 
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And treat an arrow from the throat to a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic with ears: I removed the barbs, and skillfully as long as I treated it, and the Christian was healed. 
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And treat an arrow in a man, that was stuck in his chest or belly, and I thought he would die; and then when he had passed XXX days, he did not change his condition; I cut into the arrow, and it was wrapped, and the treatment worked, and there was no bad accident. 
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you see a man who has an arrow in his back or leg, and the wound is healed over; and the arrow remains inside him, and does not change its natural position, nor feels any pain in any of his natural works.  
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And see I another man, to whom an arrow fell into his face, and the wound was sewn up; and he remained so suffering great pain; and many other similar things. 
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And treated an arrow to the man of princes the king, that it was lodged in among his ribs, and was a little leaning to the right side; and the arrow was entirely returned I was called to the cure after this one which was three days.  
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If I found the wound very narrow. 
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I felt it with a whole subtle tent, and did not feel it at all; and he felt pricking and pain below his right ear. 
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought that it was from the tip of the arrow
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I put the plaster on myself for days, and closed the wound directly, and kept the patient there a long time, until he felt the arrow one day inside his nose; and he told me.  
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I put on the wound medicine corrosive by hands for many days, until it was open, and I felt it and sensed the head of the arrow which dried up in its place; then I adjusted it in the opening of the wound with that corrosive medicine, until the head of the arrow appeared visibly to me; and it remained well for IIII months, and then it expanded so much that I put the pliers in it, and my hand on one side and the other, and it could not issue; therefore I did not cease to refine and devise instruments, until I took I day the pliers well made, according to what its form will come at the end of this chapter, until I extracted it, and restored the wound. 
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the wise men judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored: I therefore restored it, and the wound was sewn up, and the patient was completely healed. 
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Or I have told you the quality of the extraction of some arrows, so that you put your cure on those that I do not say, because the books cannot take everything; but the wise masters compare well on a very small thing, and on those that are present and failing, find new work, and new instruments, to the descent of strange things which happen in this art.  
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that the arrows are not found in the limbs where they are fixed except according to II manners: either by the place where they enter, or by another part; and that which is found by the place where it enters, it is an arrow entering into its flesh, and it has never been any other way. 
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not jump now, leave it as long as the bone is carried around, and make an ointment for the exit; and also if it is stuck in the bone, and it cannot move out, leave it so for some days, and move it each day; and then when it jumps, and if it does not jump, pierce it all around with a fine needle, until the area around is enlarged, and then treat it.  
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is fixed in the bone of the head, and goes up to one of the ventricles of the brain, and some of the accidents that I have said appear to the patient: do not draw it out, but leave it until it is healed after some days, because if the arrow comes to the syphax, it is death.  
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is lodged only in the bone, and does not come as far as the skin, and remains in the patient for some days without bad accident, then the engine of the breast.  
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply lodged and cannot be removed further, then administer torments as I have told you; then treat the wound until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is returned to its place in the body and if one cannot see it, then probe with all the tent; and if you feel it, then treat it with any suitable instrument; and if you cannot because of the depth of the wound, and the depth of the arrow, and there are no bones or nerves or vein, then fens as much as the wound is great; and treat the arrow if you can, and if it has ears in the wound to which it clings, then remove the flesh which is ensnared on both sides at the point that you can, and then break or bend the ears of the arrow, as much as you can draw it out; and be subtle that you do not break the arrow, but rather that you draw it out more easily.  
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot at once, lay it thus until the place around it is softened, then treat it, for extraction is painful.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the flow of blood makes you contrary, so administer what we have said about the cure in its chapter; and guard yourself from the incision of the nerve and the vein, and put anything as you can move to draw out the arrow without peril, soon or late, firmly or gently; and put the patient according to the form that it was when the arrow fell into him, for this is the greatest aid that there be, and if you cannot, so place it according to what the signs show you. 
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from another part, where one sees nothing of it, or the skin is swollen in that place so that if it is seen or felt apparently: cut therefore above, as long as the pliers can take hold, and then extract it: if it jumps out now.  
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, then turn your hand roundly, until it enters into the bone, and enlarge the bone, then draw it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot be drawn out, leave it still, and then begin the extraction again until it is drawn out; and if there is an arrow in it, push it out with all your strength; and if the shaft has fallen, and you see to administer a thrust, administer the instrument pointed so that the point of the arrow enters into the head of the instrument; and then push out, and if the arrow is lodged, push the instrument into its pointed entrance, in order to facilitate extraction.   
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the wound is surrounded, it is necessary that you cut all the flesh surrounding where the venom is, if you can, then treat the wound as it is proper. 
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow falls or in the belly or in the bladder or in the ribs, and it is near, and you can cover it, then strike it; and keep from covering the vein and the nerve, and then extract it, and then sew up the wound, if it is necessary; and care for it until it is healed. 
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the pliers used to treat arrows is similar to an eye's beak, and see here the shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many ways: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the pointed head is like the feather of a bird, to put at the tip of the arrow, as it is shaped: 
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape of the pliers for cutting and grasping is like this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the common veins of the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are XXXI veins of which one heals from, for which there are XVI chiefs; that is to say: II batans who are after the ears, who are called the two "herbech"; and the II arteries that are in the II temples appearing; and II veins that are in the II tear ducts of the II eyes, that are called "aspires"; and the vein that is in the middle of the forehead; and the vein that is at the chief of the neck; and the II guindeges that are on the throat; and the II veins that are in the lips above the mouth, and these are the veins that are called "augeherich"; and II veins that are below the tongue. 
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins with which one commonly heals are V in each arm: one is the cephalic, and it is on the left side of the body, and the common people call it "vein of the head"; and the middle one is called "fasted", and it is composed of the cephalic and the basilica, and the common people call it "vein of the heart"; and the basilica is on the right side of the body, and the common people call it "veins of the belly," and it is above the bone, and it is the one with which one heals, which opens clearly above the pouch. 
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the saphenous vein is the one that is between the little finger and the ring finger, and there are two of them; and in the leg and foot there are three veins: the one is below the bend of the pocket of the left side, and the second which is called phlebitis that is at the ankle of the right side; and the vein that is called “saphenous,” which is in the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg there are three veins below those. 
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The bloodletting of the veins that are after the ears so helps with old catarrhs, and with migraine; and the quality of the bloodletting, as I tell you, is that you raise the head of the patient, and rub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth; then bind the patient's neck with a bandage, until the two veins appear behind the ears in their places depending on the head: that is on your back, and where you feel the pulse below your buttock, so reign; then take the lancet, and put it under the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand to all of the vein above, and cut and the skin and the vein well two points of the passage, and make blood issue as much as you see; then bind and tie, until it is healed; and I have already said incision and cautery in the first book.  
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The blood of the II arteries that are in the II temples, it is good for old migraine, and sore, and customary ophthalmia, and to the body of tears sharp as the eyes; and the qualities of the vein are as I say: and it is that the patient restrains his neck, until the II veins appear openly; and feels the pulse below your right; and then signs of an inch; then lift the heart above the vein on your right index, and put the lancet underneath, and lift the vein upwards, and the cup, as you have done in the other two veins, and make a correction of blood according to your need; then untie the patient, and put your right on the vein an hour, then put cotton on top; and then the tie forms, and let it rest until it is healed; and we have already spoken of their cutting and their extraction, as the beginning of the book. 
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The vein of the front so it is worth as much as the vein of the cephalic for diseases of the face ancient, and to migraine, and to redness; and qualities is that the patient strains his neck by twisting, until the vein appears; then take the instrument which is called "digger," whose form here is: 
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And place the point upon the vein, and steady with your hand, or another thing, and let the blood flow according to the quantity that you see; then tie around the patient's neck, and bind the vein as long as it is healed and never use a broad flame. 
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not fitting for the flames to be too large; and heal across, because the bone is near, and by chance, it breaks the flames when they are subtle.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The blood of the two veins that are in two tear ducts helps the eyes, and the nose, and the cheekbone, and around the eye, and to the diseases of the face; and the qualities of their blood is that the patient restricts his neck by twisting with any linen, as before; then the vein, and whether the vein be through, a prick through the long of the flame a prick wide, because there is no flesh. 
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flame is subtle, perhaps it breaks; then make correction of the blood, as much as you have need, and then tie on cloth, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The blood of the vein of the nose is good for fever and ague, and for ailments of the face, such as migraine and pain that comes in the face, even when it is old; and the qualities of the blood are that the patient tightens his neck, then strains his nose to your left hand, and takes a fine thin needle, and puts it into the space which is between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open well at first, and the wound will now begin to correct; and do not let it go too deep, and make the correction of blood according to your need, then tie it for a night, because it is quickly restored; and this is the form of the needle: 
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The blood of the II guindeges helps in the treatment of the alaine, and at the beginning of meselerie, and many illnesses, and to empiety, and to corrodens, and to herpes, and estiomenes; and the qualities of the blood are that the patient restrains his neck below one and the other, as we have said; and let the master be standing on the chief of the sick, and the sick lying on the seat, then pierce the vein of the long one a little broadly, then draw out the blood temperately, or as much as necessary; then repeat in the other vein, then untie the linen, and restrain both veins moderately, that the patient does not strangle; and let him leave until morning, that the wound be healed. 
de la sainie des leivres	of the vein of the leaves 
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The blood of the veins of the lips above helps to heal in the mouth, and corruption of gums, and fissures of lips, and sores and tumors.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the qualities of the vein are that you make the patient sit before you, and restrain his neck as I have said; then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one being on the right lip and the other on the left, and recognize them by those which are black, and by those which around them have small black veins: cut therefore both of them, and if you do not know them, and you are in doubt, cut the largest of each side, and also do with the two veins that are above and below, for it is a same manner. 
de la sainie desoz la lengue	Of the vein under the tongue 
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The bloodletting of the veins that are below the tongue helps after the bloodletting of the cephalic, and it is to the relief of the throat, and to the diseases of the eye, and to the diseases of the mouth; and the qualities of the bleeding are that the patient sits between your hands before the sun, and he lifts the tongue, and looks below on each side one black vein: then bleed both, and do not go too deep in them, for below are the arteries. 
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the cut from which one is commonly bled are bled in two ways: or they are pricked with a whole flame very thin, or olive-oil fine as a trenchant cutter, and it is called «anesil»; and they are wide and fine according to the width and narrowing of the veins. 
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the flame mirror is much renowned, and is as wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is necessary to open the veins that are full of thick visible blood and contain thick and troubled blood; and this is the shape of the olive flame.  
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and is more subtly pointed, and is for healing veins subtly, where it has subtle yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The vein of the basilica, which is one of these veins, so helps to those illnesses that are under the throat, and the neck, and the chest, and the belly; and it behoves the surgeon to drain wisely, and that he should stay away from the artery which is below. 
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if it hits the ground, and blood runs out, then you should stop it up as I have said; and it must not be a pricking flame but cutting like a knife. 
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilica does not open manifestly, then you must strain it, and change another; or you want no vein of it, or you heal in its place the vein from the arm: it opens manifestly; and the cup at the flame is as we have said.  
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you wish to know the place of the vein, then so it is right that you pull out the arm, that you touch the place as much as you know the pulse; then mark the place with a sign, and then tie the arm, and cut the vein of the flame anesil; and guard that you do not wound in the artery when you see the place enfleit, for it is from the artery: avoid therefore. 
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it protrude upward like the urine of a child, and the skin is red and subtle, know that it is blood from an artery: haste then, and put your finger on its length, then remove your finger if the skin is intact; many times this happens; bind his arm, and let him so, and do not move him; and be in fear, and do not move him until he is healed. 
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the limb is not aching, and it feels warm, and the medicine is not present, then cut the artery if it opens, because the head of the retraction; and ache the limb.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And take a piece of fig bark, and make it into strips, and take one half and tie it well above the other joint; if it doesn't bleed, that is good; if not, cure it, as we have said, with powders that stop bleeding; and bleeding isn't harmful in more positions for the small wound and the tightness of the arm band. 
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The vein of the arm in the middle if helped that it treats blood from the head above, and from the body below, because it is composed of the basilica and cephalic, as we have said; and it behooves the surgeon that he lie himself for the nerve that is below, and if he does not too much draw, and he finds the nerve, and he inflates it and the saints are scratched, and perhaps cannot heal; and this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in any man because of its subtlety, then it behoves you to feel it from the instrument anesil; and avoid the nerve to your power. 
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if he has a vein between the two nerves, then make it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The vein of the head helps so much that it draws blood from the head and helps the eyes; and it is necessary to bleed in a prick at the olive branch or the myrtle branch because it is the safest of all veins because it does not have below it a nerve nor artery.  
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	However, it is necessary to seek the lightest place, and do not grieve if one has to try the first time, and they start again; and by chance some men swell up in some places when they have tried the first time, but it does not harm them. 
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the blood is according to your thinking.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing that you must know of healing, is that bleeding is administered only to keep health and to avoid future illnesses; and let the bleeding be done in one of the III veins that are or cut: namely, cephalic, femoral, and basilica; and one must bleed at the beginning of Lent on fast day, and in autumn and winter after eating, when the sign of repletion appears; and one must bleed the first day or the third, after II hours or III days. 
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The bloodletting which is administered to the sick has no set hour, but when need is of day or of night, at all hours and at all times; and it does not behoove to blood children until XIV years, nor woman carrying fruit from the fourth month until the seventh. 
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Do not bleed old men who have passed sixty years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when some wants to bleed, in whatever manner it may be, it is necessary that he purge the intestines with a light clyster, if he has much phlegm retained, so that the veins do not attract superfluities harmful to the principal members; nor let anyone bleed who is too full of meat, nor who is drunk, as long as he is so, nor who is dropsy; and it is worse to bleed after colic passion, and vomiting, and loosening of belly, and multiplication of labor in woman, and childbirth, watchfulness and fasting, and all that the virtue, or by thing of the arm or of the body; then subtilize the humors, if the blood is thick, by meat and by drinks and by medicines, if you have the power; then enter into a bath, if nothing forbids it, to subtilize the blood, and bleed from the vein of the wrist on the third finger, as we have said; and guard yourself that day from labor, and pain, and lust, and similar things; and be calm and joyful, and let the bleeder stand higher than the one who is bled, and rub his arm two or three times, then pull the linen apart in the middle, because when it is too tight or loose, it cannot correct the blood; and then rub the place with your hands, until the veins swell, and you feel them; then moisten the bleeding site of a little bit of old oil, then put his finger of his left hand on that vein below the wound, an inch or so where he wants to bleed, that the vein does not flee and fail to be pierced. 
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that are as thick as cords in the healthy person, and some that are flat with windiness, so that when one puts the flame on them, they withdraw from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus it is with these; and if it operates on the vein, it is too tight a wound, for which reason the surgeons should be advised about these things. 
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein is opened the first time, it is good; if not, it begins again a little below where it was or above carefully, if the leg is not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the limb is swollen, and the patient fears it, let him leave it for one or two days, and do not bind the arm: by chance there may come boils; nor enter into a bath, then restart the bleeding if he wishes; and if the vein is small, or the blood is subtle and you doubt that there is as much blood as you see, then pierce in the same vein all the way straight; and the work gently, so that the limb be swollen; for this happens many times when the wound is small.  
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the place is inflamed, do not begin the bloodletting, and put on a little bit of oil, because it dries the flesh of blood, and it is suitable in this place the oil; and thus administer the oil in each bleeding that you bleed the veins, to stop the flow of blood; and this same thing works for three times and boils when one puts it on the place; so subtilly it spreads and separates when it is too large. 
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if there comes an abscess large, which happens many times, even when it is not drained except at the time when the opening of the vein is small, then hasten and put upon it a sponge moistened in water and a piece hot, and restrain it for an hour; and it behooves you to do this after the issue of blood from the vein, and if it remains in place after some days neither black nor greenish, then it does not harm him; and if you see, put upon it nothing of aloes or myrrh set in calamine juice, monstastre, or seeming. 
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times abscesses and appearance happen at the saint of the basilica: put therefore your hand upon it, and if you find the place soft to the compression of the hand, so is that appearance bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore eschew that you put on nothing of those things we have said, for perchance it comes short without the artery; but make one plaster dry to harden the place, then the cure of another cure, until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each wound with blood according to the quantity of its virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the wound is black, let it issue until it is red; and if you see it swollen, let it subside until it is fine; and if it is too hot, let it cool.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is necessary for him who is fat and full, and has need of bloodletting, to make a wider wound on him, and let the flames be wide; and for him who is weak, do the contrary, and it is necessary to bleed little by little and often, and one must bleed by cutting across, not by pricking; and this manner of bleeding is safe from the shedding of blood and the severance of nerves, and it is better than bleeding through long or wide.  
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And to one whose body lacks blood, it is necessary to give softened bread in pomegranate juice; if he is burned, treat him with the blood III times or IV. And if he is of a cold complexion, temper before the blood softened bread in muzzy syrup, or in aromatic honey syrup with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and well-smelling syrup. 
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if it happens at the vein, after the issue of much blood, then it is necessary that he moisten broth of meat, and fragrant syrup fine, and use the other things that we have said in the division or chapter of syncope, for the evacuation of vein.  
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to bleed his arm, and bleed another time, if it is necessary, when he is weakened by great bleeding, that he bleed little by little, according to the quantity of his virtue continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wants to bleed his arm after the first bleeding, and he has a strong body, he bleeds seven hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wants to bleed from another place, he must bleed on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	Because there is much blood within the body which is already warmed, and brings fever; so it is necessary to draw a large quantity, and widen the opening until it flows in a stream; then when you have fulfilled all the conditions of health, and put your hand upon his arm while he is healthy, that death may not come into its place of the stream, and this happens many times, when the healer is negligent; and it is not necessary when you see to loosen the arm, and make blood flow a second time, and the opening is closed, that you press strongly upon it; nor if it is curved, that you extend the arm completely, for this would be bad; but let it remain until he heals a second time; or you do point to the tip of the flame, as long as the blood which is congealed at the opening of the vein flows out, and put upon I piece of cloth put back into shape, and press lightly. 
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, let it be and do not bind it at all, until the abscess is appeased.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if necessity exists to draw blood a second time, let it be healed in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein from which blood is taken from the arm is in the place of the vein of the head because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the manner of the vein is that the patient puts his hand in hot water until the bone is red; then be tied moderately so that the vein appears well; and now pierce it through, neither too wide nor too long; and let the holes be large, and let the bleeding be done close to the joint of the hand, and if he cannot draw out any blood from there, put the hand back in hot water, and leave the blood in the water until you have enough; and if it is summer, do not put the hand back in hot water, because one puts it more in winter than in summer; and the vein of this vein is safer than all other veins, for there is no artery nor nerve. 
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The blood of the vein in the right hand's salvation, it is good for all diseases of the liver, and here is how: constrain the hand, and put it in hot water, until the vein swells, if you see it; and if the vein is crooked, and if you cut it completely through, it does nothing wrong; and do not go too deep in its course, because the nerves are under all naked flesh; and then put the hand back into hot water, if the blood is frozen in the wound, and cannot flow out.  
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as much as is necessary, put oil and silk on the vein to close it firmly, and do this for each vein.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The blood of them in the left hand is good for the disease of the mouse, and do as I have told you towards the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The blood of the sophene is worth it for all the diseases that are below the body, such as diseases of the marrow, and retention of flowers, and diseases of the reins, and hips and legs ancients, and similar diseases. 
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the qualities of his remedy is that the patient puts his foot in hot water, and rubs on the vein until it burns, and ties above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot go many veins; heal therefore either wider vein, or at the ankle, that one is worth. 
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you cut it on the foot, be careful of the nerves that are below, and cut it across like when cutting; and let the flames be as thin as a thread.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if he cannot issue blood from it, put the foot in water, and let the vein empty well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the needle is required the first time, then it begins again the second time above a point, because the flesh is salty; do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and so make of the sophene of the other foot equally. 
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The skin of the sciatic vein is at the ankle's spur, and its incision brings relief to the hip pain when it is hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the qualities of his vein so is that the patient enters into the bath, and strains above the ankle IV by twisting, for otherwise it does not open the vein; and if it opens, then close the vein in all the manners that you can, and crossing; and vaut mues that you cut it, because the vein is dry, and it is much replenished to man's hands. 
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not find it [the dislocation], then look carefully for any vein that is open or toward the back of the leg, and towards the lower knee, and guard the nerves; and make as much correction of blood as you see, and then untie the bandage, and put on cotton and bind it; she is now healed. 
des sainies de ventouse	of the suction wounds 
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Sucking blisters are made of horns, or reed, or glass; and the suction is done in two ways: either by pricking and drawing blood, or without pricking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this cupping which is for wounding is according to II manners: or it is with fire, or without fire; and cupping that is done by wounding and by extraction of blood is done in XIIII places of the body, because one is all in the head; and the other is in the neck; and II others in II ribs of the neck; and the cup below the chin; and the cup on the II shoulders; and the cup on the hips; and cups in the II arms; and cups in the II legs; and cups in the II ankles; and cupping does not treat of blood, but of small veins that are scattered in the flesh, and for this reason it does not weaken at all, as one does with bloodletting from a vein; and it is not proper that it be administered, neither with fire nor without fire, in any illness that comes from repletion, until all the body is emptied. 
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if by necessity of diseases it is necessary to bleed, or for customs, let us administer it every hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in each time; for there are some who, when they have need to bleed, have a heavy head; and there are those who feel fullness and redness in their face, and in their head, and in the neck, and darkness in their eyes; and those who feel a drop of blood in their mouth, and have swollen their tongue, and bleed from it; and there are some who dream, and see by blood and nightmares and death and similar things. 
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we saw these signs, and even when it was removed the month, we commanded to blow after .iij. hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The bloodletting of the temples helps in the great pain of the head … which comes to the eyes, and it is not good that this be done after the evacuation of all the body; and this ventosation is in place of the cephalic bloodletting, and it is not good for those who are of cold complexion to use it, or who have catarrh, because it causes them great discomfort; and for this reason it is not good that the old people use it, nor those who have or colds diseases. 
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who heal from it often become oblivious, and for this reason it is necessary to place the cupping glass a little lower down due to the fear of oblivion.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The ventilation of the neck is in the place of the vein of the head and the basilica, and for this reason it is good for the treatment of the pain, and for cutting the channel of the stomach, and for all, and for inflation; and one should not put too much pressure, because if it holds too tightly, it can cause obstruction in the stomach or heart. 
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The ventilation of the II ribs of the neck is good for pains in the head, and ophthalmia and migraine, and for strangulation, and pain at the roots of the teeth, and it is in the place of the vein of the basilica; and you must command the operator that he express his hand when putting it on, so that he does not cut the artery, and does not come a hemorrhage.  
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The evacuations below the chin are worth for mouth diseases, and for gum rot, and similar illnesses that are in the mouth; and it is in the place of the veins of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The ventilation of the shoulders is good for illness that comes from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The incisions of the veins are as valuable as three veins of the arm, because it draws blood from these large veins; and command the patient that he does not feel too much in them, because the skin is bare, and there are nerves and arteries below. 
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The suction cup which is on the buttocks is good for hemorrhoids of the foundation, and for diseases below, and it behoves that the suction cup be large, and be of metal, that it has need to well draw; and perchance, if it were subtle, it would break; and there I make great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The suction cups of the legs are well-suited for drawing blood from the whole body, and they help with old pains in the reins, the hips, and the bladder, and they loosen up the flowers; and they are in place of the two shins, and the two ankles, but nonetheless they weaken the body after long use, and bring weakness in many dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The manner of putting on the suction cup is that you put it first empty, and succeed moderately, and place it carefully, and move evenly, and do not cease doing so until you see the place red and swollen, and appear the blood's color; then firm, and replace the suction cups, and take care in the disposition of the body, for there are those who have tough flesh, and clear pores: therefore it behooves to strike only once, and it behoves to make wide wounds, and a little deep; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the vein is thick, it behoves to strike twice: the first time to soften the path of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the vein is very thick, it behoves to strike a third time; and when we wish to draw blood little by little, we prick only once.
