Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want much blood, so often we restart; and if the vein is thick, so fire it in a moment, and the end that the veins are pricked soundly, and it is suitable for him who has thick and hard skin, and who have rough pores, that you anoint the places of the cups with oil appetizing and dissolving: if it is summer, with violet oil, or almond sweet oil, or cucurbit seed oil; and if it is winter, with cresson oil, or lily, or chamomile, or a similar one. 
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluity is large and cold, then take wormwood oil, or balm, or anise oil, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the one whom one heals has tender skin and large pores, one should not put any oil on it, but one should wash it after ventosation with rose water, or cold water, or mulberry water, or pumpkin water, or porcelain water, or something similar. 
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And he who has much moisture, let him rise from ease with water of myrtle, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have large superfluities raise themselves from old wine, or from water of rue, or from decoction of anise or chamomile, or others like it; and it does not suit to bleed with a leech before the bath nor in the bath, but after the bath an hour or two; and do not sleep after the leeching, and it is proper that he should rise, when he must be leeched and when he is leeched. 
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And guard he who is sick is choleric, and if his blood is too hot and inflamed; it behoves him to eat cold things, such as pomegranates and endives and lettuces at the meal, and similar things; and minced pigeons, and meat of roast, and moist meats. 
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those who have a cold complexion, take syrup of honey and fragrant wine, which is between old and new, and mince quince and pears and small onions and pigeons; and on the day that he will be bled, he must drink more than eat; and it is necessary to give some men at one time triacle or musk before bleeding or after, in order to strengthen the principal members; and be subtle with it, but it does not become those who are hot to drink it. 
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The suction cups that are put without harming are those that are put on the liver, and on the spleen, and gout, and on the belly and the bladder and the hips and the hip, because these members do not suffer being injured on their own, and one does it only in order to draw blood from member to member, like we put on the nipples when the milk flows; in order to remove the viscosity that is in the member, like we put suction cups on the belly and on the bladder to reduce the member; and remove the pain, when there is an inflammation or a stone, so it removes by its attractive virtue perhaps the inflammation, or displaces the stone from its place; and thus does it when one puts it on the liver and on the spleen when there is retained flatulence, and these suction cups are administered empty to suck only so much; and sometimes they are administered together with fire, and some times full of warm water, like in diseases of the pleurae, and in this manner one fills the suction cup with hot water alone, or with water where herbs cooked fit for them have been put. 
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the suction cup administered with fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And it shall have two of a large and half palm from side to side, and have or on the side near the middle a small hole, as if to put in a needle, and be of iron, so that it does not burn the patient when placed upon the limb; and have in the middle a bar of iron or steel, to place a candle held, and be both large and small according to the illnesses and the age of those who take them; for the cups of children are other than those of old people, and those of the thin ones than those of the fat. 
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And one must thus place this suction cup upon the limb: grasp the candle of wax or the lining, and place it within the suction cup across from the rod that is within the suction cup, so that the flame is at the bottom of the suction cup that it does not burn the patient; and then place it upon the limb, and the opening should be upon the wound that we have said, so that when one wants, it goes in the vapor, and one removes the suction cup; and grasp the lining as before, and restart often, if you have need. 
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the suction cup therefore which is administered in illness of pleurisy, to all acute, it has no stick nor puncture, and is not administered further than when it is full of liquid, and is placed on the limb only so much; and this is the form: 
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Leech are not brought unless in members where one cannot put leeches because of their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar; and in the naked skin, such as two or three, and other similar things; and the qualities of the user is that when you find leeches that are in clear sweet water do not let them be sucked, so take them; and put them in a nut in sweet water, until they are friendly, and have nothing in their bellies; and then heal them by vein and leech cup, then rub the member until it is red, and put the leeches on top; and when they will be full, and fall off, if it is their place where one can put a leech cup, put it on because this is very good afterward.  
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If this is not the case, lift up the place of it, and then with water, very well, and then sprint it; and if its pains are too much after the skin of the wounds, then moisten a cloth of linen in cold water, and put it on, until the wound is closed; and if the wounds are multiplied, then put on crushed vitriol, or salt, and similar things, until they are closed; or you put on the place half of peeled beans, and let them remain until they dry on the place, so it will now stop; and if you need more of this, then take other wounds. 
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the wounds do not want to take, then rub the place with fresh blood, or you insert a needle there until the pus comes out, and then put them up, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will flare; and when you see that they are bleeding, sprinkle on a bit of aloes and silk ground, or ashes, so they will close now.  
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is many times necessary in the art of medicine, and is the restoration of fracture and dislocation.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear child, that the fools of this chapter do not see that which is written in ancient books, nor have they ever read a letter; and for this reason, the science has been banished from our land, because I have never found any good one; and I know nothing, except through the wisdom of ancient books, in which I have studied so much that I have treated the science, and by experiment, and by the custom of my life; and I have written down in this chapter what is contained, and have summarized it at the end, and have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are used, as I have done in these two chapters before.  
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we say or prologue of this book the summaries of the word and the chapters where the sages put their understanding, and remain on the truth, so that those who are experienced know and learn this noble art, and learn it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or torsion or sprain comes to anyone, it is necessary that you hasten to heal the patient on one side and the other, if no thing hinders it, such as weakness of body, or childhood, or old age; or if his skin is not very warm, or too cold; and avoid cold foods, that is to say, cold meats, and flesh of mutton and venison, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and do not fill yourself too much with meats which fill the veins with blood, until you have doubt of a hot abscess, or expansion of matter in the limb; then the patient returns to his first government that he has used. 
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary that one feed the patient with meats that make great nourishment, or which have viscosity, such as wheat cooked in water, and peas, and testes, and tripe, and stomach of veal, and eggs, and fresh fish, and thick wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For with such nourishment it recovers strength and the fracture heals more quickly.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that the broken bones of the old and decrepit cannot be well taken back or joined according to their nature because of the dryness of the limbs, nor those who are too tender, such as the bones of little children; but nevertheless, care, reset on the broken bone the large tendons that bind and join the limb together, as much as it enforced before; and not at all point of its work, and for this reason it is necessary to nourish with large meats, as we have said. 
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the leg or foot, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that go straight through and others that are jagged, like the point of a quill pen for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if with a fracture, and a fracture to a tiny split.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And to each manner has its engine, and its instrument proper in the restoration, according to what the remembrance comes in its place; and is known the fracture of the bone by those that the lews are twisted, and open well by outside, and feels at the pressure of the hand; and when there is no torsion nor felt at touching, and the patient does not feel great pain, if there is no point of fracture; but it can have well torsion, or split, or small fracture.  
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If it is not advisable that you move it by hand, but put on the medicines that come after here, and then restrain it gently.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that the fracture that goes in arc, and are the two parts disjointed, it is necessary now to put them back equally, so that abscesses come not; and if abscesses come, let him leave none day, until the abscesses are appeased; then he puts it equal to the measure that you can easily and wisely, and know that the restoration of it is lighter than the restoration of this one where there are pieces; then the restraint, as it is necessary after. 
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if the bone is broken into pieces, from the two parts, whether it is the hands or feet, or to the hand if it is a small limb, or to the two cords, or to one cord and to the hand; and place the limb according to its natural figure, so that when the parts of the broken limb are separated, you reset with all means the additions in their places as much as you can, and keep that by your work there comes no lesion nor pain to the patient; and adjust well the two heads of the bones according to the best forms.  
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And it feels well by the hand if it seems to you that it is not well: then straighten it beautifully, and do not restrain it too much, nor press as those who do it through their work abscess hot and contraction of the limb, as we have wanted many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is in place, carefully instruct the patient not to move it, neither while awake nor asleep, neither by turning, nor in any other way; and guard well that the limb be so assured that it feels no pain. 
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when he feels no pain, except at the point, it is necessary to put him in such a position that he does not feel any pain; and guard that it be put straight, so that tortuosity does not come when it is restored; and the qualities of the broken limb are according to what I tell you. 
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that the broken limbs are diverse in smallness and in largeness and in form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small limbs, such as arms and legs and the like: so it is necessary to wrap them in soft and fine linen cloths; and those that are large, such as thighs and legs: so it is necessary to wrap them in a wide and hard bandage, because the wide bandages embrace the whole great limb, and restrain it from all sides equally, so that there is no twitch; then tie entor light splints, III tours or IIII according to the limb, and restrain the hand one point at all the bandage, then go above the fracture and restrain less, than the fracture then distance a point the fracture; and soften the bandage little by little, until you grasp a large part of the healthy side, then take the other bandage, and turn it back straight over the broken side; then raise to the lower part of the fracture, and restrain moderately, neither too much nor too little, as we have said in the first paragraph above; then put between the bandages splints of linen or cloths, until it is all equal, then tie everything above with a bandage, and then put your well-made plates on top, if there is no abscess or swelling. 
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is a swelling or abscess, put on top of it a soothing thing for the abscess, which removes the swelling, and leave it so for some days; then restrain above the stelae, and be half an inch wide sage, or from rods from which they make the claves, or from strips of palm, and be according to this figure: 
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	but it is necessary that the splint that one puts on the fracture be a little larger and wider than the others; and also as long as it is needed for the limb of smallness or greatness; then restrain upon the splints as you have done at the first hour, then tie above a thread evenly, as in the first hour on the fracture; more tight it is above, less; and it is necessary that the threads be medium, neither too thick nor too thin, and be of soft linen; for if the threads are thick, as I want from works of the fools who make their ties with cords of linen twisted, and this is a great error, for the tie cannot be equal if it is too subtle, and it does not become that there be between each splint less than two fingers' width. 
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is distressed by the heads of the stars after the tightening in their healthy ones, then put beneath them compresses of linen, or wool felt, so that it does not become inflamed.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the crushing, and the bone is broken, I will say its cure here afterward.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not fitting to set all broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limb is great, it should not be put in splints for fear that after 5 or 7 days, or more according to your certainty of abscess coming forth; and see here the manner of the ancient plasters for restoring fracture, dislocation, and torsion: and that you take flour which is held on the sides of the mill, and it confides with an abundance of egg, and put this confection, neither too clear nor too thick, and in use, and it is the common manner of the plaster restoring the fracture in more dispositions, and even to women and to small children, because it is not too hot nor too cold. 
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another manner of plaster restoring fracture and dislocation and torsion: take three ounces of  barberry, lead oxide, and asafetida and gum arabic, ana 10 grains each; myrrh and aloes, ana 5 grains each; alechil (probably a typo for "aethiopica" or another resin), 8 grains; and make it into powder, and mix it with an abundance of egg. If the complexion of the man is hot, use this plaster because it is of good composition, and restores broken bones quickly, and it benefits many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another manner of ointment that is good for torsion: take mugwort and wormwood, ana X З.; myrrh and aloes, ana VIIII З.; acacia VI З.; Armenian bolis X З., and grind well, and confit with water or the white of an egg, and administer. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another manner of poultice for joints and bones dislocated from their places, and soothes the pain that comes about, and the usage of bone, and the fracture: take new wool, and moisten it in vinegar and oil, cooked, and put on the place. 
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This poultice does not heal, but it is good for soothing a hot abscess, and removing pain properly. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another manner of plaster that restores broken bones: take dried fig leaves, and ground ivy leaves, and grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another manner of plaistering for the restoration of the fracture of the bone and to lessen the remainder of the abscess. 
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take root of vismalve, chamomile, flowers of violets, flour of quince, one part each; and grind, and boil with wine, and if the limb is inflamed, boil it with moist coriander water, or plain water, and use. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another manner of setting, stronger than the first, when an abscess comes to the restoration of the limb. 
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take the roots of wormwood, and seeds of flax, balm, melilot, and henbane, and flowers of violets and chamomile, of each one part; and grind, and confit with salt water, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the member, and its rest.  
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Ipocras says in his book that on the broken limb to restore it one should put a certain made of wax and oil, and nothing else more, and he says that it is between two not too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen that one should put on the broken limb, to restore, things dry and warm a little, like myrrh and aloe and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another manner of plaster that is good for injury and pain: take mugwort and heads of sheep decocted, or feathers of owl, and wormwood, and seal equally, and grind them up, and make a plaster of it and apply it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then release it a little after, and be careful that the patient does not feel any pain, nor has he moved the bones from their place; if he does not release it by hand for several days And if pain comes to the place, or itching, lack of rest or swelling, then hurry, and release it, and remove the bandage now; and take a light cloth, and a sponge of moist sea, and dip in water, and raise the place, until the itching ceases, and the pain is appeased; then let the limb rest for an hour, then put on a dry cloth, moistened in water or rose oil, and tie over a nut, as long as you are sure of a hot abscess; and calm the inflammation of the limb, and the pain be removed, then begin again the fine binding, and a little bandage, and do not restrain it as strongly as before; and refine until it is healed. 
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is hot and red and pain and swelling are all gone, and you need ointment and linen, then recommence it, as you did at first equally.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if it does not come to the limb any of those things that we have said, do not unbind it before III days or IV or V or VII; and no time leave it XX days, according to what one sees, until the fracture is healed, and approaches the adjustment of the bone on top; therefore restrain it more than first, and let it thicken its flesh, as I said before; and if you see it drying more than is necessary, know that nourishment cannot come there; so put water warm on it then, every time that you unbind it, and this be each third day, and wipe a little the wound; by this work then shortens the nourishment to the limb, and amends hastily those that do the foolish mire, that remain the limb crooked: this is bad, and thus are works fearful, and I see no other thing than to leave it and operate it correctly. 
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of various ways of fracture
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	Many kinds of fractures there are, and diverse figures, and the causes are destined; for there are fractures that are made from a sword's percussion, and the colz os all the bone up to the syfac which is below the bone, as is done with a haiche or fust; and for this reason this kind of fracture is called "haichure." 
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword cuts the bone from above without piercing, and this kind of fracture is called “absolute”; and the wound of these two fractures is great or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a blow embedded, or splitting or of the collarbone from stone, or of the head on stone, or similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if it has a break that reaches up to the skin which is under the bone, or above the bone, and this wound is large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound which is put back into the bone as subtle as a horsehair, and is the fissure small, and for that reason this fracture is called "capillary"; and if the wound which is made either by hitting with stone, or by falling, or by similar thing, and makes enter the piece of the bone down, and is the lews hairy like those who make the blacksmiths when they forge on the cauldrons; so enters the stone within. 
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more to those who have or chief moist bones, such as the head of a child; and it happens in all these manners of fracture that pieces are separated into small parts like stars; and I will speak of it in its place. 
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And let us know all kinds of fractures by the traction on them, and the inquiry at the ends, and by the corrupt flesh which is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of capillary is known by those who when they have uncovered the bone and rub above it, see the fracture black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the cure of the fracture, take care of the accidents of the patient, and if you see no evil accident, such as vomiting of blood, loss of understanding, extension, numbness, and ague fever, and eyes becoming inflamed and red, and other similar things in more dispositions, then it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see an unavoidable accident, and you hope for salvation, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the fractured bone comes to you first, and it is in winter, then it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day, as much as you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, then hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the flesh under the bone does not rot, and comes the accident that we have said.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the bone fracture comes to the cloth that covers the brain, then you should cut the split part like this: and it is that you prick the head of the patient deeply, and uncover over the bone in every way that you can, and on the shape of the wound more softly than you can, and if discharge of blood comes when uncovering the bone, or abscess put a poultice, if he needs help with this, and it is that you fill the place with cloths softened in rose oil; and make the wound rest until the abscess has calmed, and be assured of the discharge of blood; then begin to remove the bone piece by piece, and this is done in two ways: one way is that you cut a narrow slice in front, and this is the shape:  
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then you put another incision larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second manner is that you have a number of incisions of various sizes, some narrow and others wide, and pointed, and made of iron needle, and in work lightly, so that you do not bleed the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and stubborn, it is necessary that you pierce it around it, so that you administer splints with drills, not too deeply that they penetrate beyond the bone of the test, and it must have above the point a margin or a circle, which does not allow the point to pass beyond the bone; and you should have several, so that each one comes in its place according to the thickness of the bone, so that you may have drills for all tests; and this is the form of the three types of drills:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The qualities for piercing around the broken bone is that you put one drill on the bone, and turn at your two hands until you know that the bone is pierced; then put the drill elsewhere a little after, and so do all around, then cut with the incisors the space of the bone which is between the holes, and do this more subtly as you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you draw the bone to your hand, or to any of the instruments that you have like tongs, pincers; and guard that you do not touch the brain nor the marrow.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you will have pierced the bone, and treated it, it is fitting that you reset the apparatus which is dislodged from the bone to all other instruments resembling a chisel, but it is fitting that it be more tempered and subtler than the other chisel; and if there remain anything of the small bones, or no scales, so the oste lightly to the instruments; then cure the wound of tents and dressings that we have said. 
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other manner of work is this one which Galien states, which is drier; and it praises a lot, and that is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a portion of the bone, where the fracture appears to open, so that when you have uncovered that part, you will place beneath the head of this lens-shaped incisor, for this is its shape:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not trench from one part, and is the piece acute in two coasts, so that the trenching is towards the bone; then hit with a small mallet above, so that you lightly chop the bone all around, and take good care of the cloth that is underneath; if it is close to the bone, lightly remove it because it must be removed easily without pain, and without fear. 
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the broken bone does not reach the skin, and the bone is broken only from above, and there are small pieces, then it is necessary to put that asperity back together, and remove the scales with a subtle razor, which you must have various quantities of, in order to administer in each place the most suitable one, according to the work and figure of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you start with larger razors, and after with more subtle ones, and do not cease doing this until it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other capillary and subtle fractures, it is necessary that you administer cause according to its placement; and this is something that is not replied to by someone who has put his study into this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the ulcer is uncovered, it is necessary that you take a linen cloth, according to the quantity of the wound, and moisten it in rose oil, and put it on the wound; then take another cloth doubled in two or three, and moisten it in wine and rose oil, and put it on top of the first cloth; and do this more gently than you can, that you do not aggravate the ulcer, then administer by above the other bandage, and do not tighten it too much except so much as to hold the wound only; and leave it like this for a day or two, until the abscess has subsided, then untie it, and administer medicines such as roots of lilies, and flour of vetiver, and incense powder, and arnica, and similar things; and of these things make a powder, and put on the wound, and administer further medicines without stinging; and guard that the wound be always clean, that you do not leave any ointment there, nor let it gather pus, for when pus gathers upon the membrane of the brain, it corrupts and hurts, and brings great harm to the patient; for when one puts on the ulcer a stinging thing, it stings through. 
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Therefore take guard, if no evil accidents come to the patient, as we have said, so it is doubtful without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the blackness does not come out except for by the medicine that has been placed on it, that it have virtue, then you must take a part of honey, and III parts of rose oil and glue one drapel, and put it on the scab; then cure it in ways of cures that it behoves, until it be healthy. 
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that at no time are the two parts of the one above broken, or the one by itself, because they are two bones; and the one below is cartilaginous, and does not break unless it is forced or twisted, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, it is necessary that you put your small finger or through the two, and put each fracture inside your index finger, and to the pouch outward, until the bone returns according to its natural figure; and do this gently, and guard that the patient does not feel pain by your work. 
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is in the part above the neck and cannot come to its place, then it behooves you to put it even at the head of a rail a little thick.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the fracture is of two parts, you will make another band; and hasten to restore it the first day, if you can; if not, after the seventh or the tenth, when the abscess of the wound has been calmed, then bind with the chief of two tents of linen cloth, if the fracture is in one part.  
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you bind one on the other side if the fracture is there; and let the bandages be so thick that they fill the openings of the neck.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And they said any restorer one must moisten the tents with butter, and change each day. 
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It does not seem to me that this is good, but it is necessary that they be softened in the preparation of a poultice of an egg, and of mill powder; then let the tent remain, as long as the bone is hard, and the cartilage hardened. 
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes one puts in their place feathers of goose instead of tents, and so to i. souffle draped around, and it holds the blister, and blows the patient among; do as you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if an abscess comes to the new while as you work on it, put  cerote or cotton moistened in rose oil, or in i. poc of diachylon.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess does not come, put on an ointment of flour of sesame and incense powder, mixed with yolk white, then put light poultices on top and do not tie it at all; and if the fracture of the bone is small and broken into small pieces, then remove them with suitable instruments, then sew the fissure together, and cure it with the things in between flesh, and soldering, as plasters and ointments appropriate for this; and if there is no wound inside the bone, then cure it with bandages, and put canes of splint on it, until it heals. 
de la routure de la mandibule	of the rupture of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is broken apart, and there is no wound outside, and the fracture is outside only so slightly, and is not broken in two, except that it is splintered inside, if one knows it lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the fracture is in the right side, that you put your left index finger in the mouth of the patient; and if the fracture is on the left jaw, then put your right index finger, and push the fracture inside lightly, and the one made by the other hand outside, and make it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the jaw fracture is separated into two, it is necessary that you administer an extension of two parts, until it is even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the movement of teeth happens, or a break, then tie them with a thread of gold or silver or silk, then place above the broken jaw properly, and put on one double cloth; and put on the cloth a large star well made, or a piece of skin equal, long and wide according to the jaw, and tie it above as much as you can, and command the patient that he rest, and eat light meats.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see that the figure changes, then untie it on the third day, and then put back in place what has changed; and put plaster above, of the powder from the mill with an abundance of egg or sesame flour, after what you have removed the cerote; and put on top the light bandage, and if the plasters adhere, and the disposition of the patient does not change, leave it as long as it is healthy; many times it is healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if a boil comes, then administer what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, reward no piece of the bone is taken away; so subtly from the removal with instruments suitable to that.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, then widen it by flame according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you will have removed all these pieces, and there is none remaining, then cover the wound, if it is wide, and put upon it one plaster suitable to that, to prevent flesh from growing, until it is healed.
de la forcele	of the forceps
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The fracture breaks more times in front, towards the shoulder, and the fracture is according to three ways: or it is broken and separated into two, and there are pieces, and it is the lightest to restore; or there is a fracture with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the works are like this when the fracture is without a wound, that you have two ministers, so that one holds the arm that feels the broken bone; and the other extends his neck towards the side; then put each fracture to your hands, so that the form be as it should, and there is no appearance nor bump.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend more, so put under the shoulder of the patient a round ball of cloth, or wool, and be thick according to your necessity; and being and light the arm, and hold the ball in your hand, so that you put each fracture as it should.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot draw the head of the shoulder by strength because it comes in front, then it is necessary that the patient lie always on his back and put under the shoulder one or two hand-spans, and put the ministers the shoulder down, until the bone of the shoulder is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then address the fracture to your two, and if you find it broken, then it is necessary that you split it up; and draw together the pieces gently, and if the bone cannot join by any means, then cut one of the incisors that you have; but put under the shoulder this instrument, in order to ward off the shaft.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and seems like a spoon, and is not too deep, and be as wide as it is convenient, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work; and have II heads, as you see, and let one be wide, and the others narrow, as is the rupture of the wound that you made when you treated the bones; and when you are assured of a hot abscess, so close the wound, and if the rupture is small, or you doubt about a hot abscess, then apply the wound with bandages and tents, according to its quantity. 
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if a hot abscess comes, then moisten one cloth in rose oil and honey and wine, and place it on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The tightening of the bone, when it is without wounds and without incisions, is that you put on the bone the plaster of the powder of the mill and of egg white, and put light bandages on top, and put a sphere under the healthy hip if you need it; then take a very large bandage of one palm wide, then put I the double drape on the bandages, and the plaster; then take a piece of linen three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around the bandage so that the head of the bandage hangs down; and put the piece of linen on the fracture, and turn the bandage over the neck, and under the healthy hip, and under the broken hip; and tighten each part, and when you see that the ligament holds the fracture well, and you clearly see that the piece of linen does not move above the broken bone, then rewrap it every day, and when the ligament loosens, then restrain it; and make the patient lie on his back, and put him when he sleeps a small pillow under the hip, to raise the shoulder upwards; so will lighten the fracture by easing the shoulder, or you tie the arm to the neck, and do not untie it unless a bad accident happens, until XX days; then re-apply the plaster, if you see that it is necessary, and restrain it and leave it like this, until it is restored; and it is restored in at most XXVIII days, and in less time for some men.  
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the breakage of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	It happens that the shoulder breaks or is dislocated in the middle, and one feels it only by touch; so arrange the apparatus according to the figure of the fracture, and reset it according to its natural form, in all ways that you can; then put on the place powder from the mill with an abundance of egg, and light bandages, and put on top a double cloth; then put on top a wide and subtle splint, a little wider than the shoulder, and if the splint is rough in any part of the shoulder, so use its roughness to bandage it with linen bandages, so that the splint sits evenly; and then bind it tightly with a very strong bandage so that the splint does not move from its place, and watch the joint every day; and every time that it softens, bind it again, and put the splint back in its place if it is out of place, and let the patient lie on his side; and the shoulder will be restored in 20 days or 25, And when this number is completed, unbind it, and be sure, because it is not bone that puts itself out easily. 
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone protrudes beforehand, and is not under the skin, so do as follows, and on the bone, and do what we have said in the fracture of the collarbone to appease abscess hot.
de la brisure dou pis	Of the fracture of the leg
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The bone is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; but it often breaks at the end. 
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it declines to the bottom, and the patient feels great pain, and lack of strength, and fever, and sometimes vomits blood, and opens the grooves in the broken bone, and he feels it well. 
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lies often on his back, and one puts one cushion between the shoulder blades, then presses the shoulder blades, and assembles the sides of the two bones with your hands, and subtly puts each in all manners as you can, until the figure of the bone is as it should be; then put plasters and bandages over the thin layer of salt, or other light stuff, and envelop it in one sheet, and lay it on the broken bone so that it does not move; and turn the bandage around on the back, and strain it firmly, and every hour check the bandaging, and if it loosens, tighten it again; and if it is necessary to untie it, for corrosion or itching that comes to the place, or pain or abscess, hasten then, and untie it, and cleanse what has come there with methods of care; then re-apply the bandage, and strain it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	of the breaking of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the breaking of the ribs comes only in their thick parts after the back, and at the top inside, and they bend only because they are smooth; and one feels it well upon examination of the sides.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the restoration is that you put the broken bone equal, as it behoves. 
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then put the splint, and restrain it with a strap, if you need it.  
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the breaking of the ribs is leaning inwards, the patient feels very great pain and stabbing, as well as from pleurisy, because the bone pierces the membrane; and besides pains, and coughing and vomiting great quantities of blood, and this is a serious illness, and the ancients put a great deal of effort into it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if some say that it is proper to administer foods which swell the belly, in order to expel the colic outward.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, except for warm abscesses if they have not yet come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if they have already come, heal them.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And some of us say that one should place cupping glasses on the area, to suck out fluids forcefully, and this seems reasonable; however, there is doubt that the cupping glass draws the superfluities to the spot for the sake of weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say any of you should cover the place with a woolen cloth in hot oil, and put tents between the ribs to make equal the inner flesh, then be cured of the cure of pleurisy, meat, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot endure because of the bone which points to the skin, and there is doubt for the patient, then it is necessary to cut above the place of the broken rib, and it is necessary to put underneath an instrument to protect the flesh; and then one must saw the bone, and extract gently, and then sew the two lips of the wound, if it is large, and cure it with ointments, until it is healed.  
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes, put on damp cloths in rose oil, and put it on the place; and cure while the place of that which it is right for the abscess, and be lying soundly on the side where it must, until it is healed. 
de la brisure dou col	of the fracture of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes a bone in the neck breaks, and it sometimes happens that it bends; and also in the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to anyone, and you want to know if he will be healed or not, take care if you see his hands softened and swollen and dead, and he cannot move them nor extend them, and when you prick them with a needle, he does not feel it. 
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is mortal in many dispositions, and if you move them and they feel well when they are extracted and pointed, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient is cured, if one puts care to it.  
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if similar things happen to the spine of the back, and you want to know if it is sound or not, then take heed if the feet are softened, and if the accident is in the hands, and on the back there is a windiness and evacuation without will; and when one has it treated on its belly, it evacuates without will. 
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when it is set on its back and he wants to sit, he cannot.  
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Know that it is mortal: if one does not labor in its cure.  
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not happen to them, then it is a lighter thing.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is that you warm it if there is an abscess, so put on the spine rose oil or oil of egg yolk, until it is calmed; then put on a comforting and drying plaster, and tie it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest; and do not sleep on that part where he feels pain, as long as it is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bones are dislocated, then it is necessary to cover the wound; and remove the bone, then assemble the two edges of the wound, if it is large, with one suture, then treat it with ointment to encourage healing until it is healed; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called "the head of the cow", then put your bag from your left hand, and place it equal to the other hand in your power, then put the plaster and bandage on top, if you need it; then restrain it, and if there are dislocated bones, do this, remove them, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the bone of the hip
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.
