It happens that the bone of the hip is broken, and if it happens, if it did not have been a little weakening at the top; and making long, and declining to the side, and coming to the patient pain in the place, and prickling, and swelling of what breaks.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you extend your hand over it, as long as you are on the break; and know which is the break and the shape of it; and if the break is at the top only, then place equal the break, as long as it is in a natural figure.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break is long, or it declines inward, then make the patient lie on his belly, as long as the restoration of that break is apparent to you.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have placed it even, put it on the plate, then put a beam of wood or of heart on it, and restrain the fracture so that it does not move; and employ the place under the ribs until the fracture is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And command the patient to sleep on his healthy side, or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if an abscess comes to this place, do not touch it until the abscess has subsided, and put on what we have said before; and then return to restoration, and restrain it as is fitting, if there is no bad accident; and this is the manner.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the fracture of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder is that which is between the collar and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, one must restore it according to one of the two ways: one of which is that you take one stick plain of medium thickness, according to this form:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two ends of the stick with two cords, and bend them upward, and place the patient on one seat; then lay the broken arm above the stick, until it reaches the armpit, and make a curve in the middle of the stick, then put under a heavy thing or have the minister extend it downward; then put the hands together so that the broken bone returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other way is that one supports the patient on his bed, and ties the hand to his neck, then commands two ministers that one holds what is above the fracture with his hands, and the other holds below at all one link, and extends each to its part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is more out, hold tight the linen below the fracture, and above the fracture, and extend each minister to its side. 
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the fracture is near the head of the shoulder, it is necessary to put one linen medium below the armpit, and the other towards the outside, below the fracture; and also if the fracture is towards the outside, then it is necessary to put the linen lightly, without labor, until the fracture is equal on top and on the outside; then put the fracture together, as it should be, and restrain it, if a pustule does not come.  
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if a puss comes, then do not bind it again until seven days, and put on linen moistened in vinegar and rose oil, until the puss is appeased; then bind it, and the manner of binding it is that you put the splint on the fracture, then assemble the arm to the helper, and put your hand on the shoulder or on the chest; and put the drape over, and bind on the helper and on the arm so that the arm is in its place as much as possible, unless something prevents it, or if the bone is not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone is moved, then use splints, and put on the fracture a splint wider and stronger than the others, and have between each splint two fingers of space, and let each splint be so large that it passes over the fracture three fingers on each side; then bind on the splints, as I said at the beginning of the chapter on the fracture, more strongly and less away from the bone.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the position of the bones, and the tension, as we have said, in the hour that you restore the broken limb, and you doubt the abscess is hot, then leave it bound until the seventh day, as we have said; then look every three days at the bandage, that itching or swelling does not come to the place, or that the nursing does not come to the limb for that it is too strained. 
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the address, as we have said. 
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if none of these accidents come, then do not loosen it until after III days or more, and have the patient sleep on his back, and have his hands on his stomach; and put under the injured arm one cushion full of wool equally, and watch each hour of the day or of the night that the figure of the broken limb does not move, or be softened the ligaments; if it receives by the virtue of medicine, and give him the food that we have before put, in such manner that the food is at first thin; and when he begins to recover, let it be thick. 
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary that the shoulder and leg should be taken back in forty days after all; and therefore one must loosen it and administer baths and medicines of ointment to direct its place. 
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the constriction is ugly and impeded, it remains to untie for one day or two months. 
de la brisure du bras	of the fracture of the arm
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of .ij. bones, which are called the two «fosciles», because one is small, and that is the one that follows the armpit; and the other is large, and that is the one that is below, towards the little toe; perhaps break the large foscile alone, or the small one, and perhaps both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small bones are broken, the restoration is light, and healing; and when the large ones are broken, then healing is bad, and more painful than when they are broken together. 
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is the small bone that is broken alone, then it should be gently extended and set straight. 
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it is the great fissure, then it must be restrained more forcefully; and extend it above the cushion, and hold the pouch of the hand higher than the others, and the small toes lower than the other toes, and let the patient be crossed upon him, and the cushion in front of him higher, so that the patient does not suffer any labor; then extend the ministers' arms to the part below his hand, or to the thigh, and one other minister to the other above. 
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then set the eyes equal, according to their best form.  
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the fracture the pieces are broken, put each one in its place, and if there is any separated that catches the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place, then do as above with the bone, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the fracture there is a wound, I have spoken of it in the singular chapter; so take care of it.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if at the beginning of the restoration abscesses appear, then glue a bandage of cerote made of rose oil and white wax, that it not be neither too hard nor too soft; and bind the bandage above subtly, until the abscesses are appeased. 
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then the surgeon takes out the cerote, and he puts on the ointment of powdered flour with abundance of egg, then he puts the splints, and let the splint of the fracture be more outward, and a little bit wider than the others; and know that it must have VI splints or arms in more dispositions: either the fracture is in one of the bones, or in II; and tighten more above the fracture than elsewhere, and every day less away from it, as I have said at the beginning of the chapter; and let the bandages that are on the splint be soft and moist, and not hard nor rough; and let the thread, with which it is bound, be linen, neither too thick nor too fine, as we have said. 
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the limb and the ligament after some days. 
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if any bad accidents happen to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, it is necessary that you raise the limb in hot water, until the itchiness is appeased; and let the limb not be allowed to rest at all.  
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then begins again the tightening, and if the ligaments are broken and the bones dislocated, and similar things, so the address. 
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if taking care that the numbing cannot come to the limb, because it is too tight, it is necessary that you soften it a little, and leave so for some days, until the numbing corrects itself, and then tighten it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said come to the patient, then do not loosen them until 20 days. 
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	or when he has pain, then he puts his hands on his neck and let his necks be even, and guard against movement and shaking, and sleep on his back; and know that this fracture is restored in thirty days or in thirty-five, and perhaps in twenty days, according to the compositions and the complexions of virtues. 
de la brisure de la main	Of the fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that on the back of the hand and among us there are few fractures, and it comes but many times to a sprain
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the palm of the hand is broken or sprained, it behoves the patient to lie crossed, and to be straight in front of him equally; then put his hand on the board extended, and extend the minister the broken bones, and put them equal the measures, until they are well joined; and put the plaster and the bandages, if abscesses do not come, then put a splint according to the quantity of the place; and be wrapped in one drape of linen.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture is at the base towards the belly of the palm, then make a sphere of cloths, and command the patient to tighten it to his broken palm; and then strain with a long cloth, and let the splint be of heart soft as big as the palm of the hand, and strain it, as it behoves.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is at the forearm, it behooves you to put a splint above, and another below in the palm, so that the hand is open and straight, then bind it tightly around the hand, and staunch the linen between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture comes to any of the bones of the two, if it is the arm, set it straight as it behooves; and restrain it with the palm, and if you see fit, put a small straight splint to raise the fracture, and let it not move; and if the fracture is in the other fingers, such as the index or one of the others, set it straight, and bind it with the healthy finger that is after; or you bind them all together in one, as much as is best, or you put above a splint, such as a poultice; and take heed to the restoration and disposition of the hot, dry abscess, and cure what comes from it, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken hip
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The bone of the hip is often broken, and it can be seen well when it turns forward and backward; and the restoration is done in two ways: one above the fracture, and one below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on his face, then each minister extends his limb to his side equally; and this is when the fracture is driven into the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the fracture is near the root of the hip, one of the ligaments should be toward the groin, and the other ligaments below the fracture. 
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And also if it is near the knee, and therefore be the ligaments next to the knee, and be the extension down; then put the mirrors the bone equal with his two hands, until it is according to its natural figure, and then put the splint, and the tie, if an abscess does not come. 
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is an abscess hot, let it cool then return to your work and your care; the ligature is made in this manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you wrap on the fracture I with a stiff bandage doubled in II or III, and remove the superfluities, then turn the leg so that the heels come to the root of the thigh, and put I long thread between the hip and the leg, below the knee, and let the head of the thread go up; then turn up the leg and on the hip the bandage, then put on the fracture splints, and put a splint on the bone of the leg; then place in the space between the leg and the hip padding cloth to make equal the tightening, then begin to bind firmly III twists or IIII on the fracture; and as you go higher up from the fracture, and less tight; then take hold of the II joints of the thread that you have put between the leg and the hip, and tie III splints that are above, then go back down to the head of the thread, until you come near the foot; and tighten, so that it does not move from its place, then leave it thus, so that there is no abscess or swelling or other appearance.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it happens, untie it, and address what comes up, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that prick, it is necessary to set them, if one can; and if one cannot, it is necessary to split the place, and draw pus out; and cure it as we have said, until it is healthy.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And sometimes the hip is broken like this, as in the shoulder and arm; however, in the restoration thus made, it does not harm the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the hip is restored in one day, or a little less or a little more, according to the diversity of complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the knee joint
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that in the joint of the knee there are few breaks, but it bends many times. 
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, then it is no longer just a fissure, or opening, and it happens to all wounds, and without wound, and this feels well.  
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is this: one sets equal what is round to its parts, as long as it can be assembled and moved; then put the plaster, and in it put a round splint, if you have need of it, and hold it as necessary, then review all the dispositions that we have said in other fractures, such as hot abscess and similar things; so put on each accident what is right for it, as long as it be healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	Know that in the leg there are two bones, of which one is called by right "mustelz", and the other is called "foscile"; and they have all kinds of fractures as it comes to the arm, and for this reason the restoration is like that of the arm equally, and the works are all the same. And if the two bones are broken together, the leg turns in all directions. 
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the slender bone is broken, it turns forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bone is broken, one feels great pain, and it is clearly seen; and it turns below. 
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Therefore administer extension and set it straight, and bind the splints evenly; but however, if the fracture is bad, and there are many pieces, that the extension be less and lighter; and the splint according to your virtue. 
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, take two fasces of chestnut wood that support the leg on one side and the other, and be as long as the leg from the knee down to below; then wrap in two lengths one bandage above and below, and tie it in the middle as well, and at this binding point the leg will not be able to incline to the right or to the left, and thus it is well; and none administers one stick along the length of the leg, and if it is of wood, and it is placed on the leg to ward off movement, and properly done is this in a fracture where there is a wound; and move each day the leg, to see if there is an abscess hot or other accident; so cure it until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the breaking of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	To the ankle no fracture comes, but to the bones of the foot there comes sometimes a fracture and to two parts, and there have been found only a few in more places.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there comes a fracture to the bones of the foot, and you see these bones overlapping one another, put the patient's foot on the ground, as if they wanted to walk, then put your foot upon theirs, where the bones are raised, then press it so that they return into their places; then put the splint and bandages above, and under the belly of the foot a small board to 2 fingers width, then restrain the foot firmly, then when you have enveloped them with cloths and other things as you need.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when 3 or 4 days will have passed, untie the bandages, because you will find the bones equal, whether broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if there are any of the bones broken, restore them, as we have said about the bones of the hand; then put on the broken bone a splint according to the length of the bone, and be one poke wider, then put under the foot that table that I have said, and restrain it well; and if there are two or three, or more, broken, put on each bone a splint according to its quantity, wrapped in one sheet of linen, and restrain the table under the foot; and let it stand upon the top of the table away from the belly of the foot, so that it holds it well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And it is necessary that you do not forget the other things that I have said about the other fractures, as soon as we have said; and secure each accident as it is fitting.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the bone of the wrist
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of the woman's nature is broken, so make her sit enlarged, then incline it to the part of the back, and be held by behind; then fill the woman's cavity with cotton, and put in as much as a stoma; then take the woman out, and lift her back little by little, and then jump the cotton, until it comes to the entrance of nature, and returns the bone with the stoma; and when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has urinated, put it back, and thus do for VII days or more: so will be restored the fracture, and if you see, take a bladder of lamb, and tie it to the opening one chain, and put the whole bladder into nature; then blow into the chain form, until the bladder is inflated inside: then nature will return the fracture; then be filled with cotton, and leave it thus for some days, until it is healed. 
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of the finger of the man or woman is broken, restore it as we have said in the bone of the hip; and are not hidden these fractures near him who puts his study and his use, and reads my book.  
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the fracture signifies to us in many arrangements the right way of restoration; therefore understand. 
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the member, when it is broken, take a goose's throat and put it into the member; then wrap bandages around it, and leave it three days or until healed, and it will be sound quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for one who has a fracture with wound, even if it is great, such as the bones of the hip or shoulder or similar, that he be healed now, so that the healings that we have said testify to it.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, then keep the vitriol restraint, if you have no other thing, then begin again to restore the fracture in the same hour or that day, if a pimple does not come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if a pimple comes to it, then leave the restoration until the ninth day, until the pimple is appeased, and do not touch it in the third or fourth day, for you would make a bad accident happen.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is appearing above the uncovered heart, then it is necessary that you put it gently in place with your hands, to a small extent.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension is not available for you to put it in place with your hands, then resort to this instrument which is of iron, which has .vii. or .viij. points long, and the width is according to the quantity of the wound; and for this, it is necessary for the artisan that he impregnates .iii. or iiij., according to what he needs in each cure of a fracture; and let it be round and one pock thick, so that it does not bend when compressed on the limb during your work, and let it be pointed in front, and thick from the middle forward, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called "palainche", for which the shoulder should be placed on top of the visible bone; and push it once, until it comes back, and be equal to each other. 
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle, and the instruments cannot well take hold of the bone, then it is necessary that you cut the head of the bone, as long as the instruments have a purchase. 
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot bring back the bone, as we have said, so cut it with a suitable instrument, either incisor or saw, to your power; then remove what remains in the bone of roughness and small splinters.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is set, and the patient feels great pain afterward, know that it is not in its natural place. 
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If it is so that it be in its place, then soak the cloth in dark red wine and properly set it; and do not put anything on the wound, such as a crust or anything else where there is oil, so that it will not bring forth rot and corruption; then administer splints when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound open, and cut the covering all around, according to the quantity of the wound, and give good heed that the wound does not become strained with the fracture; and many times have foolish people done this, and brought upon the patient either death or corrosion at any time; and let the strapping be softer and more gentle than other fractures.  
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that a bad accident may happen, as we have said, and you feel pain in the place, then it is not fitting to put on dressings; but wrap around, instead of dressings, hard bandages, and tie them. 
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one day or two that the wound swells, remove what you have placed on it with all wine, and put ointment for healing wounds, such as ointment of terra-firma and similar. 
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you unbind the limb two times a day, morning and evening, as long as it is joined and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limb be bandaged in such a manner that the bow pulls gently downwards.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if on the next day it does not join but returns backwards, know that there are small pieces of bone, for which reason you must cleanse the wound with a sponge and remove all these loose pieces that cause the pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula comes to the place, or another manner of corruption, then it is necessary that you cure it, according to what he says in his chapter before. 
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken and open on the limb, such as the hip or shoulder, and other similar bones of the large limbs, do not treat it, for many times death comes from it, but leave it until it purrs; perhaps after 20 days or 30, then heal the wound, if you can; and if you cannot, leave it.  
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of bristles that come from the swelling
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We often come after the health of the fracture, even when it is near the joint, and it is an ugly thing to see the figure of the limb; and by chance, the member cannot do its natural works.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care then if it is fresh: if it has administered medicines styptic, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocol, acacia, and similar others, as you take any of these things, or all together, and make them confit with styptic wine or with yolk of egg or with aysil; and put them on the wound in poultices, and bind them well, and do not untie it for many days; and then untie it, and begin another, until the swelling is removed; or you bind upon a piece of plank well made; for the properties of the plank are that it removes all the swellings from the limbs; and if the swelling has already become hardened like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, then cut above it, and make the superfluity apparent; or you return it to any razor, until it is removed, and treat it until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	of the limb that is weak after the cure
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the broken bone is restored and afterwards the limb remains weak and subtle, this happens for many reasons: one because it was bound too tightly and was not bound as it should; or because there were too many bandages, and it could not come to the nourishment of the limb; or for multitude of bruising; or for too much movement, not at the right time; or because he has little blood in his body, so is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat and make the body supple, until the blood is multiplied in him; and administer baths to him, and give him joy and ease; then put poultices on the limb so that the poultice draws to the great nourishment, and the bruising often of cold water, until the nourishment comes to the limb; and returns to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	to the limb twisted after health
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after restoration, and the broken bone is apart, and the shape of the limb is ugly, nevertheless it does not lose its natural function: so do not believe the fools who say one must break the limb anew, and many foolish people have done this in our land; and this work is blamed, and brings great evils, and perhaps death; nevertheless, if the nodules and torments are fresh, it is necessary that they be raised with hot water, or softening herbs be cooked, such as leaves of vismalve, and roots, and melilot, and similar things; and the i. plaster softening, such as dyaquilon well made, and you take the muslin of vismalve, and you confit it with fat of geline or oil of sesame, and make a plaster on top; or you take figs grease, and grind them with hay of colon, and similar medicines that lessen the swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And sometimes dislocation is removed by rubbing continuously and lengthily with wet hands.  
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And let there be movement to the limb each hour. 
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the torticollis is ingrained and hardened, like a stone, and it is necessary to remove it with iron, then it is necessary to cover until the bone, with the sharp incisor lightly; and put care and study into the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation comes from any joint out of its place, for which it cannot move, and the limb is ill-figured, and the patient feels great pain and great injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to anyone, it is now necessary to bring it back without bracing.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	Because if one delays, then the limb swells, and by chance if one sets it back in place with pain; therefore it is not fitting to move it when it is swollen: many times it brings forth a spasm and other pains; however, when this occurs, have the patient bled, then leave him until the abscesses are all appeased; then rise the member with warm water and oil, then reset it gently, and care for each member as if it had come to its place. 
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters of dislocations from the head to the feet.
des mandibules	of the jaws
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It happens that the jaws are dislocated and the dislocations of both are according to .ij. manners: or they are a bit displaced from their places, and softened a bit; or they are completely dislocated, and hang towards the cheek, and cut off the saliva from the mouth that it cannot hold it, nor can it close its mouth, and envelops its tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns by many more disarrangements.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is whole and complete, then it behooves you to reset it carefully, and not shirk; and in such a manner that the ministers hold the head of the sick person, and put the thumb of one of his hands into the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, if the dislocation is of two parts; and the other two hands should be outside, to put it equal; and command the sick person to soften his jaws, and move them in all directions. 
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the fist puts it even, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it is being reset with pain, even if it is the two jaws together, apply hot water and oil, until they are gently reset; do not hesitate to reset, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are brought back evenly, and the mouth of the patient is closed well with softened stuff, so he puts on cloths moistened in cerote made of rose oil and wax, then tie him lightly with soft ligatures; and let the patient sleep on his back, and his jaws be between two cushions, so that he does not move them neither to the right nor to the left, nor does he strive to bite, but takes light food, as long as the pains are removed, and the mandibles are healed; and then eat what he wants lightly, and do not work hard to open his mouth when eating and drinking, until the mandible is well healed and healthy. 
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be put back in place within an hour, and are not converted to their places, then fevers and accustomed boils come, and perhaps a solution of the belly, and perhaps vomiting of clear mucus.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is pernicious; and many times die those who have it, within eight days.
de la forcelle	from the fork
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The sprain cannot dislocate from the inside of the rib and from the hip, and it is dislocated no times to the outside, and one feels it well.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is that the patient lies supine on his back, and extends his arms; and then presses the place firmly with his palm, and it will return; then put a splint and bandage on top, and restrain it; and the head which is towards the outside cannot dislocate; if so, and if it dislocates again at any time, reset it in its place, as we have said; then put on the splint and bandage, and restrain it, and order the patient to rest until he is healed; and in the same way is restored the head of the shoulder when it is displaced from its place.  
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	Know that the shoulder is dislocated in only three ways: one of which is that it is dislocated to the side of the hip and outward; and the second is to the side of the breast; and by chance dislocated to the upper part, and this happens rarely; and it does not dislocate behind for the shoulder, and it does not dislocate inward for the nerves; and more often dislocated downwards toward the hip, especially in those who have little flesh, because in these it is easily moved; in those who have enough flesh, it is moved with difficulty, and returns with difficulty.  
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance it happens to some men that there is percussion or fracture, and swells the shoulder with a hot abscess, and they think that it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Therefore it behoves you to prove it, until you are certain; and then begin the cure.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And is known the dislocations when it is down towards the seat, and puts difference between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find between their diversity manifest; and you will find at the head of the shoulder a hollow, and under the seat to touch the head of the shoulder, as if they were one bones; and the sick person cannot bring his hand back to its place, nor move any movements; and also, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, because you find it manifestly to touch; and this manner of dislocation is not hard to bring back, when it is new, or if the child is sick. 
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the manner is that the ministers lift the hand of the sick person up, then put their hands under the armpit, and lift the joint with force upwards to its place; and the ministers lift the hand, and extend it upwards, then put it down; so it will come gently.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we have said within a few days afterward, then it is necessary that the patient be bathed in hot water; and give him an ointment softening and soothing, such as a decoction of aloe and fenugreek and melilotus in water, and let him take it; then lay the patient on his back, and put under his buttocks a cloth of wool equal, neither too soft nor too hard, then put the foot of the wounded person's foot on the cloth, and lift the head of the shoulder virtuously, and pull the hand of the patient; and another minister holds the head of the patient so that he does not move downwards; this shoulder returns now, and if you see it so reset according to this manner: and it is that you make present the man who is taller than the patient; and let him be on his right side towards the ribs, and put his shoulder under the buttocks of the patient, and lift the buttocks upwards, so that the patient hangs in the air; and another minister pulls the hand of the patient down towards the belly. 
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, he can carry nothing heavy with him, and the dislocation returns now. 
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And to reset it in another manner: and one takes a long stick in the earth, whose head is as that of a pistol, and is neither too big nor too thin; then put it under the patient, but that he has blankets above, and the patient lies on the long part of the stick; then extend his hand down on the other side forming, and the joint will return to its place quickly; and if it does not want to return for all these things that we have said, so do this cure: take a stick from the arm of great and four spans wide, which has the head round to enter in through the shaft under the shoulder, according to this form: 
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then tie on top of the staff a sheet so that the staff does not hurt the patient, then put it under the armpit of the patient; and extend his arm on the staff of the long, and tie the shoulder to the staff, and the arm to the head of the hand, then put the arm on one step of a ladder of the wide, and let the hands be extended down, and let the body hang from the other side: the joint will return now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in, in whatever manner that may be, it is necessary that you put under the shoulder a sphere of wool even, then put the plaster prepared from powdered millet, with incense and auburn of egg, on all the shoulder and around, then strain under the shoulder carefully, and turn the linen upon the plaster, and embrace the hand to its collar, and let the hands remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he bathe softly, as long as the limb is strengthened, because it will heal more quickly; and then bathe again after 5 or 7 days, and move it; and if it is hardened and is not softened, then it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is out of place due to moisture that has come, or for another cause, then it behoves you to administer cautery to three perforations, as it is placed in front of or chapter of cautery. 
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all these things, and it loosens after seven days, and the joint does not hold, and cannot raise his arm up, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is cut or extended or softened; and know that the joint is never fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that is towards the hip, and the breasts, or rear, it is made by impulse, and extension of hands, and it administers in another place; and cure until it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after the healing comes pain to the limb, and slowness of movement, then the patient uses baths many times, until that pain is alleviated, and returns to its first nature.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the shoulder is dislocated to points, and returns to points; and it is dislocated from all sides, even before and behind, and the dislocation is not put back, because one sees it well and feels it well; and is dislocated according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the diseased blade with the healthy one, if you can see it clearly. 
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is sprained, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch the shoulder at all. 
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary that you reset it thus as an abscess comes from there, because if an abscess came from there, it would be painful to put it back; and by chance it cannot be brought back completely at all, even when it is behind; so it is worse than the other dislocations, and is of greater pain, and by chance death comes.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is, when it is such that you can bring it back, that you extend your hand to your two hands; and his arms should be spread out, and his hands hold against the cutting edge of the knife, above and below, and put the joint to its shoulders together, or at the root of its palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is at the front, it returns when he doubles his hand to his hand, and fire of the root of the palm the knife which is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it does not want to return to its place, administer strong extension; and that two ministers extend the arm, and hold it with two ministers, so that it does not move during the extension; then turn the arm on each side, then when you have enveloped a double long and wide cloth; and when the minister has joined the joint to his hand, he puts oil of any kind to soften the joint, then pushes the joint firmly, until it returns; and when it is in place, put a dry plaster over it with yolk of egg, and strain it firmly, and put the arm on the collar of the sick person, and leave it for some days, then untie it. 
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firm in its place, untie the bandage, and leave it; and if you see that the joint isn't well set, then reapply the plaster and the bandage, and leave it so for some days, until it is firmly set; then unbind it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if he feels pain after the resetting of the joint, and it moves, bathe him well and rub it gently, and press until it is soothed; or put on the joint a wool sheepskin grease, then leave it for one day and one night, then remove it, and let him enter the bath; and when he sweats, rub the joint moderately, then put the sheepskin back on, and then enter the bath; and thus do II times or III, until it is healed; and if you see, put on top wool of wet hay heated with butter, and strain it over; it will return to its position. 
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The joint of the hand is dislocated, and its return is lighter than other joints. Nevertheless, it must be brought back to its place immediately as soon as it is dislocated, so that the limb does not swell or come to have a hot abscess.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And the replacement is that you put the patient's hand on a table, and extend the minister's hand, and look at it equal, so that it puts its palm on the appearance of the joint, and pushes it until it returns entirely; then it is necessary to see if it is well in place; then put the patient's back of their hand on a table at extension and replacement. 
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is in the back of the hand, then the patient puts the back of their hand on the table, and the one caring for them puts their hand on the appearance of the joint. 
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it returns now, it is well. 
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he cannot bear it, and you cannot put it back in its place after several days, the joint remains twisted; and does not harm the patient except that as long as the hand is softened, and cannot strain anything at all: then know that the nerves are cut, or the artery; if there is no other remedy but to restrain by cautery according to the case, and perhaps there is nothing else. 
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, put on the poultice that we have said, then bind it and leave it for .v. days, then untie it and leave it so.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well, and there is any swelling, moisten it with hot water, and rub it until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the thumbs of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	Sometimes the knuckles of the hand are dislocated on one side, sometimes on the back of the palm or belly; therefore, they take the joint and put the dislocation to their pouches until it returns, then support the head of the joint, and pull it toward the direction where it is disjointed; and leave it for two days, and then make it equal on the day; and don't tie it, as we have said, and untie it by day, and make it move, and tie it back again; and do this often, until it is tight, and also do so if it is dislocated in the belly of the hand, and do as you have done before, until it is healed; and also do so when it is dislocated on another side. 
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	of the dislocation of the shoulder blade of the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the shoulder blade of the back or neck is dislocated, or if there are several dislocations, if there is no cure, because death hastens the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the signs are that the articulations jump out without will, and cannot hold them, and many times they are softened any member, or the two thighs or the two arms or one. And many times it moves the shin to four parts; that which moves at the rear is called “gilbositez”: the cure of this is that you reward if the gilbositez came from childhood: if there is no cure nor healing altogether. 
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And that which comes from falling or percussion or similar things, the ancients said were cured by great words, in which there is little profit at all; but I have abridged it according to my intention, and have formed instruments in diverse ways.  
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the swelling that comes to the breast forward, there is nothing nor health; and also that which comes straight in II sides, and one can cure only that properly which comes at the back, as I said; and it is that the patient be spread on his face in I place equal, and have a strain below him, so that he does not move; then put the stick at the head in earth forming, and the other to the feet, and tie a linen under the armpits of the sick man, and the other to the hips, and knees, and ankles; and two ministers tighten the linens, one at the head and the other to the feet, among the II sticks; and be well closed, the stick as we have said, and the mire puts his palms on the spine forming, until it returns. 
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return by this cure, then take a board of III arms long, and place it under the armpit, and the patient be on his side, and push the head of the board under the armpit, then put the middle of the board on the spine; and put the limbs of the patient on the other end of the board, and press well, until it returns to its place; and if you see, do it with the tourniquet which turns by hand. 
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.
