And is that you put II tisons at the head of the sick man of an arm great, and towards the feet II others, and have between each tison, up and down, a palm of space of long; and have in each tison I pertus, where the turner corrects, and be the tison firmly in earth, so that they do not move; and between each II tisons have I tison turning, for which the lien turns, and have in II turning II small tisons of a palm of long, to turn the turner; and then tie the lien which is among the assels to the turner towards the head, and the other lien towards the feet to the other turner, and each of the ministers turns his turner to all the lien, and the master puts the spine even as we have said. 
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And when it is evened out, place a drying plaster with an abundance of egg upon it, and then the bandages, and then the stele of a tablet of three fingers in length, that which covers the site of the gibbosity and the portion of the healthy spine, then tie it with a linen band, as we have said, and use the patient to subtle nourishment, until it is healed; and if anything comes at the end of healing, it is necessary to administer softening and soothing medicines, with the stele that we have mentioned above; and sometimes one administers a piece of cork, and sometimes it appears in the back spine of the back, and one thinks that it is dislocations; and this is the bone which opens up, for which reason one should not have presumption: by chance would come death. 
des dislocations de la hainche	of dislocations of the hip
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Know that the joints of the hip and the joints of the shoulder come out only by dislocation, not as other joints; and the joint of the hip is dislocated in .iiij. parts: inside and outside, and front and back; and more inside then, and less dislocated front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of its dislocation within it is that when one joins the diseased leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and opens the patient's knee more than the healthy one, and the patient cannot double his knee; and there is the swelling which is below inflamed with an abscess, because the head of the hip comes there.  
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of the one to whom it comes to the fire, is that this accident is contrary to those before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the sign of the one to whom it happens in front, is that his leg is well according to its fulfillment; however, he does not double his knee without pain, and if one wants him to move forward, he cannot before, and retains his urine, and swells his groin, and when he goes, he passes on his heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the sign of the one to whom it happens behind, is that he cannot spread his knee, nor double it, and that leg is more twisted than the other, and the groin is softened, and the hip joint is at the place under the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The treatment of this type of dislocation is that you consider whether the dislocation is old, and it remains according to its position, then there is no need for treatment; and there is no need for him to have presumption.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in those whose dislocation is fresh, and there are .iiij. manners of dislocations, so hasten that you return the joint, and the extension inside and outside, and the movement to right and left; perchance it will return, and has need of other cure.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this manner, then you must appear to the minister strong, and hold the leg firmly with two hands, or at the linen that is tied above the knee; and another minister extends his hand above in such a manner that he puts his hands below his shoulders, then the grasp of a linen band upon the hip; and another holds the head of the leg; and extend upwards and downwards all at once, as long as the patient is lifted from the ground at one time, and remains hanging. 
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This manner of extension is common to four similar things, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If this is not so, it is necessary to take care of its appearance. When the dislocation is at the hip, it is necessary that you support the patient on his healthy side, then put the linen on the root of the groin, and the place which is below the angle, then stretch the linen upward toward the angle, and towards the thigh; then seize with other ministers his arms, and embrace the large place of the diseased groin, and extend it outward form: so it will return to its place now; and this manner of dislocation is lighter than others. 
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot tighten it in this manner that we have said, then it is necessary that you tie the two feet of the sick person together with a strong linen cloth above the two heels, and above the two knees, and let the sick leg be extended two fingers more than the other; then let them be hung by the head from a pole, and let it be two arms' length above the ground; then command the minister to embrace the head of the hip, and let there be other ministers hanging with the sick person, who embrace firmly the hip, because the joint now returns easily.  
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocation is at the back, the patient lies down, as we have said in the one who has gilbosite, and straitens the linen on the sick leg properly, and on the foot also; then he puts two sticks, one at the head and one at the foot, then puts a stick between the hips of the sick person in the middle of the shape; and have a planty of moist cloths around it so that it does not blister the sick person, then stretch each minister towards him, and the myres puts equal to his hand the dislocation. 
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it is good. 
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If this is not done, place him upon a table, and press him as we have said in the chapter on childbirth, and lay the patient upon his healthy side. 
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, it is necessary to extend the sick leg as far as possible, and according to what I have said; and put the minister his pain to be on the aching joint, then press with the other hand, and extend it down towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is at the hip, it is not necessary to extend the patient down, nor raise up the ground, but it is necessary that he is as if his hip was dislocated outward, as we have said about lying on the two hips; and be upon his face, and the bandage extended as we have said before, and one must press upon the joint to the table; and will be in place when the patient extends his legs, and they are even; then adjust the thighs, and put the splint, and the strap of a bandage, so that the hip does not move; and rest III days or IV, then untie it, and put the splint on; and if you see that they are even, then strap it, as before, and let it be for III days; then untie it, and let him walk well, until the limb is strengthened. 
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee is dislocated in three ways: that is to say, inside and outside, and behind; and it does not dislocate forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the signs are that you command the patient to bend his leg at his hip, and if it does not come to rest at his hip, know that it is dislocated; and the restoration of all this is that you make the patient sit straight, and extend his leg as much as he can, and place your back on his flank, and put his foot on your feet; then take his knee with your palms, and retract between your two, then bend the two bones forming the knee; and other ministers extend his foot, until the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that it rests lightly on his hip; and apply the plaster on top, and make the leg rest on the hip, and bind them together firmly for three days or four, then untie it; and do not let the patient work, as long as the limb is strengthened. 
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not set right, administer strong stretching, as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until it is sound 
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels are sometimes dislocated, and sometimes completely pulled out, both inside and outside.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs of it are that the ankle is swollen, and tender before the part where it is dislocated; its returning is light, and one must extend it gently with his hands when it is only softened. 
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is dislocated completely, it is necessary that you make the patient sit straight, and hold him by the ministers except by the leg, above the ankle; then pull the foot to you with your right hand, and then with the left two times, then up the leg, and put the foot back up well; and do this two times, as we have said, pushing and pulling the foot; if it comes back, it is good; if not, begin the work again, for it will come back; and if it cannot come back like this, make the patient lie on his back on the ground, and put a stake firmly in the ground between his hips, and tie blankets around, so that the patient does not get cold; then hold the ministers the hip, and other ministers extend the foot to their hands or to the ligament, so that they tie it above the ankle of the foot; then stretch each minister equally, and the stakes be well between the hips of the patient to hold the patient when one extends; then put your hands on the dislocation, and other ministers hold the sound leg below, and the dislocation will return quickly. 
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it is set, put the plaster and bandages on top, and constrain it firmly, and tie his foot to his leg, and guard the nerves that are above the ankle behind, so that the ligatures are not too tight; then let him lie II days or III, and if the ligatures soften, then strain it; then untie it on the third day or the fourth, and forbid the patient from walking for IIII days; and if he goes before this term, it is not certain that he will not dislocate again.  
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes there, it is necessary that you soothe it, as we have said elsewhere, until it is healed.
des dois	of two
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the joints are dislocated, it is necessary to gently extend them without effort, and this is an easy thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in any of the back or foot, it is necessary that you make the patient sit on his flat or i.e. table quite straight, and put your foot on what opens of these joints, then press with your foot firmly, until it returns; and when it is equalized, and there is nothing open, then put under the sole of the foot a table to the shoulder, then strain firmly, and leave it for III days, then untie it; and let him rest, until he is healed. 
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	Of wounds and dislocations together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with dislocation, and one wants to restore it, many times the patient dies: so be not presumptuous in the cure, if you are not wise in the art and have not used it long; and if you are not pitying and merciful and tardy, nor bold; and use at the beginning of calming things abscess hot, and leave the patient in the hand of God, if you do not see hope of health; and when you see hope, then restore the limb to its place, so that the abscess chauld may come there; and when the limb is in place, administer calming things abscess hot, and cure the wound, as it should be, with drying ointments; and if with dislocation a fracture, and small bones are displaced, set them, and do what we have said in simple diseases; and keep yourself from entering into fear, according to what I have said, for this will cause you to die according to your Creator, and for the safety of your arm and your body.  
Amen	Amen
